1934.05.11

Publication of the Rajchman Report - Suggestions for League of Nations Technical Cooperation Methods - Purely Technical, Not Political - The League's Cooperation Advisory Committee to Review on the 14th 1

Dr. Rajchman, the League of Nations' representative for technical cooperation in China, arrived in China last October. The League of Nations Administrative Council and the Chinese Technical Cooperation Committee are scheduled to meet in Geneva on May 14th to discuss technical cooperation with China. Dr. Rajchman left China some time ago to return to Europe to present a report. Before his departure, he compiled an English report on his work in China for submission to the League of Nations, with a copy for the Economic Committee. The report consists of eleven chapters in addition to the introduction: Chapter 1 is on the history of the Economic Committee, Chapter 2 on agricultural products, Chapter 3 on the cotton industry, Chapter 4 on silk, Chapter 5 on water conservancy, *

Chapter 6 on highways, Chapter 7 on public health, Chapter 8 on education, Chapter 9 is a summary of Chapters 2 to 8, Chapter 10 is an outline of the government construction projects as described by President Wang, and Chapter 11 is a conclusion, "Recommendations for League of Nations Technical Cooperation Methods." The entire text consists of 50,000 words. The committee has now translated the original report into Chinese, without any alteration of the meaning. The Chinese and English reports were simultaneously published in Nanjing and Geneva on the 10th, it is said.

The report by Dr. Rajchman, the League of Nations technical cooperation representative, is very lengthy.

The most important chapters, Chapters 9 and 11, are published first

below. (The rest will be published tomorrow.)

Chapter 9: Summary of Chapters 2 to 8 2

1. To present the National Economic Council's business plan for 1934, it is necessary to discuss its economic situation, as the scope of the business depends on the amount of funding available. For convenience, the budget and a summary of the plan are listed below.

2. The distribution of the above-mentioned business and expenses is as follows:

Highways: 6,800,000 yuan

Public Health: 500,000 yuan

Cotton Industry: 1,000,000 yuan

Silk Industry: 750,000 yuan

Jiangxi Reconstruction: 1,900,000 yuan

Northwest Reconstruction: 2,500,000 yuan

Tea Industry: 64,000 yuan

Fuel Research: 100,000 yuan

Economic Investigation and Research: 200,000 yuan

General Administrative Expenses and Expert Fees: 750,000 yuan

Reserve Fund: 436,000 yuan

Total: 15,000,000 yuan

3. To explain the planning procedure in more detail, it is as follows:

For highways, 4,500,000 yuan will be used to continue the construction of highways connecting the seven provinces;

Another 700,000 yuan will be allocated to extend highways connecting other provinces; 800,000 yuan will be used to build northwest highways; 500,000 yuan will be used to promote highway transportation; and 250,000 yuan will be used for highway investigation, research, and management expenses.

Public Health: The public health expenditure is set at 500,000 yuan to cover the various business expenses and management fees of the Central Health Experimental Institute.

Cotton Industry: 1,000,000 yuan will be used for the cotton industry, mostly for improving and promoting cotton planting, and for investigating the cotton spinning, weaving, dyeing, manufacturing, and sales industries.

Silk Industry: 750,000 yuan will be used for the silk industry, for planting mulberry trees, producing seeds, setting up new-style cocoon drying machines, guiding breeding, encouraging new-style silk factories, establishing joint silk factories, and encouraging farmers to plant mulberry trees and raise silkworms.

Jiangxi Reconstruction: The allocation of funds for post-disaster work in Jiangxi Province is as follows:

Promoting existing credit cooperatives, establishing new purchasing and sales cooperatives, and establishing a general management office in Nanchang:

500,000 yuan

General Office for Social Improvement in the province: 560,000 yuan

Ten rural work agencies: 300,000 yuan

Relief for disaster victims and the unemployed: 300,000 yuan

Management and reserve expenses: 190,000 yuan

Total: 1,900,000 yuan

Northwest Reconstruction: The allocation of funds is as follows:

Irrigation projects: 1,300,000 yuan

Animal husbandry: 400,000 yuan

Prevention and treatment of animal diseases and public health: 300,000 yuan

Agricultural cooperative business: 400,000 yuan

Management and reserve expenses: 100,000 yuan

Total: 2,500,000 yuan

4. The plans for improving the silk and cotton industries have been assigned to the Cotton Industry Control Committee and the Silk Improvement Committee, respectively. Both committees are organized with representatives from businesses related to the work of each committee, and social leaders who are not related to the work of the committee serve as heads. The organizational regulations of the Cotton Industry Control Committee stipulate its functions as follows:

The Cotton Industry Control Committee has the power to guide, supervise, implement control, and reward and punish the national cotton industry and textile industry.

The functions of the Silk Improvement Committee are as follows:

The Silk Improvement Committee has the power to guide, supervise, and reward and punish the national sericulture, silk cocoon, and other industries.

The Silk Improvement Committee may first implement control in a certain area or scope, and gradually promote it to achieve the goal of national silk control.

5. The Review Committee of the National Economic Council has been established, with the Director-General of the Academia Sinica as the Chairman, and the Secretary-General of the National Economic Council, the Director of the Geological Survey, and the heads of relevant ministries and commissions as members. The purpose of this committee is to provide the National Economic Council with technical opinions from the Academia Sinica, etc. Every plan of the Economic Council should first be submitted to the Review Committee for review, and the Review Committee may also propose to the Economic Council the work that it deems the Economic Council should do.

Another function of the Review Committee is to coordinate and allocate research work on economic construction plans. According to what we know, some of these issues have already been discovered in the business procedures of the Economic Council. The Review Committee has allocated this research work as follows:

Highway planning procedures: (1) The Geological Survey will investigate fuel issues; (2) The Highway Administration will investigate improved highways, the most suitable motor engines, and vehicle styles.

As mentioned earlier, the Economic Council has requested the cooperation of the League of Nations' communications and transportation agencies to study the above issues, and Chinese technical personnel will go to Geneva this summer to discuss precise investigation methods.

Water Conservancy: The Water Conservancy Administration is collecting documents, and Jiang Yizhi will take them to Geneva soon. Experts to be sent to China this autumn will be consulted first.

Cotton Industry Control Committee: The Academia Sinica is currently studying the plan to establish a cotton industry research institute.

Land Policy: The Land Committee will be organized with three members. The technical work of this committee, such as land and aerial surveying methods, will also request the technical cooperation of the League of Nations.

General Economic Issues: The current situation and future development of light industry, the effectiveness of tariff policies, and the impact of monetary policy on economic development are currently being investigated and studied by Chinese economists under the orders of the Review Committee at home and abroad, and the League of Nations' cooperation and assistance will also be requested for the progress of this work.

Chapter 11: Conclusion (Recommendations for League of Nations Technical Cooperation Methods) 3

1. The above has provided a general description of the businesses in which the various technical agencies of the League of Nations have participated in cooperation. The text often mentions the reports of various foreign experts, which may lead readers to misunderstand the contributions that the various agencies of the League of Nations can make to China's construction work. The effectiveness of the work of foreign experts in China is actually limited. They not only need to know the facts, but also need to understand the true meaning of the facts and their interrelationships. They rarely go to places in China, and they are not familiar with the language, so they rarely come into contact with the people. Differences in perspective are inevitable. Moreover, foreign experts are treated with courtesy by their Chinese colleagues, so they cannot fully understand the hard work of their colleagues in collecting materials and translating documents. Furthermore, within the scope of each business, due to the differences in local customs and habits, and the differences in each period of social evolution, it is not easy for foreign experts to cope with this complex and special task if they only rely on their experience in their own country. Therefore, in addition to their own country, each expert must have knowledge and experience of other countries. The difficulty of the tasks of Chinese administrative and technical personnel cannot be described by those who have not experienced it.

2. It is common for the Chinese government to temporarily hire foreign experts as consultants or extend their service to various administrative and technical agencies. The number of foreign personnel is already quite large. In the future, with the development of industry, the technical staff will be expanded, or more may need to be hired. We do not want to rashly propose to modify the current method of hiring foreign personnel recommended by the League of Nations' technical cooperation representative. However, whether this method is appropriate is also a question. The foreign experts serving in China are already of different categories. The government departments, national agencies, and provincial governments often hire suitable personnel through the introduction of public and private agencies with which they are familiar. Therefore, all personnel hired through the League of Nations often think that they have an unwritten relationship with the League of Nations, or think that they should enjoy special conditions during their term of office. All of this is enough to increase the League of Nations' responsibility, and this responsibility may not be something that the League of Nations Administrative Council is happy to bear.

3. All experts responsible for dispatch by the League of Nations have their special tasks. The League of Nations is also willing to accept the Chinese government's continued requests for dispatching experts and proposals for expanding the technical cooperation plan in 1934. It is recalled that when the National Economic Council was established in 1931, the Chinese government consulted with the Secretary-General of the League of Nations to maintain permanent contact between the economic and financial groups of the League of Nations and the National Economic Council, and to exchange statistics and other reports. Now that technical cooperation has reached a new stage, it is even more necessary to realize this contact and the organization of contact as soon as possible.

I respectfully propose to the Secretary-General of the League of Nations to expand the budget for the technical liaison officer in China (including the office of the technical representative of the League of Nations Administrative Council) (Note).

The Review Committee of the National Economic Council, which is dedicated to economic research and design and is organized by the Director-General of the Academia Sinica, the Secretary-General of this Council, and the Director of the Geological Survey, as mentioned above, can request reports from the office of the technical representative on time in accordance with the 1931 agreement. Now that the National Economic Council has designated several issues for research in order to have concrete plans, if the League of Nations' financial and economic groups can alternately dispatch one senior official to Nanjing, it will definitely be deeply desired by the National Economic Council.

(Note) This office was named the Office of the Technical Cooperation Representative of the League of Nations stationed at the National Economic Council after consultation with the Secretary-General of the League of Nations in November 1933.

The task of the experts dispatched by the technical agencies of the League of Nations should be limited to discussing a certain type or group of clearly defined issues. However, before the discussion, it is necessary to conduct a precise investigation and research in China. This investigation and research work should be carried out by Chinese administrative, technical, and academic agencies or private experts. If the necessary documents can be taken to Geneva by relevant personnel before the foreign experts depart, so that the foreign experts can carry out some work on the way to the East, the term of office of the foreign experts in China can also be reduced accordingly. The matters submitted for discussion by foreign experts should be limited to those related to the planned business, and the selection of foreign experts is especially important. Only those with international reputation can be competent.

During the progress of this business, the League of Nations' technical representative must have a longer term of office. This representative must have more international experience in addition to his own country, and must be clear about the procedures of the international organization he represents. Because with the development of business, the situation and circumstances change accordingly, and the technical representative is the one who relies on on-site investigation of the traces of changes. Therefore, each technical representative should first maintain the necessary contact with the international technical aspects, and then the success of cooperation can be expected. Chinese colleagues should also take this opportunity to make the most of the strengths of foreign personnel, jointly design, and see the implementation as soon as possible.

4. Chinese technical experts are all diligent and devoted to their duties, and the various businesses are proceeding without interruption in order to achieve success. The success of China's construction can be predicted. They have suffered from disasters and wars in the country, and feel that the international cooperation methods are rarely effective, so they can all be unmoved by political heresies and rumors, and devote themselves to the work of active development. There are also those who work hard to plan in order to use the best methods to revitalize the country under the current environment. Although they have true technical knowledge, their background is half from China and half from abroad, and they have also carefully studied the operation of the economic organizations of the major countries in the world. Therefore, they have extraordinary insights into the application of Western public enterprises, finance, economy, industry, agriculture, and foreign social policies, and regard them as the philosophy of the foundation. This may be something that the world does not expect. In short, there are many people in China who have the necessary expert knowledge, can understand their own technical needs, and are insightful about the improvements or innovations that China should have. Except for a few kinds of special experts, these people and their younger generations are more than capable of coping with emergencies under favorable circumstances. Unfortunately, only a few of them have held administrative responsibilities. Although they know very well the difficulties encountered by the great powers and the ways in which they respond, and sometimes their knowledge is even more thorough, except for a few special cases, they have not had the opportunity to participate in public life, industrial management, or the practice of economic policies abroad.

5. The organization and regulations of the League of Nations' technical agencies are quite flexible, and can be used to supplement cooperation methods. The most important thing is to pay attention to sending Chinese experts to foreign countries for inspection. Currently, the Chinese who come into contact with foreigners overseas are only diplomatic officials and well-known figures in the intellectual world who are proficient in foreign languages. In the future, more important personnel in the economic field and public service should be made to have technical contacts with foreigners, and the methods of contact should be specified. The Secretariat of the League of Nations and the International Labor Office are rich in unique information and special technical experience. For fourteen years, Europe has often had a transition period, and the political, economic, and social system before the European War has gradually evolved to adapt to today's new situation. All the materials and experience are enough for people to use. China's participation in this change and evolution is even more profound than that of other countries. The three revolutions of 1911, 1925, and 1927 are steps in the great change, starting with the separation of the old political system, diplomacy, and economic business, social life, and education system. Today, the development of economy and finance, the changes in society, and the trend of politics are seeking a new method of construction. Some of the facts are detailed in the previous text. Therefore, today, the League of Nations should provide all conveniences to enable China to have close contact with the technically responsible personnel in the agencies of various countries, so as to seek practical ways for economic business and economic and social reforms, and the effectiveness of technical cooperation can be seen. The specific methods of contact between Chinese and foreign staff are as follows:

(1) Under the guidance of the staff of the Secretariat of the League of Nations and the International Labor Office, and with their experience, use the files of the two agencies in a systematic and planned manner.

(2) The Secretariat of the International Bank for Settlements, the Secretariats of various economic and design committees, and other similar agencies in Europe and the United States can also provide the same convenience.

(3) The technical committees and sub-committees of the League of Nations and the International Labor Organization should invite experts with the above qualifications and interests to participate in the field during their meetings and specific research.

(4) Technical issues related to China's construction can be entrusted to well-known economic and industrial research institutions abroad for testing and research, and it is still agreed that Chinese experts will participate. The detailed methods depend on the nature of the research and investigation.

(5) The League of Nations Health Organization has provided convenience for senior technical personnel of the Chinese government to gain special experience in similar agencies. If this method can be promoted in other areas, it will be even more beneficial.

(6) The proposal of the Chinese Ministry of Education to the League of Nations Committee on Intellectual Cooperation regarding the method of guiding the studies of Chinese students, if developed properly, will also become an important task.

For this reason, I ask to meet with the various technical agencies of the League of Nations and the International Labor Office to examine the appropriate methods for various issues and various individual experiences, so that the Technical Advisory Committee and the Labor Office can have a basis for proposing concrete construction.

6. The National Economic Council recently decided on the business plan for 1934 and stipulated the business expenses as 15 million yuan. The business expenses this year are three times the amount used in the previous two years. The provincial governments in the construction areas selected by the government will receive considerable encouragement and assistance, and the selected economic facilities are already on track. With the solid foundation established, the agency for national economic development will be based on this. This is the original wish of the government when it established the National Economic Council three years ago. In the past three years, the domestic and international situation has been extremely serious. In order to adapt to the environment and take care of the facts, the Council must make its organization flexible and gradually evolve to an appropriate position to develop administrative capacity. The standing committee members of the National Economic Council are now filled by the most important authorities in the government. They must review, research, design, and be responsible for raising funds. The method of technical cooperation between China and the League of Nations is also determined by the standing committee, and the principle of technical cooperation is not limited to the business subsidized or directly handled by the National Economic Council. The cooperation of other ministries and commissions in handling technical business can also be determined by the standing committee.

7. Technical cooperation should continue to be based on the agreements signed in 1931 and renewed in 1933. The method of its implementation should be within the scope of the organization of the League of Nations' technical agencies, and should be flexible so that it can be determined according to the economic and political changes of the present time and the needs of the situation. The purpose of technical cooperation is to enable Chinese and foreign technical agencies to cooperate and consolidate the foundation and authority of China's economic development agencies.

8. Sir Arthur Salter was recently hired by the National Economic Council to study China's current economic and financial problems. Mr. Salter spent three months in China and has recently compiled an investigation report. The matters discussed in the report are listed in order as follows: China in the world economic recession, the Chinese silver dollar and other currencies, the concentration of silver in Shanghai, the equalization of international payments, the equalization of trade, the decline in prices, currency and monetary policy, the re-entry of foreign capital into China, the government revenue and expenditure budget, national debt, agricultural production, industry, railways, and highways. Mr. Salter's report is rich in data and can be used to form an economic development policy.

League of Nations' Opinion After the Publication of the Report - Contains Elements That May Cause Serious Competition 4

(Geneva) According to sources close to the League of Nations, Japan's opposition to technical cooperation between the League of Nations and China is actually to undermine the increasingly solid Republic of China. The consolidation of China will deal a fatal blow to Japan's hope of dominating the Far East. They also said that the Rajchman report is purely technical and has no political odor, but the various provisions for rationalizing the cotton and silk industries, building water conservancy projects, and building highways are enough to restore China's prosperity and contain elements that may cause serious competition. It is not yet known what action the League of Nations Administrative Council will take on the Rajchman report. It is believed that the method will be determined after the Advisory Committee on Chinese Affairs reviews the results on May 14. (Reuters dispatch on the 9th)

The League of Nations Praises China's Construction Movement 5

(Geneva) Judging from the report on the League of Nations' technical cooperation plan with China currently under consideration, it can be seen that although the League of Nations has many concerns about directly resisting Japan, it is making sincere efforts to support the General Assembly's resolution of February 24 last year to give China any international assistance it requests to strengthen its foundation. The report has been designated by the authorities as purely technical and non-political, but it is believed that after the implementation of the plan, it will deal a major blow to Japan's policy of controlling China. The efforts to expand China's recent construction movement are also highly praised here. (Central News Agency dispatch on the 9th)

The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs Expresses Opposition 6

(Tokyo) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs expressed its opposition to the Rajchman plan on technical assistance to China published by the League of Nations, believing that the plan cannot save China. 1. The fundamental prerequisite for solving the problem is to promote China's stability and unification, which must be realized by China itself. Otherwise, the joint assistance of the powers will not succeed. Therefore, the Rajchman plan cannot be implemented. 2. If the Rajchman plan can be established, the economic and financial assistance will inevitably have political implications and be politically used in China's internal affairs. However, judging from the examples of several international loans to China in the past, it is already quite obvious. Therefore, the Rajchman plan has the risk of being used to promote China's internal strife. 3. Japan basically agrees with technical and economic assistance to China in principle. However, Japan has the power to maintain peace and stability in East Asia. Therefore, Japan is absolutely opposed to any assistance plan that despises this most relevant fact. (Dentsu dispatch on the 10th)

(Tokyo) A Reuters reporter visited officials of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs today and asked about the opinion of the League of Nations officials in Geneva who suspected that Japan's opposition to technical cooperation between the League of Nations and China was actually to undermine China's consolidation. Officials of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs refused to comment on this "unreasonable interpretation by the League of Nations," but said that Japan's judgment of the overall situation in the Far East is far superior to and more important than that of any country, including the League of Nations. Japan is now pursuing a definite policy aimed at maintaining China's security and order. At the beginning of Rajchman's visit to China, his mission was indeed technical, but later he turned into a practically enthusiastic political agent. (Reuters dispatch on the 10th)

(Tokyo) The Japan United News Agency published an article today with the authorization of the authorities, foreshadowing the possibility that the Japanese government will warn China or the League of Nations about the issue of providing financial assistance to China. The article stated that it is now known that the Japanese government intends to adhere to its previously announced policy, that is, if international financial assistance to China does not first reorganize China's international debt, the result will inevitably increase China's burden in vain. The huge amount of money remitted by overseas Chinese every year has recently ended, and the excess of imports over exports last year was more than 600 million yuan. If this continues, China will inevitably go bankrupt in a few years. It is rumored that the League of Nations will continue to provide financial assistance to China in accordance with the Rajchman report's list of so-called technical assistance, including assistance to the National Economic Council in Nanjing. This move will increase the burden on the Chinese people and delay China's unification, security, and prosperity. This move will be counterproductive to the promotion of peace in the Far East. Japan cannot tolerate this, because Japan understands that it is the conservator of peace in the Far East. It is now believed that the Japanese government's warning will clearly state that there is a need to suspend consideration of international financial assistance to China, and will state that if any situation arises in China's financial affairs due to international assistance, the Japanese government will take appropriate plans to respond as necessary. (Reuters dispatch on the 10th)

Daily News Promotes Debt Collection: Hoping China Will Reorganize Debts to Japan 7

(Tokyo) Today, the Tokyo Nichi-Nichi Shimbun published an editorial entitled "Hoping China Will Reorganize Debts to Japan," the gist of which is that, given China's current situation, these huge old debts are difficult to reorganize, which we acknowledge. However, if the National Government genuinely intends to resolve the matter, it can discover concrete methods such as repaying part of the old debts or converting part of them into new loans. If the National Government continues to ignore the old debts, it will be difficult to hope for future Sino-Japanese economic cooperation. The National Government's initiative to reorganize debts to Japan is worthy of celebration as it can improve Sino-Japanese relations. (10th Dispatch from Dentsu)

Current Affairs Commentary

On the War on the Arabian Peninsula 8

— Heng

Two weeks ago, foreign dispatches reported the outbreak of war between Hejaz and Yemen. Subsequent news was scarce, with no developments reported. However, according to reports in recent days, Yemen has been defeated by Hejaz and its capital is about to be besieged. This indicates that the war between the two sides has not ceased since its beginning and has now reached a decisive stage. The reason for the temporary silence in news is that in the preceding days, the world was focused on the more important Far East issue and had no time to attend to this smaller problem. In fact, this problem is also worth discussing.

Observing recent telegrams, the current war between Hejaz and Yemen contains the background of British and Italian imperialism. Overly sensitive observers suspect that Britain and Italy may conflict because of this. However, the inside story is not so simple. To accurately understand the significance of this war, it is necessary to examine the various events on the Arabian Peninsula since the Great War; otherwise, all judgments will be inadequate.

Hejaz and Yemen are both Islamic countries on the Arabian Peninsula, both located by the Red Sea. Before the Great War, the entire Arabian Peninsula belonged to Turkey, so both Hejaz and Yemen were subordinate to Turkey. At the beginning of the European War, the Muslims of Arabia responded to Turkey's call and stood on the side of Germany and Austria. British Red Sea traffic was temporarily threatened. At this time, Britain's war effort, in terms of both material and manpower, largely depended on support from India. Securing Red Sea traffic was imperative, so Britain vigorously sought control of the Arabian Peninsula. Its dispatch of troops to Mesopotamia, Palestine, and Iraq, its Red Sea coastal guard, its instigation of the Sharif of Mecca, Hussein bin Ali, to revolt against Turkey, and its promise of independence to the Arabs were all concrete manifestations of its co-optation policy. Only after the Great War did Turkey completely relinquish sovereignty over the Arabian Peninsula. However, the independence of the Arabs has still not been fully realized. Among them, Syria, Palestine, the League of Nations Mandate of Transjordan (historically a Jewish area, but now populated mostly by Arabs), and Mesopotamia were all divided by Britain and France under the guise of the League of Nations mandate. Hejaz, which was not partitioned, also became a British sphere of influence under Hussein's rule. The only regions that were relatively independent and not controlled by the great powers were Asir, between Hejaz and Yemen, and Nejd and Hasa under the rule of Ibn Saud, as well as Kuwait in the Persian Gulf. Apart from these, most of the Arabian Peninsula was under British control. However, the British were still not satisfied and constantly sought to use King Hussein of Hejaz as a puppet to achieve their goal of controlling the entire peninsula. In 1924, they took advantage of the opportunity when Turkey deposed the Caliph of Islam to support Hussein as the Caliph, thereby winning over the hearts of various tribes in Arabia. Unexpectedly, this move by the British not only failed to appease the various tribes on the Arabian Peninsula but also aroused the anger of Ibn Saud, leading to a major movement to overthrow Hussein. As a result, Ibn Saud defeated Hussein and seized Hejaz. By 1930, Ibn Saud had also conquered Asir, which shielded Yemen. Therefore, the King of Hejaz reported in today's newspapers is actually the former King of Nejd. In 1932, as the territory under his jurisdiction had greatly increased compared to before, it had been renamed the Kingdom of Saudi Arabia. Now he is simply called the King of Hejaz.

If we do not overlook the course of these events, then the current war on the Arabian Peninsula is not difficult to understand. In short, it is a manifestation of the Arabian national independence and unification movement. After the Great War, it was only natural for the Arab tribes to seek to break free from shackles and become fully independent countries. Ibn Saud is leading this independence and unification movement. Since Ibn Saud defeated the pro-British Hussein in 1924-1925 and seized Hejaz, he has quelled rebellions, conquered Asir, and his prestige has grown daily. Apart from the areas within the sphere of influence of Britain and France, the only places that Ibn Saud's power has not reached are Yemen on the Red Sea coast and Kuwait in the Persian Gulf. Therefore, the prospect of unification is not far off. Although Ibn Saud has recently reconciled with Britain, it is an exaggeration to say that he is a British puppet. According to a Reuters dispatch from London, the British Minister to Hejaz inquired about the destination of the Hejaz authorities' troops and stated that if the Hejaz troops invaded the Aden region, Britain would intervene. This shows that the British may not necessarily regard Ibn Saud as a tool for expanding British influence.

However, Italy's ambition in Yemen has been harbored for a long time. Geographically, Yemen is directly opposite the Italian colony of Eritrea on the other side of the Red Sea, making it extremely convenient for Italian operations. In addition, the British have no intention of controlling Yemen, which makes the Italian efforts all the more active. In recent years, such as the training of the Yemeni army and economic and financial assistance, all have been proceeding steadily. The intention is to share the spoils on the Arabian Peninsula. Since Ibn Saud annexed Asir, Yemen has been uneasy and its reliance on Italy has become more pronounced. From the internal perspective, the current war is nothing more than a clash between the Yemeni king's quest to achieve his own separatist path and Ibn Saud's unification movement. From the external relations perspective, it is Italy's plot to seize Yemen as a preparation for operating on the Arabian Peninsula. The war between the two countries has now reached a decisive stage. Whether the Arab unification movement can be completed can be predicted here. What we can predict is that this unification movement is not only disliked by Italy, but it is also unlikely that Britain will readily agree. Therefore, Italy's secret assistance to Yemen is within reason. As for Britain's assistance to Hejaz, it seems too early to say, and the talk of British-Italian conflict is even more exaggerated. After all, Britain, France, and Italy each have colonies around the Red Sea, which has not started today and have always been at peace with each other. If it is said that the Italian operation in Yemen can constitute a British-Italian conflict, who would believe it?

The symptoms were the same as the previous day. After enemas and medical treatment, they were all fine. However, the nature of the toxic substance is still under investigation. It is generally believed that it may be due to unclean food or beverages. Ni Zhengcong, the section chief of the hygiene office, and Jiang Jiemin, accompanied by doctors and nurses, went to the scene in the afternoon for a detailed investigation and brought back the beverages and leftover food for chemical testing. It will take some time to reach a conclusion. Seventeen more villagers outside Ximen, Nanjing, were found to be poisoned in the afternoon of the 10th. The investigation revealed that it was suspected to be caused by contaminated salt. The two shops of Dexinglong and Taimaoheng were ordered to stop selling salt pending chemical testing. (Special dispatch from the 10th)

US Silver Bill Situation Increasingly Chaotic; Roosevelt Intends to Delay; Senate Silver Faction Experiences Rifts; Treasury Proposal Also Rejected 74

(Washington) President Roosevelt issued a statement supplementing his views, silver senators also made new statements, the silver faction itself revealed open rifts, and senators and the Treasury Department hastily drafted a silver bill. All these contradictory facts have made the silver bill situation extremely chaotic today.

President Roosevelt explained his attitude towards the silver bill, stating that any silver policy decided by Congress must be in the form of a directive, not a permit, but the method of implementing this policy must be left to the chief executive. He also believed that the silver bill does not necessarily need to be passed in this session of Congress. President Roosevelt also solemnly stated that he is still studying the suggestions made by the silver faction at yesterday's White House meeting, and that these suggestions are not particularly novel. Regarding the suggestion to increase silver reserves, President Roosevelt believed that there were many precedents in American history, and that in some periods, the amount of silver reserves was greater than what is currently proposed. The reduction of silver reserves to 12% is only a recent phenomenon.

The division within the silver faction itself is due to Senator Borah hindering the Senate silver faction meeting. Borah, speaking to reporters, said angrily that the proposed silver bill is purely permissive, which is not what he wants. He would rather wait and appeal to the people of the whole country before mid-June, and they should reject a mandatory silver bill, which will be clear by then.

After Borah left the Senate meeting today, Senator King stated that the silver faction still does not have a unified opinion on the specific silver bill. This statement was met with disagreement from all sides, as the silver bill drafted by Senator Thomas had already been submitted by the silver faction to Treasury Secretary Morgenthau, and this bill is what they consider to be the specific bill. Thomas's new bill combines all the bills he had previously proposed into one, and it was drafted based on a plan that the silver faction claimed to have obtained the President's approval. Its contents are as follows: (1) Stipulates the composition of currency reserves, with gold accounting for 75% and silver accounting for 25%.

(2) Acquires silver for the state at a purchase price not exceeding 50 cents per ounce.

(3) Grants the President the power to act at his discretion to purchase silver in accordance with the 25% silver reserve policy.

In addition to Thomas's bill, other silver senators have many other proposals. For example, Borah, Pittman, and King each submitted a silver draft to Treasury Secretary Morgenthau. Borah's proposal advocates state ownership of silver and the purchase of silver, and issues it to the President in a mandatory manner. King's and Pittman's drafts are said to be the same as Thomas's bill, and it is also said that Treasury Secretary Morgenthau and Treasury General Counsel Oliphant also submitted drafts to the silver faction.

Treasury Secretary Morgenthau and Oliphant consulted with Senator Pittman this morning, and then held a meeting with the entire silver faction in the afternoon. They will continue to meet tomorrow.

Silver senators are all busy drafting and have no time to meet with reporters, but King still took the time to tell people that the silver bill is expected to be passed in this session of Congress. (National Telegram, 8th)

US Treasury's Proposal Rejected by Silver Faction 75

(Washington) An Associated Press reporter learned today that after listening to the fifteen articles of the silver bill proposed by Treasury Secretary Morgenthau, the silver senators rejected them all. Morgenthau's draft is as follows: (1) The President is free to dispose of the silver in the country to clarify the government's policy of minting silver coins, without making provisions for the state ownership of silver.

(2) Purchase silver reserves only with existing hard currency and without issuing additional silver certificates. When Treasury officials read the proposal to this point, silver faction leader Borah left the meeting and declared that he could not agree with this weak silver bill. Therefore, the bill was not read any further. Treasury Secretary Morgenthau said that President Roosevelt had not yet reviewed the draft, and the silver senators believed that the plan they had proposed at the White House meeting on Tuesday would eventually be adopted by the government. (National Telegram, 9th)

Roosevelt's Consideration: No Final Decision Immediately 76

(Washington) It was learned today that President Roosevelt is giving serious consideration to the proposal to nationalize silver, but is unwilling to make a final judgment on the silver legislation bill until the draft is formed. Regarding the 25% silver currency reserve, President Roosevelt can accept permissive and guiding legislation. In other words, if Congress declares its approval of this type of reserve, President Roosevelt will regard this declaration as a mandatory declaration of policy. President Roosevelt believes that the timing of the implementation of this policy should be decided by the President. It was heard that President Roosevelt stated during his meeting with silver senators yesterday that the government can only purchase silver bars and cannot confiscate silver coins in the same way as gold. Senator Pittman stated today that there has been excellent progress in the drafting of the silver legislation bill, and it can be submitted to President Roosevelt this week. (Reuters, 9th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt declared that he is currently studying whether the nationalization of silver is appropriate, but will not make any decision until the bill is submitted to the President by Congress for review. Furthermore, once the nationalization of silver is implemented, the government will limit the silver it recovers to silver bars, while silver coins will still be allowed to circulate in the market. According to the above-mentioned bill, after silver is nationalized, it will be used as a currency reserve, with gold accounting for 75% and silver accounting for 25%. (Havas, 9th)

Roosevelt Issues Declaration on War Debt Issue: Suggests Debt Collection; Reducing Debt Burden Can Also Be Considered 77

(Washington) The war debt issue has taken an important place on the political stage today. President Roosevelt has officially declared that the United States insists on collecting war debts, but can consider the requests of countries that are currently experiencing difficulties and can reduce their obligations. As for the question of whether to accept a partial payment as a sign of good faith in June this year, it must be decided on a case-by-case basis. Currently, one point of serious consideration in the war debt issue is whether countries that make temporary partial payments to show good faith should be regarded as countries that have not fulfilled their obligations, and whether the clause in the Johnson Act stating that the United States cannot provide loans to them should apply. The recent British budget did not include an item for repaying US debt. (Reuters, 9th)

(Washington) The White House announced today that the United States is still willing to accept the suggestions of European debtor nations regarding war debt control. The President stated that how the war debt due on June 15 will be handled will depend on the situation at that time. The President continued, stating that European countries have not yet made any representations to the United States regarding good faith payments and war debt reductions. The Johnson Act has not affected the basic policy of the United States over the past year. The so-called basic policy is that if debtor nations believe they are unable to pay their debts, they can negotiate with creditor nations. The current situation is one example. The US government, on the surface, still hopes to recover more than US$12 billion in war debts and various emergency investments, but in reality, the government may have other opinions. (National Telegram, 9th)

(New York) The New York Commercial Daily's Washington dispatch stated that President Roosevelt will declare in his message to Congress that the United States cannot accept partial payment of war debts as a sign of good faith in the future, and will declare that additional legislation is neither necessary nor appropriate. The New York Times reported that congressional leaders have notified President Roosevelt that Congress interprets the Johnson Act as recognizing that even good faith payments by debtor nations cannot be regarded as fulfilling their obligations, and that President Roosevelt must acknowledge this point. (Reuters, 10th)

Direct US-Russia Navigation; Passage Through Northern Sea Route; May Be Realized in the Future 78

Shumilovitch, General Manager of the Leningrad Soviet Arctic Company, predicted that commercial navigation directly from Siberia to the United States through the Northern Sea Route may be realized in the future. Once this route is opened, the resources of the Lena River basin will be developed. The area is rich in products, with lush trees, minerals, and timber. Transportation costs can be reduced, and merchant ships can operate on a regular basis on this route. A large icebreaker must be prepared in Vladivostok to assist merchant ships in passing through the frozen area of ​​the Zalesky Strait. (National Telegram, 10th)

Japan and Germany Echo Each Other; Japanese Training Squadron Welcomed in Germany 80

(Berlin) Commander Matsushita of the Japanese training squadron and his entourage are currently visiting Berlin. German officials are treating them very warmly. President Hindenburg, Chancellor Hitler, General Goering, and Foreign Minister Neurath have taken turns receiving them. Matsushita spoke at a reception hosted by the German-Japanese Association today, saying that Japan's homeland is now in a position that is somewhat similar to that of pre-war Germany. The difficulties are self-evident, but the entire Japanese people are united and know that they must do their best and work hard to promote the welfare of the people of their homeland. Germany and Japan have the same efficiency, courage, and perseverance, which is no coincidence. Germany and Japan are currently facing various international difficulties and must work for peace, but this peace must be a peace of equal rights. Matsushita's remarks have attracted great attention here. (Reuters, 10th)

(Berlin) A semi-official political diplomatic newsletter published an article explaining the friendship between Germany and Japan, saying that the Japanese have a deep understanding of the intellectual and spiritual foundations of German life, which is greatly admired by Germany. The report also said that Japan's current situation is no different from that of Germany in 1914. (Havas, 9th)

Britain Tries to Make a Last Effort to Save Disarmament "Decline"; Advocates Narrowing Scope of Negotiations; Negotiate Convention on Limiting Air Force; Diplomatic Contacts Proceed Simultaneously in London and Paris 81

(London) All parties are now actively trying to save the destruction of the Disarmament Conference. Foreign Secretary Simon is meeting with General Ribbentrop, the disarmament special envoy sent by German Chancellor Hitler, this afternoon. Disarmament Conference Chairman Henderson also met with French Foreign Minister Barthou and the British Ambassador to Paris several times on his way to Geneva. Before Barthou and Henderson met, the French government issued a statement saying that the statement that the French Foreign Minister will make to Henderson has been approved by the cabinet. This almost means that France has made a final statement. (Reuters, 10th)

(London) The British Cabinet reviewed the crisis of the Disarmament Conference today and decided on the final rescue method. According to reliable sources, the British Cabinet approved the proposal to France, Germany, and other countries to propose an air force disarmament convention. This type of convention is also the only compromise point in the Geneva talks. If France refuses to discuss this type of convention, the Disarmament Conference may end there. At the same time, a movement aimed at an air force disarmament convention is currently underway. It is learned that France may refuse to limit the air force convention, as this type of convention is tantamount to acknowledging the equality of the German air force as legitimate. Britain has hinted that it is willing to recognize German air force equality within eight years. If France firmly refuses to discuss Britain's proposal, the Disarmament Conference may be permanently adjourned. The British Cabinet's recent attitude clearly supports ending the conference and implementing the expansion of its national defense. An Associated Press reporter learned today that the new armament advisor of the German Foreign Ministry, von Ribbentrop, has secretly arrived in London and has met with Foreign Secretary Simon and Lord Privy Seal Eden. He also plans to consult with Prime Minister MacDonald on the general disarmament situation and work on the proposed air force convention. The Cabinet meeting today decided that if Disarmament Chairman Henderson, Lord Privy Seal Eden, and French Foreign Minister Barthou have any hope of reaching a compromise on air force disarmament, then Foreign Secretary Simon should follow Eden to Geneva on Thursday after Eden goes to Geneva on Saturday. The British military is very willing for France, Germany, and Italy to participate in the air force disarmament conference. After the British air force fell to fifth place, the British government has clearly expressed concern about the aerial security of its territories. (National Telegram, 10th)

(London) The Foreign Cabinet held a regular meeting to discuss the disarmament issue. As a result of the meeting, it is learned that the government has issued instructions to the British delegation attending the Geneva meeting. The scope of the instructions is very broad, and the principles indicated therein are as follows: (1) Use every possible effort to negotiate with Paris or Geneva to ensure the establishment of a disarmament convention. Therefore, the fact that Lord Privy Seal Eden, the British representative attending the Disarmament Conference, went to Paris to consult with French Foreign Minister Barthou is generally considered extremely important. (2) After the UK's last attempt to compromise, if there is a possibility that the UK's disarmament plan will be finally agreed upon by various countries, the UK representative will propose to conclude a convention limiting the application of the air force. Blue Mountains Arrives in Tokyo, Hirota Greets at the Station, Blue Mountains Delivers Speech on Mission to Japan, Hirota Strives for Understanding Between Japan and Australia 89

(10th Dispatch from Rengo)

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota has decided to take the opportunity of Australian Deputy Prime Minister and Foreign Minister Blue Mountains' visit to Japan to have a thorough discussion on fundamentally adjusting Japan-Australia trade. The current Japan-Australia trade relationship is as follows: (1) Australia's trade surplus with Japan is consistently large. Last year, Australia's trade surplus with Japan reached 15.3 million yuan and is expected to increase in the future. (2) Australia's exports to Japan account for 10% of its total exports, with wheat accounting for about 21% of its total production. (3) If Australia, as an agricultural country, were to completely cut off its annual wheat exports to Japan, it would inevitably cause a profound agricultural panic. (4) Japan relies on Australia for 97% of its annual wheat imports, so severing trade relations with Australia would also be a fatal blow. As mentioned above, Japan and Australia have a close and inseparable relationship. Therefore, it is necessary for Japan to adjust its trade deficit with Australia to some extent. In this regard, it is not impossible for Japan's modern industrial capacity and Australia's current productive capacity to shake hands in a mutually beneficial way. Regarding this matter, the Foreign Minister plans to urge Foreign Minister Blue Mountains to consider and propose fundamental measures to adjust the one-sided trade. (10th Dispatch from Dentsu)

Next Year is the Key to World Peace and War: The Success or Failure of the Naval Conference and the Survival of the League of Nations 90

(Geneva) Diplomats here today issued a prophetic warning, stating that next year will be one of the most critical years for world peace since the signing of the Treaty of Versailles. The most important event will be the 1935 Naval Conference. The Saar plebiscite and the withdrawal of Japan and Germany from the League of Nations will also come to fruition next year. These three issues will plunge the world into panic. According to pessimistic observers, if this year's disarmament conference ends in complete failure, the League of Nations in 1935 may cease to be the League of Nations. However, officials in charge of the League of Nations do not express excessive pessimism. Although they believe that the League of Nations is currently facing many difficulties and that the coming year will be even more difficult to deal with, they believe that if they can overcome these future difficulties, the future League of Nations will be healthier. According to a senior official of the League of Nations, the League of Nations is now in a transitional period from the European era to the era of the entire world, because the League of Nations is committed to the interests of Europe and also to the interests of the entire world. Some League of Nations officials also stated that although some member states have left the League of Nations, major powers such as the Soviet Union and the United States are now trying to get closer to the League of Nations. The United States' cooperation with the League of Nations is currently the closest and most extensive. The Soviet Union's tendency to join the League of Nations is also very obvious. Supporters of the League of Nations are very pleased with this news. They all believe that the League of Nations is currently in trouble and must struggle. Next year will encounter the biggest political panic. Europe will focus on the Saar plebiscite, the Naval Conference, and the difficult issues of Japan and Germany's departure. As for the League of Nations itself, it currently has two propositions: one faction advocates allowing the United States and Russia to join and urging Japan and Germany to return to the League of Nations to enhance the League of Nations' position. These supporters of the League of Nations all advocate that the League of Nations should aim for world peace and not be limited by the European continent. The other faction advocates that the League of Nations should focus on Europe. This faction believes that the League of Nations can fulfill its task by implementing the Treaty of Versailles. However, all members of the League of Nations recognize that the success or failure of the 1935 Naval Conference will directly affect the League of Nations itself. They believe that the Far Eastern issue is closely related to the League of Nations. Although this conference is not led by the League of Nations, the outcome of the conference is the key to resolving the Far Eastern situation. Its impact on the League of Nations and the whole world is self-evident. Many observers say that whether Japan and Germany will return to the League of Nations will depend on the success or failure of the 1935 Naval Conference. No one can answer the above questions at present, but they have been deeply considered by diplomats and politicians. (10th Dispatch from Kokumin)

Political Turmoil in Japan is Unpredictable (Tokyo Correspondence) 93

Saito Cabinet's Transition Period Extended

Military Intervention Limited Secretly

The Saito Cabinet was originally a transitional government during the so-called emergency period. Observations in Japanese political circles believed that it would be difficult for Saito to continue for a long time. Moreover, the military had long had the intention of seizing power and establishing a strong cabinet, so Saito's downfall seemed inevitable. In addition, the political parties had also expressed dissatisfaction with him, especially after the ethics issue occurred and Ichiro Hatoyama resigned. The cabinet's downfall should have been inevitable. However, he did not fall, and there was even a situation of long-term continuation. The reason why he did not fall is that the military itself did not completely advocate the immediate establishment of a military cabinet. In particular, the powerful figures in the upper echelons felt that it was unwise to abandon the constitution, and that challenging foreign countries also contained huge risks. Secondly, the political parties were dissatisfied with the current cabinet, but they had many concerns. They were afraid that once a military cabinet was realized, the political parties would completely lose the opportunity to interfere in political power. At the same time, the political parties had lost the sympathy of the people, and the opportunity to form a cabinet became even less. Therefore, the Saito Cabinet was able to maintain itself.

This time, for the issue of supplementing the Minister of Education, the Seiyukai did not immediately recommend someone to join the cabinet, which was another stalemate. It seemed that the Seiyukai was about to part ways with the Saito Cabinet. Unexpectedly, the military called for a tough diplomatic policy, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs issued an unofficial statement on April 17, so the cabinet was very praised by the military, and of course it also calmed the military's dissatisfaction. The stability of the Saito Cabinet increased somewhat.

There was also an unexpected gain for the Saito Cabinet, which was the Privy Council. Because Kiichiro Hiranuma was the Vice President and the leader of the right-wing faction, he was one of the powerful successors to the position of Prime Minister after Saito's downfall. He also had a tacit understanding with the military, especially the young officers, so he always wanted to instigate a movement to overthrow the cabinet. However, he was very incompatible with the elder statesman Kinmochi Saionji, so he lost the support of the zaibatsu and some of the military. The navy was even more dissatisfied with him. Therefore, the movement to overthrow the cabinet that he instigated could only mobilize the movement of the National League faction. This time, Yuzaburo Kuratomi (President of the Privy Council) resigned from the position of President because he could not defeat Hiranuma's power and it was inconvenient to engage in open struggle, using eye disease as an excuse. This should have been a good opportunity for Hiranuma. He could easily launch a movement to overthrow the cabinet, and he could also use the power of the Privy Council to restrain the various actions of the cabinet. This was Hiranuma's good fortune and the prelude to the transformation of Japanese politics. Who knew that Kinmochi Saionji happened to enter Tokyo at this time? The Saito Cabinet in distress received powerful help. Regarding Kuratomi's resignation, according to the usual practice, after Yamagata resigned, Kiyoura was promoted to President with the qualifications of Vice President. After Kiyoura, Hamao was also promoted to President with the qualifications of Vice President. After Hamao resigned, Hozumi was also promoted to President with the qualifications of Vice President. Kuratomi's appointment as President was also the same as succeeding Hozumi with the qualifications of Vice President. In short, the Privy Council has always had the tradition that the President is always promoted by the Vice President. But this time, it violated the precedent, and Hiranuma Kiichiro was not promoted to Vice President, but instead went to invite the former Minister of the Imperial Household, Kiyotake Ichiki, to serve as President. In Japan, where bureaucracy prevails, how could such a counter-conventional thing be allowed to happen?

The reason is that not only is there a gap in feelings between Hiranuma and Saito, but if the position of President falls on Hiranuma, then even if Saito can barely maintain it, he will eventually resign in a short period of time, or even cause a major political turmoil. This is the maturity of military rule and the death of Japanese constitutional politics. Saionji, who adhered to the theory of constitutional convention, was even more opposed to this. The political parties, of course, were also unwilling to place all the political power in the hands of the military. Therefore, when Saito recommended Ichiki as President, he did not discuss it with Hiranuma, and it was a means to suppress Hiranuma. After Hiranuma found out, he was extremely dissatisfied with Saito and could not actively launch a movement to overthrow the cabinet for a while. He will probably submit his resignation after a considerable period of time and resign from the position of Vice President of the Privy Council to carry out activities from another aspect. (May 7)

Liaoning Puppet Military Police Uprising Gains Momentum, Triggered by Japanese Army Confiscating Firearms, Rebels Immediately Unite with Volunteer Army 94

(Shenyang Correspondence) In addition to actively constructing military works in the Northeast, Japan aims to eliminate internal elements and wipe out the volunteer army. Recently, it has been observed that the puppet army often evades attacks on the volunteer army, so special precautions have been taken, fearing that they will collude with the volunteer army. The puppet military police also feel uneasy, fearing unforeseen circumstances. Furthermore, persuaded by patriotic people at home who resist the enemy, they have successively rebelled and surrendered to our volunteer army. Among them are Wang Dianzhong, commander of the puppet garrison in Yingkou, with more than 400 troops, and Wang Yongcheng, captain of the puppet police team in Fusong, with more than 300 troops. It was found that Wang Dianzhong's troops, due to the persuasion of a special commissioner from a certain national salvation organization, deeply felt the danger of being discarded after their usefulness was over. They expressed a good impression of the volunteer army. Whenever they attacked the volunteer army in the eastern region, they only put on a show and were unwilling to put in any effort, which was discovered by the Japanese army. In late last month, the Japanese army launched a large-scale attack on Deng Tiemei's troops and detained Wang Dianzhong, escorting him to Shenyang or Changchun, with his life or death unknown. They also disarmed two companies of the army stationed in Tianzhuangtai. Yang Yinzhou, the regimental commander of the army stationed in Yingkou, upon hearing the news, immediately led his headquarters of more than 400 troops to rebel, surrounded and confiscated more than 200 firearms from the Japanese garrison, and killed more than 100 Japanese soldiers. The market was chaotic for a while. The Japanese navy blockaded the seaport, and ships changed to landing in Dalian. Furthermore, Wang Yongcheng was from Tang Juhua's volunteer army and had been serving as the captain of the Fusong County Public Security Brigade under the puppet government for nearly two years. He often supplied the eastern volunteer army with military supplies. Recently, because the Japanese repeatedly limited the confiscation of firearms and disbanded the troops, Wang suddenly led all the police regiment of more than 300 people to rebel, taking the Japanese army stationed in Fusong by surprise, surrounding and disarming them, seizing more than 100 firearms, and then attacked Mengjiang County, Jilin, inflicting heavy damage on the Japanese army. He is now in contact with a special commissioner from a certain national salvation organization and is preparing to launch a large-scale attack this summer when the green gauze screens rise with the volunteer armies of Wang Fengge, Deng Tiemei, Ren Fuxiang, and others. According to information from the headquarters of the Japanese Kwantung Army, regarding the anti-Japanese and punitive puppet situation of the volunteer army in various parts of the Northeast, in January and February of this year, the Japanese army mobilized to deal with the volunteer army in various places a total of 401 times, with 53,876 officers and soldiers participating (excluding the puppet army). Statistics show that there are 282 volunteer army leaders and 97,638 troops. Japanese military intelligence is likely to be accurate, and the volunteer army still has more than 100,000 people fighting in a bloody battle, which proves that the hearts of the people in the Northeast have not died. Recently, Captain Hanabu of the Japanese army stationed in Jilin committed suicide, and Colonel Iizuka was killed in battle. The county chiefs of the three counties of An, Fu, and Meng in Liaoning Province led the police and militias to rebel, all of which were triggered by the confiscation of civilian guns and the forced purchase of civilian land. The rebellion of Wang Dianzhong's puppet garrison in Yingkou was also caused by the Japanese detaining Wang Dianzhong to resolve the puppet army. Therefore, the people in the Liaodong area would rather voluntarily send their guns to the volunteer army than hand them over to the Japanese puppet authorities. Wang Fengge's volunteer army alone has received thousands of guns, greatly increasing its strength. The people in various counties on the Jehol border have jointly refused to hand over their guns, resulting in fierce battles. All these events are showing a tendency to gradually expand. Recently, as the time for the green gauze screens to rise is approaching and the clouds of war between Japan and Russia are gradually thickening, the bloodbath in the Northeast will give the anti-Japanese volunteer army a boost.

Kong Xiangxi Arrives in Hankou, Expresses Financial Opinions, Scheduled to Inspect Hunan 95

(Hankou Correspondence) Kong Xiangxi, Deputy President of the Executive Yuan and Minister of Finance, went to Jiangxi from Beijing to visit Chiang Kai-shek, intending to come to Hubei immediately. Because of a foot ailment, he stayed in Lushan for a while. He descended the mountain on the 8th, accompanied by his wife, Madam Soong Ai-ling, and Madam Soong Mei-ling, the wife of Chairman Chiang Kai-shek. They sailed on the warship "Haixing" from Xunyang and arrived in Hankou at 11:00 AM on the 9th. Military and political dignitaries gave a grand welcome. A reporter interviewed Mr. Kong on the ship and had a long conversation. A record is as follows: Mr. Kong said, "Since I have been in charge of the Ministry of Finance, I have been shocked by the lack of recovery from the people's difficulties and the daily depletion of national resources. I have been thinking of engaging in rectification in order to enrich the country and nourish the people. During the Fourth Plenary Session of the Central Committee, I proposed two proposals for rectifying land taxes and reducing surcharges, which were both passed and handed over to the Executive Yuan for verification and handling. As I am in charge of accounting and politics, I will naturally urge their implementation. Because there are too many exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous taxes, the people cannot bear them. Moreover, land taxes exceed the regular contributions by several times, so they must be resolutely abolished. This kind of long-standing accumulation of exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes is due to the failure to determine local budgets, which is the crux of the matter. In the future, to abolish exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes, budgets must first be determined to make income and expenditure suitable. County budgets are approved by the province, and surplus funds are submitted to the provincial treasury. If there is a shortfall, the provincial treasury will subsidize it. Provincial budgets are approved by the central government, and surplus funds are submitted to the central government for approval and storage for construction purposes. If there is a shortfall, it will also be subsidized by the central government. In this way, income and expenditure will have fixed measures, financial resources will not be depleted, and the people will be spared from harassment. Furthermore, in order to implement benefits to the fullest extent, a national financial conference will be convened on the 21st of this month to discuss in detail, focusing on the abolition of exorbitant and miscellaneous taxes, the reduction of surcharges, and the determination of budgets in order to obtain a complete solution. My departure from Beijing this time is to inspect the finances of the five provinces of Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Henan, because the above five provinces are bandit suppression areas, the finances urgently need to be rectified, and the people especially hope to recover. When I was in Jiangxi, I visited Chairman Chiang Kai-shek and inspected the finances. The anti-bandit military affairs in that province have indeed made significant progress and can be concluded after the autumn. However, the local area is devastated, and the people have fled, so we must step up recruitment and construction. Moreover, those who follow the bandits include those who are coerced and those who follow blindly, so we must add persuasion. Then, the clearing of the countryside and the post-war settlement can be practical. The central government is obligated to bear the post-war expenses in the bandit areas and is making every effort to raise funds. All the funds for treating the symptoms have been allocated in full, and a portion of the funds for treating the root causes has also been allocated. In the future, we will continue to strive to raise funds to meet urgent needs. Educational expenses, part of which will be taken from land tax surcharges, are being considered so that we can take care of both. Hubei Province's request for independent education fees, because what it requested is the salt tax, which is related to the entire issue, must also be considered. The road construction fees for the seven provinces were originally allocated from the US cotton and wheat loans. The project is progressing rapidly, and the original plan has been fully completed. A new plan is now underway. There has been no road along the Yangtze River, which has greatly affected industrial production. In order to meet the needs of the times, the construction of roads is necessary." Regarding the silver issue, the world is paying attention, and our country is a silver-using country, so we must not ignore it. We are currently studying it in detail and investigating the national silver situation, and soliciting opinions from the provincial governments in order to comprehensively decide on a method, aiming for mutual benefit between the national economy and the people's livelihood." Mr. Kong's entourage included Xu Jianping, Director of the General Affairs Department of the Ministry of Finance, Secretary Tan Xian, Counselor Li Yuwan, Qian Cunzhi, Deputy Director of the Central Bank's Confidential Affairs Department, and Adjutant Zhou Huang. Mr. Kong stayed at the Central Bank, and Mrs. Kong and Mrs. Chiang stayed at Yih Village. That evening, Mr. Kong discussed important matters with Zhang Xueliang, and then summoned Jiang Han Customs Superintendent Xi Debing, Tobacco and Alcohol Stamp Bureau Director Li Rongkai, Mining Tax Office Director Zhu Shenshao, Salt Affairs Inspection Office Director Yao Yuanlun, and Unified Tax Bureau Director Xie Fencheng, and attended a banquet for officials and bankers. Because the financial conference is about to open, Mr. Kong was unable to stay for long and is scheduled to inspect Hunan on the 10th. Zhang Xueliang also plans to inspect Hunan and may travel with Mr. Kong. (9th)

Jiangsu Construction Department Promotes Rural Sideline Occupations in Jiangbei: Implementation Plan Approved, Utilizing Abandoned Land for Production 96

Zhenjiang Correspondence: The Jiangsu Construction Department, noting the worsening rural economy in Jiangbei in recent years and the increasingly simple livelihoods of farmers, who rely solely on the cultivation of wheat, cotton, rice, and miscellaneous grains as their source of income, which is no longer sufficient to cope with the increasingly complex modern social life, seeks to remedy and improve the situation. In addition to striving for improvement, enrichment, and reform, it should also promote various rural sideline occupations. Therefore, the organization of a Committee for Promoting Rural Sideline Occupations in Jiangbei has been established. After repeated meetings and discussions, an implementation plan for promoting rural sideline occupations in Jiangbei was drafted and approved by the 656th meeting of the Jiangsu Provincial Government. The guiding principles are roughly as follows: (1) Utilize wasteland, vacant land, and gaps for planting or raising livestock; (2) Utilize abandoned water surfaces for raising fish, turtles, or oysters, and utilize rivers, lakes, and seas for collecting various aquatic products; (3) Utilize farmers' spare time and energy to engage in various agricultural livestock, agricultural product manufacturing, or handicrafts; (4) Utilize joint credit to borrow funds from outside sources to regulate finance and develop production; (5) Utilize agricultural products as raw materials, or purchase raw materials from outside, and within the possible scope, utilize machinery to process and refine them, or utilize leftover and waste materials to produce more products, thereby increasing their value; (6) Inspect the supply and demand of various rural sideline products at home and abroad, and select those businesses with development prospects that can plug leaks and promote beneficial rights to be undertaken first. All of the above should be linked to the main agricultural occupation, and the promotion of sideline occupations should not hinder the main occupation of profitable production. The scope of promotion is divided into (1) Planting category, including crop cultivation and horticulture; (2) Animal husbandry category, including animal husbandry, poultry farming, beekeeping, and sericulture; (3) Handicraft category, including agricultural product manufacturing and rural handicrafts; (4) Forestry category, including tree planting, bamboo forest production and manufacturing, and forest product collection and hunting; (5) Aquaculture category, including aquaculture, fishing, algae harvesting, moss harvesting, shellfish harvesting, and all aquatic product manufacturing. The promotion methods are divided into investigation, publicity, oral publicity, written publicity, material object publicity, training personnel, recruiting trainees, establishing specialized training classes, establishing women's work-study classes, holding lectures, establishing people's livelihood factories, or vagrant skills training centers. School teaching materials should pay attention to sideline occupations. The types of promotion should be determined based on the situation of each county in Jiangbei, and the types of sideline occupations that should be promoted urgently in each county at present are decided below (omitted).

### Robbery and Assault in Nanxu Village, Qingpu 97
