They first rushed to Zhang Yonglu's house, rummaged through chests and cabinets, and forced him to reveal the location of his hidden silver. When Zhang, seeing the situation, panicked and answered slowly, he was immediately shot in the face by a robber's gun. The bullet exited from the back of his head, and his injuries were quite serious. There is fear for his life. According to a comprehensive calculation after the event, the loss amounted to more than five hundred yuan.

### Follow-up Report on the Search of Minsheng Company in Kunshan 98

The previous report detailed how Luo Qixiang, the police chief sent by the county government, and Yang Chunsheng, the captain of the water police team, led more than ten officers to search Minsheng Company on North Main Street in the city for drugs without success. It is now learned that Wu Zijin, the manager of the company, learned of the situation in Taicang and immediately came to Kunshan to inspect the goods. He also published an announcement in various newspapers to explain the situation and prepared to negotiate with the authorities to reassure businesses. County Magistrate Peng Baichuan, realizing that there had been a misunderstanding and fearing that the situation would escalate, ordered the two captains, Luo and Yang, to go to the company on the morning of the 9th to apologize to Manager Wu. He also sent someone to invite Wu to the government office to explain the misunderstanding and express his apologies in person. After Wu agreed, the storm finally subsided.

### Minor Homicide Occurs in Jiusheng Lane, Suzhou 99

Xiao Di, the second son of Xu Yongliang, No. 14 Jiusheng Lane, Hulong Street, was only eight years old. A few days ago, Xiao Di and Huang Yanren (10 years old, from Haimen), a young apprentice at the Hanzhen engraving shop in Chayuanchang, were playing at the door when a quarrel suddenly broke out over a trivial matter, and they even started fighting each other. Xiao Di was ultimately younger and weaker, and was injured by Huang Yanren. After returning home, Xiao Di, fearing that he would be scolded by his mother, did not dare to say anything. By the day before yesterday, Xiao Di's injuries were serious, so he was sent to Shende Hospital for treatment. He eventually died due to lung damage, which could not be cured, at about 4:00 pm on the 9th. Xiao Di's father, Xu Yongliang, reported the case to the police precinct in charge and summoned the young perpetrator, Huang Yanren, for questioning and sent him to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. The District Prosecutor's Office sent personnel to conduct an inspection yesterday (the 10th) afternoon, ordered preparations for a coffin and burial, and began investigating the case.

### Changshu County Defense Corps Begins Training 100

The County Defense Corps of this county has been ordered to draw up training, with each district limited to send 15 people to the city for training. The training location has now been selected at Zifusi Temple at Sanliqiao outside the South Gate, and Lu Zengyu and Huang Renpu have been appointed as captains of the first and second squadrons, and Wan Xiaoquan as the special affairs officer. ### Representatives Go to Beijing to Petition 101

Since the city and township telephone of this county was taken over by the province last month, the Ministry of Communications Telephone Bureau, due to its long-distance telephone business relationship, plans to remove the three lines that were borrowed to connect the urban area. However, if this matter is implemented, the city and township telephone will inevitably be equal to a formality, which is opposed by all parties. However, the company is forced to comply with the order of the ministry and is in a dilemma. Currently, eight representatives of township heads selected by each township district set off for Beijing on the 9th to petition the Ministry of Communications, requesting that the three lines not be removed in order to maintain communication.

### The Grandeur of the Wuxi Racing Incense Fair 102

Today is the 28th day of the third month of the abandoned lunar calendar. There is usually a grand and lively racing fair in the city, and this year it is especially grand, exhausting the ability to compete for novelty and victory, and enjoying the fun of sound and color for a whole day. It is unprecedented. Early stage of actively preparing, it has caused a sensation far and wide. People from other ports come to Wuxi to watch the fair, and they come in droves. As of yesterday morning, all the rooms in the large and small hotels in the city have been booked up. The Wuxi-Cheng long-distance bus company will also open a special bus for watching the fair today (the 11th). There are a total of seven racing associations today, commonly known as the Seven Temples to Dongyue, namely Zhang Yuan'an, Yansheng Palace, Fu Palace, Yanshousi Palace, South Water Immortal Temple, West Water Immortal Temple, and City God Temple. All of them are racing to the Dongyue Emperor. The racing association is divided into daytime and nighttime events. The daytime fair will open around noon, and the nighttime fair will be lively all night long. According to reporters' preliminary inquiries, the front section of the Fu Palace fair is mostly historical costumes from famous historical dramas, using wheeled floats and pavilions for installation, Wagang Village, Zhaojun's Peace Marriage, Five Elements Mountain, Changban Slope, Zhong Kui Marrying His Sister, Eight Hammers Making a Scene at Zhuxian Town, Gorgeous Fate, Mother Meng Teaching Her Son, Seven Swords and Thirteen Knights, Seven Captures of Meng Huo, Heavenly Maid Scattering Flowers, etc. are extremely dazzling. Especially in the play "Black Basin Case", the fair specially installed wireless electricity, and Guotai Radio Station broadcasted "Black Basin Case", which was vivid and colorful, opening a new page. Zhang Henshui's long novel "Modern Youth" published in the Xinwen Bao, "Tears and Laughter", and Lianhua Film Company's "Humanity", "Sister Flowers", and "Tarzan the Ape Man" were all made into dramas. There are also Tan Ci "Pearl Tower", and the "New Life Movement" advocating "Propriety, Righteousness, Integrity, and Shame". "Propriety" is Wu Jizi's politeness and concession for the country, "Righteousness" is Guan Yu's righteousness reaching the clouds, "Integrity" is Lu Longqi's integrity and incorruptibility, "Shame" is King Goujian of Yue's greatest shame. The West Water Immortal Temple's fair is also unprecedentedly grand. In addition to borrowing a large number of antiques and jade from Suzhou for display, because the horses in Wuxi were all hired out, a large number of horses were specially rented from seven counties including Suzhou, Changzhou, and Kunshan. The play is full of intrigue and conflict. The entire crew of the Xinguang Stage is invited to perform a shocking, mechanical scene, with sound and color. There are also Nezha Stirring up the Sea, Da Huagu, Lian Jinfeng, Hong Bi Yuan Bianliang Tu, Eight Beauty Racing Cars, Killing Fish at Home, Du Shiniang, and the Moon Palace Dance and Pigsy Getting Married in "Journey to the West". More than 300 children are recruited to decorate as little monkeys, each riding a bicycle, arranged in a long formation. There are also the old and new dramas in the film "Love and Duty" "The Female Knight of the Barren River", and "Huang Huiru Visiting Prison", "Puppet on Stage", "Lu Chunyang Turning Stones into Gold", and "Rock Driving a Fast Car". Many young girls are also selected to hold 20 flower baskets, presenting flowers, large flower baskets, Dragon Palace grease dance, Immortal World, Qingwen Mending the Fur Coat, Magu Presenting Longevity, etc. The South Water Immortal Temple's fair also has the entire crew of the Nanyao Great Stage, performing dramas such as Xue Rengui's Conquest of the East, which is extremely prosperous. On this day, all Peking Opera theaters in the city stopped performing because the actors participated in the racing fair.

### Female Worker Commits Suicide by Drowning After Being Wrongly Accused 103

Xia Jun, the 18-year-old daughter of Xu Ludong, a resident of Huangxu Town, Zhenjiang, is now a female worker at a certain cloth factory in Changjing, Jiangyin. A certain factory staff member wrongly accused Xia Jun of stealing four yuan, and sent a letter to her family, urging them to take her back quickly. After receiving the letter, Xia Jun's father, Ludong, took his wife from the town by car to Wuxi on the 7th, and went to Changjing. That night, he hired a small boat in Changjing and took his daughter back. He asked her about the truth. When the boat passed the Sanruan Bridge area, about four miles away from Zhangjing Bridge in the Seventh District of this county, because it was too late to drive to the city, it was anchored in front of the Yuanji Cocoon Bank of the Chamber of Commerce at that place for the night. At about 12 o'clock, Ludong woke up and unexpectedly found that his daughter, Xia Jun, had disappeared. He searched with a light, but could not find her. The next (day) morning, he reported to the second squadron and third detachment of the police stationed in the cocoon bank, and took out Xia Jun's photo and left a note stating the mailing address, asking them to help find her. Ludong then took the original boat to Wuxi, transferred to a rice cart and returned to the town. It was not until about 5:00 pm that day that Xia Jun's body suddenly floated in the river in front of the cocoon bank. Mei Shengbao, the chief of the 461st Tu, then pulled the body to the shore and sent someone to guard it, and reported to the local court in the city, requesting an autopsy. After receiving the report, the Prosecutor's Office, led by Prosecutor Ren, Wang the coroner, and bailiffs, took a wheel to the countryside at 7:00 am yesterday (the 10th) to conduct an autopsy. It was confirmed that she had fallen into the river and died before her death. After the autopsy, he ordered Tu Zheng to temporarily coffin her body and wait for the corpse to be claimed by her family. The reason for Xu Xiajun's death this time was nothing more than that she was wronged and unable to vent her anger, so she committed suicide by drowning.

### Villagers in Changzhou Commit Suicide by Hanging After Being Falsely Accused 104

Sun Delu, a villager in Sunjiatou Village, Xushu Township, Seventh District of Wuyi, was recently taken to his door by Sun Linhai and others from the same village, holding hemp ropes, and falsely accused of being a thief, and was insulted in every possible way. Sun Linhai then went back, but Delu was very angry, so he hanged himself on the barrier at night and died. The next morning, his wife discovered it and untied the noose, but Delu had already died. The case was heard by Yang Dehui, the patrol officer of the public security substation in charge. After sending police to investigate and confirm the facts, he planned to take Sun Linhai and others to the office, but they had all fled without a trace. Patrol Officer Yang reported the situation to the Public Security Bureau. Yesterday (the 9th), in addition to ordering the arrest of the fugitives, the Public Security Bureau also ordered a letter to be sent to the County Inspection Office to send personnel to conduct an autopsy for investigation and handling.

### Current Status of Jiangsu Province Highways in Zhenjiang 105

In recent years, the responsible authorities of Jiangsu Province highways have urged various counties to actively requisition labor for construction. The detailed situation of each highway that has been built and is not yet completed has been learned as follows. Those that have been completed include the Yi-Wu, Jing-Jian (Jing-Mo section), Su-Jia, Sheng-Ju, Zhen-Yang, and Zhen-Dan-Jin lines. The length of the trunk lines is 252 kilometers, the trunk lines open to dirt roads are 582 kilometers, the branch lines are 815 kilometers, and the county roads are 734 kilometers, totaling 2,761 kilometers. Those that are not yet completed and are being built are the Xi-Hu, Zhen-Cheng, Yang-Qing, Pu-Yang (Pukou to Yangzhou), Li-Wu, Jing-Jian (Nanjing to Jianping, Fujian), and Su-Chang lines. The length of the trunk lines is 238 kilometers, the branch lines are 952 kilometers, and the county roads are 1,787 kilometers, totaling 2,977 kilometers. The trunk lines that have not been started are 242 kilometers, the branch lines are 676 kilometers, and the county roads are 117 kilometers, totaling 1,035 kilometers. The Jing-Hang National Highway is currently being renovated. According to the person in charge, it will take half a year to complete all the above unfinished lines.

### The Zhenjiang-Yangzhou Road Extends to Qingjiangpu in Yangzhou 106

Transportation in Jiangbei has always been inconvenient. Since the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou bus service was opened, transportation from the provincial capital to Xing has not been difficult. However, the 300-mile long journey from Yangzhou to Qingjiangpu is still hindered. Now the Yang-Qing and Yang-Liu highways are about to be completed. Lu Shaozhou, the founder of the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou Bus Company, plans to borrow the Yang-Qing Road to operate the bus service, so as to connect with the Zhenjiang-Yangzhou Road. It has been approved by the Construction Department. It is planned to entrust the road to Lu for management. The method is that the roadbed is lent out by the public, and the road surface is laid by Lu and Lu Zhou two managers. From the completion of the road and the opening of traffic, a nine-year patent will be given. After the expiration, it will be taken back by the public, or a method of extending the extension will be determined. The company will first pay a deposit. As soon as the contract is signed, the road surface can be organized.

### Pessimistic Outlook on Silkworm Flooding in Four Townships in Xiaoshan 110

Due to the uneven warm and cold weather this year, the early batch of silkworms in the four townships of Xiaoshan was mostly damaged. Now it has passed the second sleep, but most of them have changed, and the sleep heads are uneven. There are also many who eat wet leaves and vomit yellow water. The late batch is in the first sleep, and the silkworms' bodies have also changed a lot. Except for the improved silkworm species in the eastern township, which shows a slight advantage, the western and southern townships are even more irreparable. Therefore, very few cocoon factories are preparing to open. It is difficult to be optimistic about the problem of villagers selling cocoons.

### Zhang Ji Returned from Fujian Yesterday, Talking About Japan's Lack of Movement in South China, the Remaining Bandits in Fujian Province Can Be Suppressed Soon, Zhang Returned to Beijing by Night Train that Evening to Report Back 115

Chen Zhaoying, the special commissioner of the Fujian Party Affairs, took office in Fujian a few days ago. Japan Has No Movement in South China 116

According to Zhang, there have been rumors recently that Japan is actively planning to invade South China, and that Japanese consuls held a conference on the other side in Taiwan, etc. During my stay in Fujian this time, I stayed for several days and did not see any movement by the Japanese side, so I don't know the details. We should deal with the Japanese side's conspiracy calmly and calmly respond. If we only talk in vain, it will be of no help. As for my trip to Fujian this time, it was purely to represent the central government in attending Mr. Chen Zhaoying's inauguration ceremony, and there were no other tasks.

Order in Fujian Province Gradually Restored 117

Order in Fujian has now been gradually restored. Fujian Province was originally a prosperous area with many products. Special attention should be paid to the downstream area of the Minjiang River, so that the products of Fujian Province can be transported and sold to other provinces. Fujian's finances are currently extremely difficult. Xu Fu, the director of the Department of Finance, will go to Beijing within a few days to ask the central government for remedial measures. As for the construction of Fujian Province, it is currently difficult to develop due to economic difficulties. I sincerely hope that the financial circles of Shanghai will go to Fujian to invest, so that the rich resources of Fujian Province can be developed, and all construction can be relied on to progress.

Suppression of Bandits Shows Progress, Suppression Can Be Expected 118

Regarding the military affairs of bandit suppression in Fujian Province, with the efforts and cooperation of the party, government, and military, there has been considerable progress. The period of suppression can be expected soon. People in Fujian Province call the rebellion of Chen Mingshu and others this time the "Fujian Rebellion" in the newspapers, which is quite dissatisfied, because this rebellion was the rebellion of Chen Mingshu and others, not the rebellion of the Fujianese. I hope that my comrades in the press will correct it. Zhang, along with Di Ying, secretary of the Central Political Council, and Li Shijia, a member of the Fujian Provincial Committee, took the night train to Beijing at 11:00 pm last night.

### Jiangsu Provincial Government and Shanghai Banking Syndicate Established Construction Loan, Totaling 1.5 Million Yuan, Guaranteed by Provincial Business Tax 119

Shen Baixian, the chairman of the Jiangsu Provincial Government and the director of the Construction Department, recently actively promoted construction projects and completed the Liutang River project and important highway projects in various counties. He specially established a 1.5 million yuan construction loan with various banks in Shanghai. The contract was signed yesterday. The loan will be allocated in succession after July. The reporter of Shenshi News Agency specially interviewed the banking syndicate and the representatives of the Jiangsu Provincial Government yesterday to learn the details, which are as follows:

Participating Banks 120

This time, the Jiangsu Provincial Government approached Shanghai to negotiate a loan, totaling 1.5 million yuan, all for construction purposes. Chairman Chen, Director Shen, and others entrusted General Manager Xu of Jiangsu Provincial Bank to approach various banks in Shanghai separately. Now it has been completely successful. The participating banks and the amount of the loan are: Bank of China, Jiangsu, and Jiangsu Farmers, 300,000 yuan each. The remaining 600,000 yuan will be borrowed by Transportation, Jin City, Mainland, Salt Industry, and Zhongnan, 100,000 yuan each, totaling 1.5 million yuan, and Jiangsu is promoted as the representative bank, responsible for receiving and delivering the loan and handling repayment procedures. All loans, except for the Bank of China, which will be released by the Beijing branch, and the Jiangsu Farmers Bank, which will be released directly by Zhenjiang, will be delivered to the Jiangsu Bank in succession for remittance to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Finance for verification and collection.

Contract Content 121

The loan contract between the two parties has been signed, and the Jiangsu Provincial Government has also approved its establishment. The content of the contract is: (1) The term of the loan is set at one year; (2) Starting from July 1 of this year, 125,000 yuan will be repaid every month until the end of June next year, when the entire amount will be paid off; (3) The interest rate is set at 9% per week; (4) The business tax revenue of the entire province will be used as the collateral for the loan. According to the business tax revenue of Jiangsu Province, the annual budget is about 2 million yuan, but the actual collection varies from year to year, but it will not be less than 1.5 million yuan in total. Jiangsu Bank was originally the agency bank for the provincial treasury. Each month, 125,000 yuan will be deducted from the business tax revenue and distributed to each bank in succession until it is fully repaid.

Use of Loan 122

The use of this loan is specifically designated for dredging the Liutang River in Jiangbei and for transportation highways. The Liutang River is very important for the irrigation of farmland in Jiangbei and is part of the Huai River diversion project. It has been carried out in segments since January of this year. Each section of the project has been completed by 60% to 70% and will be completed soon. However, due to the huge amount of money required and the urgent need for it, the project can be carried out smoothly and the completion can be seen early after the provincial government actively plans for the establishment of this loan. As for the highway network in Jiangsu Province, it is under construction actively. All trunk roads in the province are planned and repaired by the Construction Department. However, because the ground in Jiangsu Province is vast and the bays are winding, the required expenses are also huge. In the future, it will also be allocated from this loan in order to complete it as soon as possible.

### Qian and Dai Go Abroad for Inspection, Qian Delivers Speech Before Departure 123

Qian Chengxu and Dai Gengxin, members of the China Industrial Federation, went abroad to inspect industries. They boarded the Italian mail ship Conte Verde at 9:00 pm last night and set sail this morning. Qian delivered a speech before his departure, which is recorded as follows:

Stabilize Flour Prices 124

Qian first said that since the work on stabilizing flour market prices began, it is still under negotiation with the government. Although the government has accepted the principles proposed by the Industrial Federation, the steps and methods are still under consideration by the government. However, the Industrial Federation's proposition is to establish a minimum market price as a principle, in order to raise the foundation of flour. In the short term, it is expected that there will be considerable measures, so that the miserably falling flour mills can be slightly saved from their dangerous situation.

Factory Inspection 125

The government has repeatedly advocated for the simultaneous implementation of factory inspections nationwide. However, due to jurisdictional issues within the concessions, the matter has been submitted to the current National Labor Conference for discussion. I am honored to serve as a consultant to the capitalist side of this year's Labor Conference and will do my utmost. However, whether or not this case should be brought up is a matter for the entire delegation to decide. In my personal opinion, Chinese production has reached a state of extreme decline. Factory inspections must be conducted by personnel with adequate training who understand the technical and managerial aspects of factories in order to achieve tangible results. Otherwise, it will not only be ineffective but may also lead to disputes.

Southwest Investigation 126

The Southwest Industrial Investigation Team has been formed and has already dispatched Mr. Zheng Yi, secretary of Wing On Textile Company, to conduct a preliminary investigation. He is expected to return to Shanghai within the year. Mr. Zheng has made several reports on various industrial issues in the Southwest. He will invite many domestic manufacturers with excellent products to transport their goods to the region to open up markets and simultaneously support the development of existing local industries, such as the pottery industry in Guangxi, which is already relatively well-established. The local Bureau of Industry and Commerce has sent a written invitation to pottery engineers to travel there soon to study improvement methods.

Japanese Formation of New Consortium for China: Banking Sector Has Not Received Report; Refusal to be Expressed if Such Circumstances Arise in the Future 127

According to the Central News Agency, it has recently been reported by the Japanese side that Mr. Suma, the Japanese Consul-General in Beijing, and Mr. Uchina and Mr. Kanai, have been negotiating in Shanghai for several days regarding the issue of reorganizing old debts owed to China and plan to form a new consortium for China, adding that due to the limited strength of the Japanese side, they are trying to persuade various banks in Shanghai to join, and that the negotiations are becoming concrete, etc. Yesterday morning, a Central News Agency reporter inquired about this with the Chinese and foreign banking sectors in Shanghai. It is understood that the extent of the contact between the Japanese Consul-General in Beijing Mr. Suma and the Japanese financial sector is unknown to foreigners. However, the idea of forming a banking consortium and persuading various banks in Shanghai to join is merely speculation. The Chinese and foreign banking sectors in this port have not received any written or verbal invitations from the Japanese side. Various banking sectors have also stated that if such circumstances arise in the future, they will definitely refuse.

Other Items 128

Finally, Mr. Qian also stated that the China Industrial Association has made great progress in its work in recent years. During my trip abroad, I have entrusted Mr. Hu Xiyuan to temporarily act on my behalf. The following are the plans that are scheduled to be actively carried out within six months: (1) the publication of the *Industrial Times*. This publication will specifically publish the status of Chinese industry with the goal of promoting the development of Chinese industry. It will be published in both Chinese and Western languages and will be promoted abroad in the future. Ten major factories have already been established as basic shareholders, and work can begin soon. (2) the establishment of a Standards Committee, which has been understood by the Ministry of Industry. The main purpose of this committee is to identify various commodities for the purpose of promoting strength and to maintain and promote genuine, good domestic products, with the aim of ensuring the future development of domestic goods.

The First Phase of Disaster Relief Bonds: The Ninth Drawing Yesterday; Number "08" Wins Prize of $300,000; Payments by the Three Banks Start on the 31st 129

The ninth drawing of bonds for the repayment of principal for the first phase of the 1931 Disaster Relief Public Bonds was held at 10:00 a.m. this morning at the Bankers' Association. Mr. Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing the night before to preside over the drawing. Representatives from the Audit Council and other organizations also attended the meeting to supervise. As a result, the number "08" was drawn, representing a principal of $300,000. Payments will be made by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications in various locations starting on the 31st of this month.

Drawing Yesterday Morning 130

In addition to Mr. Jiang Lufu, Director of the Public Debt Department of the Ministry of Finance, who came to Shanghai to preside over the drawing, Mr. Xu Hu from the Audit Council, Mr. Lin Lemin from the General Customs, Mr. Ju Zhijing from the First Special District Local Court, Mr. Yan Dayou from the Money Industry Association, Mr. Jin Wenyuan from the Central Bank, Mr. Zhu Qizhen from the Bank of China, Mr. Mao Rui from the Bank of Communications, and Mr. Song Ziliang, manager of the National Products Bank, were also present. The meeting was chaired by Director Jiang.

Chairman's Report 131

Today is the day for the ninth drawing of bonds for the repayment of principal for the first phase of the 1931 Disaster Relief Public Bonds. I am extremely pleased that you have come to attend and observe. The total amount of bonds issued for the first phase of the 1931 Disaster Relief Public Bonds was $30 million. In addition to the principal that has already been drawn from the first to eighth drawings, today's drawing is for the ninth drawing, totaling $300,000. All bonds that are drawn will be paid, along with the tenth installment of interest, by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications in various locations starting on the 31st of this month. Payments will be made in cash regardless of location. Please have the supervisors examine the drawn bonds and the bond stubs in order to carry out the drawing.

Winning Numbers 132

After the Chairman's report, he designated personnel to carry out the drawing. One bond with the number "08" was drawn and presented to the Chairman for inspection, then handed over to the supervisors for verification. The winning number was then displayed on a plaque and announced. At the same time, it was registered by the registrar and sealed by the supervisors to certify it. The total principal to be repaid is $300,000. The numbers of the winning bonds and the amounts will be published in the *Finance Daily* and other newspapers in Beijing and elsewhere so that the public can be informed. Payments will be made starting on the 31st of this month.

Sino-Japanese Outstanding Issues: Possibility of Direct Negotiations 137

According to the Xin Sheng News Agency, regarding the possibility of direct negotiations between China and Japan, a certain dignitary stated yesterday that this is not impossible and will depend on the proposals made by the Japanese side, in other words, the subject matter of the negotiations. If they truly insist on forcing us to recognize the puppet organization, this is absolutely impossible. Otherwise, the resolution of various outstanding issues between China and Japan, as is being discussed outside, is still possible. Our country is an independent nation, not a protectorate of any other country. Therefore, our diplomacy also has its own independence. Moreover, there are many outstanding issues between China and Japan, including the Sino-Japanese Treaty, consular jurisdiction, and water and electricity negotiations, among others. If such problems are resolved, it would be welcomed by us. The reason why our country opposed direct negotiations in the League of Nations in the past was that Japan wanted to use gunboat diplomacy to force us to recognize its so-called Five Principles (that is, the Five Principles proposed by Japanese representative Yoshizawa after the September 18th Incident). Therefore, we opposed it. Later, after the puppet regime was established, Japan wanted to force us into direct negotiations to recognize the puppet organization, so we refused again. In short, direct negotiations are not impossible. Any negotiations that force us to recognize or involve the loss of sovereignty and humiliation of the country are impossible.

Second Water Cutoff at Peide Lane, Xinzha Road Yesterday Afternoon; Company Refuses Payment by Tenants on Behalf of Landlord; Taxpayers' Association Sends Letter to the Municipal Council Forwarding Original Letter from Representatives 141

The water cutoff dispute at Peide Lane on Xinzha Road, after water had been restored, it was suddenly cut off again, which greatly angered all the tenants. A meeting was held yesterday to discuss how to respond, and assistance was requested from all sectors. Mr. Wang Xiangu, a lawyer representing the tenants of the lane, responded to the water company's letter, which has also been forwarded to the Municipal Council by the Taxpayers' Association. The details are as follows:

Company Refuses 142

The water cutoff dispute in the lane has been protracted. After the company automatically restored the water supply a few days ago, the situation had become calmer. At 10:45 a.m. on the 9th, the tenant representatives of the lane, Liu Chengyong and Wang Jieqing, accompanied by lawyer Wang Xiangu, brought cash of $500 to the company for negotiations, intending to show consideration for the company by prepaying water bills for one and a half months on behalf of the landlords. Unexpectedly, the company refused to accept payment, saying that a contract must be signed first. The representatives replied that if they wanted to sign a contract, they would have to follow the authorization of the general assembly, and they could not act on their own. They then made an appointment to go again on the morning of the 10th. Upon returning, a general assembly of all tenants was convened that evening, attended by more than 150 people. It was decided on the spot that a one-sided contract was unacceptable. If the company cut off the water again, they could only let it happen.

Another Water Cutoff 143

At around 10:00 a.m. on the 10th, the two representatives, Liu and Wang, acting in accordance with the decision of the general assembly, went to the water company again for negotiations. The company still insisted that a contract must be signed first as a condition for accepting payment. The representatives then stated that if it was absolutely necessary to sign a contract first, then the contract must state that the water bills paid were on behalf of the landlords, because the landlords in the lane had not deducted the water bills included in the rent and returned them to the tenants, and the tenants could not bear a double obligation. However, the company resolutely refused, and the negotiations ended without result. Unexpectedly, when the representatives returned to the lane at 11:35 a.m., the water supply in the lane had already been cut off by the company at 11:30 a.m.

Request for Mediation 144

After the water cutoff, at around 3:00 p.m. on the afternoon of the same day, the tenant representative of the lane, Liu Chengxiong, accompanied by lawyer Wang Xiangu, went to the Municipal Council to explain the process of the water cutoff and requested mediation. Mr. He Dehui, a council member, received them and expressed his willingness to forward the request. Last night, the tenants of the lane convened an executive committee to discuss how to proceed with the negotiations and decided to issue a declaration requesting assistance from all sectors, expressing their determination to persevere to the end and never yield.

Wang Xiangu's Letter 145

Lawyer Wang Xiangu, representing the tenants of the lane, sent a letter to the Taxpayers' Association, stating: "We are writing to you on behalf of all the tenants of Peide Lane on Xinzha Road. We have recently received a reply from the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association, which quoted a reply from the Public Concession Municipal Council stating, 'We acknowledge receipt of your letter regarding the water cutoff at Peide Lane. Upon investigation, it is found that one clause in the contract mentioned in your letter is not applicable in this situation, because the landlord is acting in accordance with Section 2(e) of the water rate schedule of the contract signed between this Bureau and the Shanghai Water Company on May 5, 1933 (should be May 3), which states that the company will sign contracts separately with each household in a batch of houses. Furthermore, the clause mentioned in your letter does not state that "the water supply cannot be cut off," but rather that "the water company is not bound by restrictions." There seems to be some misunderstanding about this matter, which should be clearly explained. The current unfortunate dispute seems to be purely a dispute between the landlord and the tenants. We hereby reply accordingly.' Upon investigation, the application of Section 2(e) of the water rate schedule in Part C of the contract signed between the Bureau and the water company on May 5, 1933 (actually May 3) should be after the landlord has deducted the water bills included in the rent and returned them to the tenants. In this case of Peide Lane, the water bills have always been paid by the landlord and included in the rent. Before the landlord has deducted the water bills and returned them to the tenants, it is the same as the water bills still being paid by the landlord. Therefore, the provisions of that section should not be invoked. Even if the landlord has requested the water company to install separate water meters and have the tenants pay their own water bills, it is only an expression of intent. If he does not actually fulfill the refund of the water bills included in the rent to the tenants, the landlord is still in a state where he should be responsible for paying the water bills. Therefore, the provisions in the contract that the water company must not cut off the water supply in houses where the landlord pays the water bills, if there are people living in the house, should be invoked. The principle is very clear. The water company did not investigate whether the landlord had refunded the water bills included in the rent to the tenants and, upon receiving the landlord's request to have the tenants install separate water meters, cut off the water supply immediately, which is evidence that the water company colluded with the landlord to oppress the tenants. The Municipal Council knew that it violated the contract but did not correct it, which means that they jointly violated the contract and automatically lost their right to exercise their functions and bear the trust of the taxpayers in the entire concession. As for the statement that the provision in the contract that the water supply must not be cut off does not state that "the water company must not cut off the water supply" but rather that "the water company is not bound by restrictions," it is even more a distortion of the law. The tenants request that the same clause in last year's contract, as printed by the Municipal Council in the Chinese-language Public Bulletin, No. 22, Vol. 4, of May 26, 1933, on page 340, section (e), subsection 3, be copied as follows: 'Regardless of the circumstances, if the water bills for a house are paid by the landlord, the company has no obligation to comply with the landlord's request to stop the water supply to all or part of the house as long as the house or part of it is still occupied, and the landlord is still responsible for paying the full water bills.' According to the above, the water bills for Peide Lane are 'paid by the landlord,' and since the landlord has not deducted the water bills included in the rent and returned them to the tenants, he is still in a state where he should be responsible for paying the water bills. The landlord's request to the water company to install separate water meters for the tenants is, in fact, 'the landlord's request to the company to stop the water supply to all of the house.' The water company naturally 'has no obligation to comply.' It should be known that the Municipal Council's invitation to merchants to operate the water supply is originally to fulfill the important responsibility entrusted by the taxpayers, so that the water supply, which is essential for life, is never lacking, for fear that the water company may be deceived by the landlord or collude with him to use water cutoffs to oppress the tenants. Therefore, there is this provision. The main subject of the clause is the resident, and the legal relationship between the landlord and the water company is 'water supply' and 'payment.' If interpreted from the opposite perspective, it is even more sufficient to fully demonstrate the thoroughness of its protective significance: (1) The water company agrees to the landlord's request to stop the water supply, 'protecting the landlord'; (2) If the house is occupied, the water company must not stop the water supply, 'protecting the tenants'; (3) Even if the water company does not stop the water supply, but the water bills for the house are paid by the landlord, the water company can still seek compensation from the landlord, so that it will not suffer losses. The tenants are taxpayers and should make every effort to protect the clauses that protect the tenants. Fortunately, the water company was able to realize its mistake and automatically restored the water supply at 2:00 p.m. on the 5th of this month, which is a good demonstration of the British people's willingness to correct their mistakes. It is hoped that the Chief Executive of the Municipal Council will strictly enforce this provision against the water company in the future and that such inhumane behavior will not occur again. Furthermore, the water company's breach of contract in cutting off the water supply for as long as twenty days has caused the tenants deep and heavy spiritual and material suffering and losses. In addition to declaring that the misunderstanding mentioned in the Municipal Council's reply does not exist, we specifically entrust you to send this letter to the Shanghai Concession Chinese Taxpayers' Association, requesting that it be forwarded to the Shanghai Public Concession Municipal Council to inform the water company to quickly express its apologies and compensate for the corresponding losses in order to show the company's sincerity in faithfully complying with the contract. We hereby report the facts and request that you handle the matter accordingly. Sincerely, Wang Xiangu, Lawyer."

Letter to the Municipal Council 146

The Taxpayers' Association forwarded a letter to the Municipal Council, stating: "We are writing to you regarding the water cutoff dispute in Peide Lane on Xinzha Road. We previously received your Bureau's reply and have forwarded it accordingly. We have now received a letter from lawyer Wang Xiangu, representing all the tenants of Peide Lane, regarding the corrections to your Bureau's previous reply. We are sending the original letter along with a copy of the same and request that you handle the matter accordingly. Sincerely,"

The Tianjin Tooth Tax Bureau Detains Fresh Fruit Case: Lu Wenshao and Others Go to Beijing to Petition, Seeking the Abolition of Disguised Likin 148

Since the Tianjin Tooth Tax Bureau detained the fresh fruit of Shanghai fruit merchants, it has led to a strike in transportation. The industry has sent representatives to Tianjin to negotiate with the authorities, but to no avail. Yesterday, they again petitioned the Municipal Chamber of Commerce for protection. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce immediately appointed Standing Committee member Lu Wenshao, along with industry representatives Cai Runshen, Xu Runsheng, Xu Yunqing, and Tianjin fruit merchant representatives, to go to Beijing today to petition various ministries and departments. They also carried a petition, the original text of which is recorded below:

Presented for the matter of petitioning, it is reported that the fruit and produce industry claims that the tooth tax originated in the Qing Dynasty. The original purpose of creating this tax was to include the nature of restriction and management, which is the same as the modern so-called franchise business, and the meaning of levying a special business tax. Likin, on the other hand, was created during the Xianfeng and Tongzhi military uprisings. Judging from its historical origin and the nature of tax collection, it is completely different from the tooth tax.

Since the Republic of China, the tooth tax method has still followed the Qing system. The general rules in various provinces are roughly divided into two types: sticker tax and annual tax. Stickers are divided into long-term and short-term. Tax is paid once when renewing. The annual tax is paid annually. The amount of tax depends entirely on the commercial prosperity and the size of the business in the tooth industry area. It is divided into several levels, and each level is further divided into several grades. In short, the tooth tax is a behavior tax, not a goods tax. The target of the tax is the tooth industry, not ordinary vendors.

From the perspective of its behavior tax, it is similar to the business tax implemented in recent years. Therefore, Article 20 of the Business Tax Law formulated by the Legislative Yuan and Article 11 of the Supplementary Measures to the General Outline for the Collection of Business Tax in Various Provinces promulgated by the Ministry of Finance all allow it to be temporarily collected separately according to the original tax rate as a transitional measure.

Because the tooth tax is different from the likin collected on goods and does not conflict with the order to abolish likin, the central government, in order to take care of local tax revenue, temporarily does not hold it accountable with the business tax, but allows it to retain its original tax rate. This is a point that those who handle the tooth tax in various provinces cannot ignore, and it is also a point that merchants and people who pay taxes according to law cannot ignore.

From the perspective of the target of the tooth tax, its scope is limited to the tooth industry and does not include vendors. For example, the same fruit and produce, if it is self-buying and self-selling, rather than acting as an intermediary broker, it should pay business tax, not be forced to pay tooth tax. This is not only based on the literal meaning, it should be the case. According to the Business Tax Law and the General Outline for the Collection of Business Tax, it is also a necessary conclusion.

However, the so-called tooth tax in Tianjin is very different from this. Without discussing others, just taking the Tianjin Fresh Goods Tooth Tax Regulations related to the association as an example, its tax collection method is: "At the beginning of the goods entering the market, according to the usual practice, the market price is estimated in advance, and the tax is paid first, and the pass is issued" (quoted from the Tianjin Municipal Government's reply to the Hebei Provincial Government). Once it lands, tax must be collected. This is clearly the nature of the old landing tax. As for its method of issuing tax bills and setting up checkpoints, the Tianjin Municipal Government also stated in its reply to the Hebei Provincial Government that "All collection points within the city can consider the local situation and set up checkpoints at any time to facilitate collection and avoid theft and leakage." The setting up of checkpoints for the tooth tax is a shocking thing for merchants, but the Tianjin authorities consider it a natural measure. Hebei is known as a province that has already complied with the order to abolish likin. It is difficult to understand why the official documents have such wording. (Omission)

Shanghai merchants, due to disputes over tax laws in Tianjin, resulted in the seizure and auction of fresh fruit shipped from Shanghai to Tianjin in February of this year by the tooth tax contractors there. The point of contention is that Tianjin's collection points only have two locations, namely Xihe and Yuhe. Those within the area are mostly tooth industries and have the obligation to pay commissions and taxes. However, goods shipped from Shanghai to Tianjin Haihe are either in transit or are self-sold and have no obligation to pay tooth tax. The contractors, however, want to collect as much as possible, forcibly taking and plundering. The association dispatched representatives to Tianjin to negotiate with the tax authorities. After mediation, a method was agreed upon on April 14. For fresh goods coming from the south and going to the north, warehouses and merchants with similar properties to the tooth industry should pay taxes according to regulations, paying cash temporarily. Vendors should keep accounts temporarily, and the money should be deposited in designated banks. In the future, they will petition the central government to determine whether vendors who are not tooth industries should pay the tooth tax uniformly according to the law and then decide whether to return the deposits.

Since this matter is to be presented to the central government for a final resolution, the association summarizes the opinions of the members and requests the following:

(1) The tooth tax levied in Tianjin is a disguised likin, which hinders the general order to abolish likin and is fundamentally illegal. The central government should first issue a clear order to stop and thoroughly reform it.

(2) After the abolition of this disguised likin, in order to maintain local tax revenue, the original tooth industries and warehouses with similar tooth industry properties should be classified and re-levied business tax, while vendors who buy and sell themselves should be levied business tax according to the business tax collection regulations of various provinces and cities.

(3) If, after assessing the situation, it is temporarily impossible to re-levy business tax, the tooth tax should also be issued according to the general tooth tax practice, graded and posted.

(4) Vendors and tooth industries are two different natures after all. The tooth tax should be strictly defined in accordance with Chapter 2 of the Civil Code to clarify the business boundaries and avoid disputes.

The association requests that the above requests be forwarded to the central government for correction in accordance with the law, and personnel should be dispatched to lead the petition to Beijing.

It is found that the association's request is purely based on the current tax law and is a reasonable request. It is necessary to eliminate the malpractices similar to likin. It is reasonable to recommend Standing Committee member Lu Wenshao to carry the petition and go to petition. It is hoped that the central government will review it and handle it separately as requested by the association to maintain the tax law and comply with the general order to abolish likin. This is truly for the public convenience.

Rong Zongjing Discusses the Truth Behind the Decline in Flour Prices 150

The market value of flour is declining day by day, and the future of the flour industry is in dire straits. The Ministry of Industry sent Section Chief Liang Shangdong to Shanghai to investigate the reasons for the decline with flour merchants in order to provide relief. A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Rong Zongjing, a giant in the flour industry, yesterday morning to inquire about the reasons for the low flour prices and the relief methods. He answered in detail. The details are recorded as follows:

Reasons for the Decline in Value 151

The recent decline in the value of flour is unprecedented in decades. The widely circulated reason is that there is a backlog of unsold goods, but this is not accurate. There is no backlog of unsold flour in various markets. The real reasons for the decline in value are: 1. The reduction in sales; 2. The low price of wheat.

The main sales market for flour has always been the three northeastern provinces. Before the three provinces were occupied by the Japanese, more than 12 million bags were shipped from Shanghai and Tianjin each year. Now, they have all been seized by Japanese merchants. According to reliable surveys, Japanese flour shipments to the Northeast reach more than 1 million bags per month. Therefore, the good flour market has been completely seized by Japanese merchants. The low price of wheat can reduce the cost of flour, but because sales are sluggish, the value of flour is declining even more.

The Situation of Reduced Production in Flour Mills 152

Flour mills in various places have reduced production due to stagnant sales. Taking Shanghai as an example, it used to be able to produce more than 60,000 bags of flour per day, but now they have all reduced production. Although the number of reductions varies from factory to factory, the average reduction is about 60%. The decline in the flour market can be seen from this. The high cost of transportation in the interior and the inability to abolish excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies are also major reasons for the decline of the entire flour industry. Because transportation costs are high, the difference between flour prices and wheat prices is too great, and people in the interior make their own flour, which invisibly reduces sales.

Relief Measures for the Decline 153

Rong believes that it is necessary to immediately find ways to alleviate the decline in the flour industry. Relief measures cannot be effective with empty words. The Ministry of Industry has no financial resources to provide effective relief due to the emptiness of the national treasury. Therefore, I believe that the current relief measures are: (1) Reduce inland transportation costs and abolish various miscellaneous levies (the transportation costs of Australian flour and Canadian flour to China are lower than those from Shanghai to Shandong); (2) Reduce the interest rates on loans to relieve the difficulties of merchants, but this is not easy to do.

167th Joint Meeting of the Executive and Supervisory Committees of the Lawyers Association 155

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its 167th joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees at its office on La Fayette Road, Rue Belles Road, in the French Concession at 7 p.m. last night. The committee members present were Shen Junru, Wu Zhengxiao, Yang Zhihao, Zhu Fuju, Mao Yun, Ma Junshuo, Hu Jue, Li Ming, Zhou Xiaoan, Chen Zhigao, Guo Shouyi, Zhang Zhengxue, Wang Weizhen, Yan Yinwu, etc., a total of fourteen people. (A) Reporting Items:

(1) The Ministry of Justice approved the request to order the prosecutor of the Shanghai District Court to lift the ban on lawyers meeting with unindicted detainees. It should not be discussed. Decision: Inform all members.

(5) The Lawyers Association notified that the revision of the articles of association was due to the failure of the meeting. Decision: Copy the original letter and forward it to the Hangzhou County Lawyers Association. After inquiring about the facts, it will be reviewed again.

(7) A citizen reported that Zhou Shixun had established a personal office and there was a risk of soliciting lawsuits. Please ban it. Decision: Send a letter to Zhou Shixun to warn him, limit him to revoke this type of advertisement with the nature of soliciting lawsuits within three days of receiving the letter, and reply immediately.

(8) Lawyers Wu Qi, Zhang Mingzhen, Zhang Yifan, and Chen Kecheng applied to join the association. Decision: Approved. The meeting adjourned at about 10 o'clock.

The development of China's radio industry has progressed rapidly in recent years, and the number of ships equipped with radio equipment has increased even more. Under the Pretext of Purchasing Stock Exchange Licenses, They Set Up a Guangdong Fan-Tan Gambling Scheme to Swindle Money: Chen Songtao Lost a Huge Sum of Money When the Transaction Failed, Was Arrested in Front of the Hotel and Beaten Severely, Suffering Injuries -- The World Is Dangerous and There Are Traps Everywhere -- 159

Xu Zhongfu (originally named Xu Shisun, also known as Shaoxi), a habitual gambling scammer who specializes in setting up gambling schemes to defraud money, was sentenced to six months in prison in the Public Concession for committing a crime in his early years. Unexpectedly, after being released, he was still incorrigible and colluded with gangs to defraud as before. There are many victims.

In the winter of the year before last, Chen Songtao, a broker from Sichuan Road Securities and Commodities Exchange, a Ningbo native (26 years old, formerly residing at 316 Sapose Road, later moved to 15 Green Yang Village, Connaught Road) intended to sell his broker's license at a price because he had no intention of engaging in speculative business. Xu saw the advertisement and thought it was an opportunity not to be missed. He immediately wrote to Chen, falsely claiming that someone wanted to buy the license, and invited Chen to Xu's house at 6 Xinle Lane, South Chengdu Road to discuss the matter face-to-face. After receiving the letter, Chen thought that Xu was the real buyer, so he went there on January 17 of last year. The two met and felt like they had met late.

At this time, Xu introduced his accomplices Dai Deru and Zhang Tieshan to Chen, and after talking, they felt more and more speculative. Afterwards, they met every day and became closer and closer. One day, as the four were sitting and chatting, a young man with a smoky face, about 30 years old, wearing beautiful clothes, behaving extravagantly, speaking with a Beijing accent, and carrying a leather bag, suddenly came in. When he entered the door, he pretended not to know Xu and Zhang, pretending to have come to Xu's house to fulfill an appointment with someone surnamed Dai. When Dai saw the young man arrive, he first pretended to introduce him to Xu, Zhang, Chen, etc., saying that the young man's name was Xu Jinqing (that is, Xu Sanyuan, who is actually Xu Zhongfu's younger brother), the descendant of a wealthy Qingdao merchant. Recently, because the chairman of Shandong Province, Han Fuqu, wanted to force him to donate money to purchase military supplies, he secretly smuggled a huge amount of family property to Shanghai, etc. After a short talk, the young man left.

Then Dai described the young man's background in detail, saying that the young man liked to gamble on Guangdong-style Fan Tan. At this time, Xu suggested to Zhang and Dai that he (referring to Xu) had a sure-win method of Fan Tan, which could make the young man hooked. In a short time, we (Xu called himself) can become rich overnight, etc. At this time, everyone tried their best to persuade Chen to join. Although Chen declined repeatedly, he finally agreed to the request because he could not refuse. However, as a result, Chen was defrauded of a huge sum of 3,500 yuan. At that time, Chen was still in the dark and had no doubts. He still associated closely with Xu and others, hoping that the broker's license would eventually be sold formally.

Unexpectedly, after Xu and others defrauded Chen of a huge sum of money, they gradually distanced themselves from Chen, and then there was no news. At this point, Chen recalled the past and suddenly realized that he had been deceived by these people. He was about to negotiate with them, but Xu had heard the news and first moved to No. 86 in a secluded alley opposite the Dian Dang next to the Mali Shi Vegetable Market on Dagu Road, then moved to No. 127, No. 38 Meibaige Road, and finally moved to No. 126, No. 727 Gordon Road, etc. But Chen had discovered all of them. After repeated negotiations, there was no result.

Chen then reported to the Gordon Road Police Station and Labor Sheng, the district chief of District A, who ordered that if they were seen in the future, they could be arrested. At 5:30 p.m. the day before yesterday, Chen Songtao, Zhang Lianqing, and friends Gu Zhuqing and Pan Hairu were in a car, passing by the entrance of the Shenzhou Hotel on Zhejiang Road, when they saw Xu Jinqing standing at the entrance. They got out of the car and grabbed him. Xu Jinqing claimed that this matter was done by Xu Zhongfu, and he was now in room 331 of the hotel. They might as well go upstairs to negotiate. Chen then followed him upstairs. Unexpectedly, the two Xus beat Chen severely, causing injuries to his waist and eyes. At that time, Hua Detective Li Wenbin of the General Patrol Room happened to pass by and heard about the incident. He immediately called the Old Gate Police Station and ordered detective Yang Guanying and a Western detective to come and bring everyone to the police station. Chen vomited blood three times in the police station and was sent to Renji Hospital for examination and confirmed that the injuries were real.

Because the two Xus had definite residences, they were not detained. The First Special Court issued a summons, and the two Xus were summoned to court yesterday morning. Police Lawyer Qian Xunjiu prosecuted according to Article 293, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law and requested that they be punished according to the law. Chen Songtao then submitted a report on the above-mentioned process, and Pan Hairu testified that Xu Zhongfu and Xu Jinqing did beat Chen. Chen Songtao also hired lawyer Yuan Yang'an to file a civil lawsuit, requesting compensation for damages of 500 yuan.

When questioned, the defendant denied beating Chen, saying that he was actually beaten by Chen and others at the time and had injuries to be examined. He also hired lawyer Wen Chao to defend him. Judge Deng Baosun reviewed the confessions and announced in court that Xu Zhongfu and Xu Jinqing were jointly found guilty of injuring the body of another person and were each fined 200 yuan and compensated the plaintiff for medical expenses of 30 yuan.

However, it is heard that the plaintiff Chen Songtao was extremely indignant after this strange humiliation. Although the injury aspect has been concluded, he still wants to continue to accuse Xu et al. of fraudulently obtaining money.

The Stranded Emei Steamer Escapes Danger After Years of Stranding – Costs a Staggering 120,000 Yuan – Finally Freed by Rising Waters 164

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Emei steamer, which ran aground upstream of Fuzhou in June of last year, has been under rescue and towing operations for ten months, costing a staggering 120,000 yuan. It was only yesterday that the shipowner, Ji Qingrong, telegraphed that the Emei steamer had escaped danger on the morning of the 9th due to rising waters and is now going to Yichang for repairs before returning to Shanghai for major repairs at the shipyard. The details are as follows:

Ten Months Aground 165

In June of last year, the Emei steamer ran aground on Huatanzi reef, upstream of Fuzhou. The hull was stranded on the reef, and the bottom of the first two or three compartments were all cracked. Because the company believed the ship, which cost 400,000 taels to build, was in excellent condition, it decided to rescue it. At that time, a Westerner named Pitotchen was entrusted to carry out the salvage. Later, the chief captain, Shen Jiyun, was sent to find a way to repair the holes in the ship. Just as they were about to tow it into the water, the upstream river water receded greatly, and the entire superstructure of the ship was destroyed, resulting in a loss of all efforts. After the water receded, the Emei was suspended high on the reef, a dozen feet away from the river, until today, a period of ten months.

Cost of 120,000 166

During these ten months, rescue work has been continuous, with costs reaching 120,000 yuan. Of this, Pitotchen alone spent more than 60,000 yuan. This year, in preparation for the great rise in the spring waters of the Sichuan River, it was towed out by hiring a large number of workers and purchasing a large amount of dynamite. First, the reef under the bottom of the Emei was blasted and removed in February, and then they waited for the time to tow it. The ship was insured for 130,000 yuan, and all rescue costs, in addition to a portion allocated by the company, were paid by the insurance company. Today, the final cost of 6,000 yuan must be remitted to the ship for the shipowner to pay.

Ship Escapes Danger on the 9th 167

Recently, the water level of the upper reaches of the Yangtze River has risen sharply. At 3:00 AM on the 9th, the Emei steamer floated out of the pile of rocks on its own during the rising water. At that time, the water in the upper reaches was extremely turbulent, and all the wire ropes attached to the Emei were broken by the water. This shows how urgent the situation was. Yesterday, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company received a telegram from shipowner Ji, stating that the Emei had escaped danger at 3:00 AM (on the 9th). All fourteen steel wire ropes on the ship were broken, and the bottom of the ship was slightly damaged. They have urgently telegraphed to Yichang to hire river-going ships to immediately sail to Yichang for preliminary repairs. Upon receiving the report, the company also ordered the newly appointed Deputy Captain Li to take a riverboat to Yichang to take office immediately.

Major Repairs in Shanghai After Arrival 168

The company now plans to have the ship slightly repaired in Yichang, and then order the shipowner to sail it to Shanghai for major repairs at the shipyard. Last year, the company originally planned to have the Emei converted to a special express train on the Jinghan Railway, but the accident caused this plan to be shelved. Now, the company intends to have it sail on the Sichuan River after it is repaired, and there is no intention to operate a special express train on the Jinghan Railway for the time being. Regarding the damage to the cargo on the ship, the passengers have already filed claims with the insurance companies. However, one foreign insurance company refused to pay, and the case is being litigated in the Sichuan court. Because it does not concern the company, they will not intervene.

Qian Shaofeng Kills His Father's Enemy and Willingly Goes to Prison – Yesterday Applies to Withdraw Appeal – Only Asks to Be Imprisoned Without Shackles 169

Qian Shaofeng, also known as Peihao, a young student from An'nan County, Guizhou Province, is twenty-one years old this year. He was studying in Shanghai last year and resided at No. 13 Yuanchang Lane, Hualong Road, in the French Concession. His father, Qian Bin, had served as the director of the Finance Bureau in his hometown. Four years ago, he was kidnapped and killed after failing to be extorted. At that time, Qian had just been married and heard rumors that he was also in danger. He fled alone and studied in Shanghai, Hankou, Beijing, Tianjin, and other places before returning to Shanghai, always harboring the ambition to avenge his father. In October of last year, he encountered his father's killer, He Zunfu, a fellow villager (who had served as the magistrate of An'nan County), residing in the Datong Apartment on Beile Road in Shanghai. He then hid a knife day and night, following He. On the evening of the 15th of that month, He went to the Huangjin Grand Theater to watch a movie, and Qian also bought a ticket to enter the venue to assassinate his enemy. At that time, He was injured and shouted wildly. Qian was unable to escape and was arrested by the detectives and sent to the Second Special Court for interrogation and detention. Later, He died of his injuries. The police changed the charges against Qian to murder and filed a lawsuit. The Second Special Court transferred the documents to the An'nan County Government of Guizhou to verify that Qian's father had indeed been killed. Considering that Qian was motivated by righteous indignation, he was sentenced to seven years in prison. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Qian expressed dissatisfaction with the original sentence as being too heavy and appealed to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court, requesting a reduction of the sentence. The Higher Court, based on the petition, concluded the investigation. The trial was held the day before yesterday by Judge Guo Dechang, together with Assessors Sun Honglin and Fan Peien, and the prosecutor. The appellant still retained lawyer Qian Shusheng to defend him. The judge asked the appellant Qian Shaofeng about the reasons for the appeal and explained the advantages and disadvantages of the appeal to him, instructing Qian to think carefully about whether to proceed or stop. Qian was moved by the words and applied to withdraw the appeal in court, requesting that the court not impose shackles during imprisonment and that he be willing to serve his sentence peacefully. At that time, everyone in the audience was moved by Qian's words and admired his ambition to avenge his father. As a result, the court instructed that the prison be notified when the sentence was executed and ordered him to be returned to the detention center to await imprisonment.

Two Police Officers Solicit Bribes – Red Pill Peddler Tries Everywhere to Raise Money But Fails to Satisfy Their Greed – The Police Officers Immediately Turn Hostile and Send the Opium Offender to the Police Station – After the Incident, the Police Officers and the Opium Offender Are Prosecuted Together 170

Bian Songlin, a native of Yangzhou, residing at No. 75 Baoxing Lane, Dongxin Bridge Street, French Concession, is thirty-three years old this year. He used to work in a yarn factory, but has been unemployed recently. Because he is addicted to opium, he makes a living by selling red pills. At about 8:00 AM on the 29th of last month, he hid four bags of red pills (totaling 4,000 pills, worth more than 30 yuan) in a handbag and, together with Feng Jinsheng (age 44, from Wuxi), a tailor, planned to transport them to the mainland for sale. When they passed the iron gate at the intersection of Minquan Road and Xinqiao Street in the French Concession, Ni Lianxue (age 31, from Jiangbei), a Chinese policeman of the French Concession Police Station, saw that Bian and others looked flustered and suspicious. He stopped them for inspection. Bian begged for help to get through. The policeman took Bian and Feng, along with the red pills in the handbag, to the nearby Yuanshang Lane and colluded with Liu Lianyuan (age 45, from Ningbo), the gatekeeper of No. 762 Lane, to extort 40 yuan from Bian. Bian agreed to give 20 yuan, but the policeman refused. After the police officer Xie persuaded him, Bian agreed to pay 30 yuan. However, Bian had no money on him and had to go home to find a way. The policeman ordered Bian's companion, Feng Jinsheng, to guard the handbag there and ordered the policeman Liu to accompany Bian home to get the money. Liu waited at Bian's house for about half an hour and, unable to wait any longer, returned to Yuanshang Lane first, instructing Bian to find a way quickly. Bian borrowed and pawned items everywhere and, after three hours of delay, managed to raise only 17 yuan. He entrusted Lu Qiaogen (age 32, from Wuxi), Feng Jinsheng's nephew, to deliver the money to Yuanshang Lane. The two policemen, Ni and Liu, refused to accept it because the amount was too far off. They told him to find a way again. Lu returned the money to Bian Songlin. Bian then pawned 30 yuan, making a total of 20 yuan, and ordered Lu to send it again. At that time, it was already 11:45 AM. Policeman Ni, seeing that the time difference was only fifteen minutes and Bian's money could not be collected, immediately turned hostile and took Feng, Lu, and the handbag containing the red pills to the police station, reporting to the police chief that Bian Songlin had escaped. The police chief interrogated Feng and Lu about Bian's address and sent detectives to arrest Bian, confiscating an opium pipe from his home. The next day, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the Second Special District Court and charged with Article 13 of the Opium Prohibition Law, requesting that the defendants be detained for further investigation. Later, the Western detective chief of the police station, Peng Shitian, ordered Bian and the other three to be interrogated. Bian confessed that the two policemen, Ni and Liu, had colluded to extort 30 yuan and, failing to do so, had been arrested and sent to the police station. The detective chief then summoned the two policemen, Ni and Liu, to the case for questioning. Ni denied it outright, while Liu confessed everything. The Western detective chief, seeing that the case was clear, reported to the chief patrol and dismissed the two policemen, taking them into custody together. Yesterday, they were also sent to the First Criminal Division of the Second Special Court, presided over by Judge Wang Gangxu. The police lawyer, Yuan Jiahong, stated the facts of the case, charging Bian, Feng, and Lu with Article 13 of the Opium Prohibition Law and charging Ni and Liu with Article 129 of the Criminal Law for dereliction of duty and soliciting bribes, and submitted the red pills, opium pipes, and pawned clothes, gold rings, and pawn tickets to the court. After the court separately interrogated the defendants, under the defense of the lawyers retained by the defendants, the court announced the end of the debate and adjourned the hearing for sentencing. The defendants were returned to custody.

The *Da Mei Evening News* reports that, according to news this morning (the 10th), the Human-Powered Vehicle Management Office is currently drafting a concrete plan to issue licenses to rickshaw pullers, based on Article 7 of the Human-Powered Vehicle Committee's report. The first step is to verify the physical fitness of approximately 55,000 rickshaw pullers, based on four pullers per vehicle and one puller per privately owned vehicle. It is said that at the beginning, the physical examination will not be very strict, and only those whose physical fitness is clearly unsuitable will be refused a license. After the initial work of issuing licenses is completed, the office will gradually tighten the requirements and proceed with the other articles of the report. It will pay particular attention to the fact that the rental fee for each vehicle for 24 hours should not exceed 80 cents, as this article has been adopted by the Public Works Department and has the force of law. However, it remains to be seen whether the rickshaw companies will comply.

Can it be charged according to the fourteenth category of fennel seeds in the agricultural product category? We hereby telegraph for verification and compliance." Its value is slightly equal to that of fennel seeds and should be charged according to the fourteenth category of fennel seeds in the agricultural product category. Amount of Cargo 177

The Jinglong steamer was originally named the Huaxing steamer. It was mortgaged and advanced by Mr. Yu to start his own line. The hull is 1,600 tons and was originally built in the UK more than 20 years ago. It now runs along the Xiamen-Guangdong route.
