Repeated Telegrams 179

After the manager of Dihua Shipping Agency in Xiamen sent a telegram reporting the accident, there were no further telegrams to Shanghai. The company waited until 2:00 PM yesterday without receiving a word. The Shanghai company sent another urgent telegram to inquire, stating, "We have understood the previous telegram. How is the ship? Can the cargo be salvaged? Please reply quickly." After this telegram was sent, there was still no reply. They then sent another urgent telegram, stating,

Dihua Shipping Agency, transfer to Jinglong, Chuán hé Cái, the insurance companies are urging urgently. What do you want to do to handle the aftermath? If it can be repaired, please come to Xiamen with the insurance company personnel. Please reply immediately to clarify the truth. Did you know about the two telegrams yesterday? Why haven't you replied? Anxiously.

Aftermath Measures 180

The Jinglong steamer's hull is insured for 60,000 yuan. Yesterday, the insurance companies were urging Hengkang Jinglong about the extent of the grounding. It was not until 5:30 PM that they received a telegram from Xiamen stating that the Jinglong steamer's hull was stranded on the rocks. The Xiamen office has agreed with the customs to send a ship to the side of the Jinglong to unload the cargo on deck and temporarily store it in the Shanghai Customs warehouse when the tide rises. They are also consulting with the Xiamen Haichuan Dockyard to send a ship to the accident site for rescue. The required expenses will be paid by the customs and then invoiced. The company has forwarded this telegram to the insurance company and will go with the insurance company personnel after the insurance company agrees to send personnel.

Cause of Shipowner's Death 181

Regarding the suicide of the shipowner, Russian Boyike, people in the company said that the shipowner was very responsible after taking office and never delayed the schedule. Although there is no detailed report on the suicide this time, it was probably caused by a sense of responsibility. He believed that the grounding was his fault, which led to the thought of suicide. All 56 crew members and 28 comprador personnel on board have been rescued and are currently in Xiamen.

The Guangzhao Upper Shelf Company Ren De Tang Case is Settled – The Defendant is Willing to Submit Books and Records for Review – A Settlement Record is Drafted in Court 182

Chen Enbao and Li Jiafu, former members of the Guangzhao Upper Shelf Company Ren De Tang, were accused of controlling the company's affairs and embezzling public funds, which was reported to the Social Bureau. The bureau ordered the company to reorganize and instructed Lu Bingjie to take over the company's affairs and funds for sorting. However, Chen, Li, and others hid the accounts and refused to hand them over, preventing Lu from proceeding. More than 190 fellow merchants of the company commissioned Lu Bingjie to retain a lawyer to sue Li Jiafu, the former chairman of the executive committee, Chen Enbao, the chairman of the supervisory committee, Qiu Shen, the chief of the general affairs section, and Li Jianfang and Mo Zhuonan, the accountants, for controlling public funds and hiding accounts. The summons from the First Special District Court has been reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that there are many accusations against Li and others, such as (1) the case of Li Shengsun, the company's accountant, who embezzled 8,000 yuan in ticket money and rent. It is suspected that the five defendants, Li and Chen, colluded in the wrongdoing. (2) Qiu Jie, representing the company, applied to the Land Bureau for a land certificate. The various expenses required should not exceed 2,000 yuan, but the *Credit Record* shows a total of 5,000 yuan spent on gifts, etc. (3) There are as many as 13 cases of falsifying membership lists with Chen Zhong's guarantee or charging fees. (4) Falsifying membership certificates and fraudulently receiving relief funds. It has been found that Huang Tian and Lu Yi were indeed instructed by others. The two have been sentenced by the court in previous years. (5) Arbitrarily reducing the price of the company's property, seeking private gain, disregarding public interest. The proceeds of the sale, 382,000 yuan, have not been disclosed in detail to this day. (6) According to the Ren De Tang's articles of association, monthly income and expenditure accounts should be printed in the *Credit Record* and distributed to fellow merchants to ensure credibility, but since June of last year, it has been almost a year, and this *Credit Record* has been delayed in printing, the accounts are muddled, and they dare not publish them, which is obvious. (7) According to the Trade Union Accounting Regulations, a final settlement statement and a balance sheet of assets and liabilities should be prepared at the end of the year, and an inventory table should be prepared at each settlement period. However, the defendants have not complied with the above matters. (8) According to the Trade Union Regulations, more than one-tenth of the members may request to send representatives to check the union's property. The plaintiff now has a collection of 192 members, which exceeds one-third of all members, to liquidate the accounts with the defendants, which is legal and should order the defendants to hand over all account books, forms, and receipts for detailed verification. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao Wanxuan continued the hearing. The plaintiff's attorney presented the Ren De Tang's membership list and the membership receipt stamped by the defendant Li Jiafu to prove the plaintiff's membership qualification. Then, the defendant's representative lawyer, Chen Zhongyin, defended each of the plaintiff's accusations, and finally stated that the purpose of the plaintiff's request was to review the accounts. The defendant was willing to provide the accounts currently in his possession to the members for review, but the documents submitted to the Social Bureau could not be reviewed from the defendant. Judge Qiao stated that the purpose of the plaintiff's lawsuit was to require account review, and since the defendant had clearly expressed his willingness to hand over the accounts for review, there was no need to litigate. Therefore, he persuaded both parties to settle and drafted a settlement record in court, stating that the defendant was willing to have the plaintiff send representatives with membership certificates or receipts to Ren De Tang to review the account books and receipts currently in his possession, but those submitted to the Social Bureau were not included. Both parties agreed, and the mediation was established. The lawyers for the plaintiff and defendant read each other's copies and agreed, and the parties who appeared in court signed and settled the case.

Resolution of the French Concession Rickshaw License Dispute 185

The French Concession Public Works Department caused a dispute by stopping the issuance of some rickshaw licenses. Since April, representatives of the Rickshaw Association, such as Zhang Huaiyang, have appealed to various parties. They received assistance from Du Yuesheng, Chairman of the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession, and committee member Tong Lizhang, who negotiated with the French authorities. The French authorities agreed to issue 100 additional relief licenses. Together with the remaining 36 licenses, a total of 136 licenses will be distributed by the French authorities in conjunction with the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession and the Rickshaw Trade Association. With the approval of the board of directors of the French Public Works Department, starting from the 7th, unemployed rickshaw pullers approved for relief must find a reputable guarantor within the French Concession and go to the Revenue Office of the French Public Works Department to obtain a license to operate. It is also stipulated that when donating and obtaining French licenses in June, the old licenses from May will be exchanged, and the old licenses registered in October of the previous year will be cancelled in the same number. It is also heard that no more requests for additional licenses will be accepted in the future.

Large-Scale National Products Company to be Established in Hangzhou 186

Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Construction Department of Zhejiang Province, and others, recognizing that Zhejiang Province lacks a large-scale national products company, which inevitably exposes the Zhejiang market to the dumping of foreign goods, have approved the request of Zhang Zilian and other national products manufacturers in the city to organize the Zhejiang National Products Company in Hangzhou. The proposal has been approved by the Zhejiang Provincial Government meeting, which has allocated vacant land behind the National Products Exhibition Hall to build a new building. The construction cost is 400,000 yuan. The plan is to build a four-story building with a basement and a platform for a commercial plaza. The first and second floors will be for commercial use, the third and fourth floors will be for hotels and food sections, the basement will be a warehouse, and the fifth floor (i.e., the open-air platform) will be for an amusement park. The business plan is divided into thirty-six departments. It is reported that Mr. Zhang has recently gone to Hangzhou to discuss the course of action with Director Zeng and Mao Zhongfu, Director of the National Products Exhibition Hall.

Shanghai Machine Industry Association Jointly Investigates Counterfeit Japanese Clocks: Yingfengtai Store Responds That It Is Selling on Consignment; Yesterday, a Letter Was Sent to the Clock Industry Association for Thorough Investigation 189

The Shanghai Machine-Made National Products Factory Association received a report from the Clock Industry Association stating that Yingfengtai Store in Jiru Lane, French Concession, was selling Japanese clocks with altered appearances, passing them off as national products, and deceiving customers. The 30th Standing Committee meeting of the Association decided to send Director-General Cheng Shouchong and General Affairs Manager He Pengcheng to investigate. The results confirmed the suspicion of Japanese goods and ordered the store to stop selling them. In order to thoroughly investigate the source of these Japanese clocks, a letter was sent to the Clock Industry Association yesterday, requesting them to send personnel to investigate the Minsheng Clock Factory to clarify the truth. The letter stated: "Respectfully, we previously received a letter from your association stating that Yingfengtai Store in Jiru Lane, French Concession, was using Japanese clock parts to assemble wooden cases, fabricating factory names, passing them off as national products, and selling them at low prices. This was discovered by colleagues, and the association managed to purchase a dozen clocks from the store, with invoices as proof. An examination revealed that the clocks had paper labels on the back stating 'Shanghai Minsheng Clock Factory National Product Alarm Clock,' and the inside of the clocks also had 'Completely National Product' paper labels. The clock faces were printed with 'Goose,' 'Lighthouse,' and 'Minsheng' trademarks, and included registration marks. After investigating various clock factories in Shanghai, no factory with the name Minsheng was found. An inspection of the parts confirmed that they were Japanese goods. This is undoubtedly a case of unscrupulous merchants altering the appearance of goods and passing them off as national products. At a time when our country's industry is in its infancy, this unexpected blow is causing the future of national products to be bleak. We have always admired your association as a leader in machine manufacturing, and we are sending this letter to you, along with representatives Zhuang Honggao, Li Weizhai, Wang Zhongzhen, and Hu Qiaqin, to explain everything in person. We urge you to uphold justice, not only for the benefit of our industry but also for the future of national products." Upon receiving this, the 30th Standing Committee meeting decided to investigate the matter. Director-General Cheng Shouchong and General Affairs Manager He Pengcheng were sent to investigate the store. According to the store, the Minsheng Clock Factory was not fabricated and had a signboard on Wuding Road that could be found. They were selling on consignment because of a friend's introduction and the presence of the words "National Product." The Association's investigators informed the store that the clocks were suspected of being Japanese goods and that they should stop selling them until it was confirmed that they were indeed national products, to avoid public anger. They were about to send a letter to report the findings when Yingfengtai sent a letter stating that recently the Association had sent Mr. Cheng and Mr. He to the store to investigate the alarm clocks produced by the Minsheng Clock Factory, based on a letter from the Clock and Watch Association alleging that the store was selling clocks from the Minsheng Factory, completely altering their appearance and passing them off as national products, and that no clock factory in Shanghai had the name Minsheng. The investigation results confirmed the suspicion of Japanese goods and ordered the store to stop selling them. The store responded that it was selling these clocks on consignment because of a friend's introduction. The clock faces had the words "Completely National Product," and the back of the clocks had the words "Shanghai Minsheng Clock Factory National Product Alarm Clock," so they believed they were national products and sold them on consignment. The factory address was indeed in the middle of Wuding Road, with an iron signboard at the intersection. Because the factory indicated that the products were national products, the store was deceived. The Association's opinion should be accepted, and the store will immediately return all remaining stock and will no longer sell them on consignment. A letter is being sent to inform you, hoping you will investigate and respond. The factory should be held fully responsible for passing off goods as national products. Therefore, a letter is being sent to inform you, hoping that you will investigate whether there is indeed a Minsheng Clock Factory in the middle of Wuding Road and clarify the truth.

Lu Peijun Suddenly Goes Missing; His Mother Asks Relatives and Friends to Search for Him 190

Lu Peijun, a 36-year-old native of Jiangyin who is engaged in the ink industry, lives with his elderly mother on Xinjiang Road, Zhabei. His wife, two sons, and a daughter are all in his hometown. Although young, Lu has started many businesses and enjoys a good reputation in the ink and oil industry. However, in recent years, his luck has turned bad, and his businesses have repeatedly failed, leading to mounting debts. On the 2nd of this month, Lu suddenly told his mother to sell all the belongings at home and return to Jiangyin as soon as possible. Lu's mother did not pay attention to this at first, but Lu disappeared without a trace that night and has not returned to this day. Lu's mother suddenly lost her beloved son and has been weeping day and night, and is now bedridden. At the same time, she has asked relatives and friends in various places to do their best to search for him.

Reading Q&A

Organizing Newspapers and Other Matters 195

Yesterday, we revealed the correspondence from Mr. Wang Lansheng, a reader of our newspaper for over twenty years, inquiring about how to read and organize newspapers, as well as the issue of Mr. Wang's son's education. Today, we will briefly respond to Mr. Wang and hope that Mr. Wang will give us his criticisms.

"How to read newspapers" is a question that Mr. Wang raised to us. Mr. Wang said, "Every day when the newspaper is delivered, I flip through it randomly without any plan, and in practice, I don't get any benefit from it." This accurately describes the common problem of reading newspapers for most people, but "flipping through randomly" cannot be immediately said to be "practically useless." Because the "newspaper" is not a "book" after all, and people who read newspapers do not have the same seriousness as when reading books. In the minds of ordinary people, the purpose of reading newspapers is not consciously realized. They read newspapers every day just like they drink tea, smoke, and chat with family and friends. Reading newspapers has become a part of modern people's lives, and they feel depressed and like they have lost something without it. Only then do they become aware of it. There are many people like this in the world. They are both concerned and not very concerned about the events happening around them, and they only casually receive some materials for "conversation aids." You say, is this kind of "flipping through randomly" useless? That's not necessarily true, but the knowledge gained is unsystematic.

As for people who read newspapers with a purpose, their attitude is naturally different from the above. Every day they open "four or five major newspapers," first look at the headlines, and quickly scan the entire newspaper, then carefully look at the parts they want to see. Some people pay special attention to market quotations and trade, some people specialize in studying international issues, some people pay attention to many conflicting phenomena in society, and some people like domestic politics. So each person uses their own purpose to constantly study the occurrence and development process of each type of event, and becomes a specialist in the study of a certain issue.

Reading newspapers should not only have a purpose, but also pay attention to the method of reading. Reading newspapers is not only for the eyes, but also requires your brain to distinguish the truth from falsehood in the news, and your hands to do the work of copying, cutting, and pasting. For example, taking the invasion declaration issued by Japan on April 17 as an example, if you feel that this issue is very interesting to you and you want to study it, you should not only read this type of news every day starting from April 17, but you also have to cut it out and paste it in a newspaper clipping book. Using this issue as the center, collect materials from all aspects, such as the attitudes of various countries towards the declaration, world public opinion, and the understanding and countermeasures of the Chinese government and the public on this situation, and compile them into research materials for one issue.

However, even if this step is done, the task of reading newspapers has not yet begun. Because the above is only about browsing news and collecting materials. The biggest task of reading newspapers is to analyze the situation, dissect the situation, and create a systematic understanding of each event. Regarding this point, it involves a person's purpose and academic ability. This is the most important step in reading newspapers.

As for you personally, we don't know what issue you are currently preparing to study. If you are preparing to study prices, you may wish to start collecting the prices of "clothing," "food," "housing," "fuel," and "miscellaneous items" in your area from now on. When the time comes, make a statistical analysis of the cost of living in your area. Isn't this the most valuable and interesting thing to do? This is what it means to "actually make some contribution." As for you saying that "if newspapers are not for browsing," "then I should start planning to study new books of the times from now on," we cannot agree with this. Because newspapers are living history, a record of human practical life, more important than any book. We very much agree that you should read more "new books of the times," but at the same time, you cannot go a day without reading newspapers.

How should twenty years of old newspapers be organized? We can only offer the following suggestions for your reference. Concrete methods cannot be determined for you, because we still do not know your "purpose" and what kind of organization you can achieve.

First, if you have ample time and can find like-minded people to work together on a certain issue, you may wish to divide the old newspapers from the past twenty years into categories such as international affairs of the past ten years, China's economy of the past twenty years, China's politics of the past twenty years, and the evolution of Chinese society of the past twenty years, and organize them separately. However, this is definitely not something that you alone or thirteen people can do. Even if you do, because the materials from a single Shen Bao are too limited after all, the conclusions reached will definitely not be very rich. However, if someone does it, even if it is not very successful, the collected materials will still have considerable value, without a doubt.

Second, if you cannot use it yourself and feel that "it is a pity to just let worms and rats gnaw on it," why not donate it to people who are capable of organizing these things, experts who are capable of using these materials? We think that for someone as enthusiastic about social causes as you, this is a more appropriate method when the first method cannot be implemented.

Third, is the "binding into volumes and storing them away" that you have already implemented. The best way to bind volumes is to bind one volume per month, with a summary of current events for each month attached, and to make a general summary each year. Elaborate monthly summaries should be decorated on the first page of each volume, and the general summary should be placed at the end of the twelfth volume. This will make it much easier to look up information when needed. This is the method of a collector.

Regarding the issue of your son's education after graduating from high school, we are very touched by your concern. You are truly a "father" standing in front of the times, making such serious plans for future generations. Society should also admire you for this. However, in our opinion, the many subjects you listed are both needed and not needed in today's Chinese society. Because Chinese society is currently undergoing major changes, all kinds of sciences are needed, but at the same time, due to social unrest, people with specialized knowledge are also unable to find their use. Engineers become magistrates, and agricultural and forestry experts become secretaries. What they have learned is not what they use, which is very common today. Regarding your son's career choice, we believe that it can be developed in any direction according to the economic strength of your family and his personal interests. But what should be paid the most attention to is: no matter what subject he studies, he must have considerable social science knowledge, and he must clearly recognize the way out for the Chinese masses, which is his own way out. Creating people who stand on top of the masses and apart from the welfare of the masses is not allowed by the times. Although we are very ashamed that we cannot give you a concrete answer on this point, we hope that the above shallow opinions can still be used as your reference! We also hope that you will give us more guidance in the future! (At the same time, we hope that Mr. Wang will refer to "How to Collect and Distinguish International News" published in this column on April 25). (End)

The book "How to Self-Study Social Sciences" was originally scheduled to be published on the 12th of this month, but due to busy printing and insufficient binding, it has been postponed for three days. We hope you will understand.

He attached great importance to the graduation entrance examination. The discussion lasted for two hours before the meeting adjourned. The following are the details of the resolved matters: (1) Should the content standards of the test questions for each subject be supplemented outside the regulations? (Resolution) Based on the Ministry-promulgated temporary curriculum standards for high schools, the minimum for graduation is (1). (2) Should the method of testing and the rules of the examination hall for each subject apply the methods decided upon in the previous session? (Resolution) Apply the methods decided upon in the previous session with amendments. (3) Assign responsibility for drafting standard answers. (Resolution) To be drafted separately by the test question drafting committee members for each subject. (4) Stipulate the dates for each subject. (Resolution) The entrance examinations will be held simultaneously in various districts from June 20th to June 23rd. The examination times for each subject are set as follows:

Date Time Subject

June 20th 8:00 AM to 11:00 AM Chinese

(5) The method of testing for each subject (Resolution) Party Principles, Chinese, Geography, Mathematics, Physics, Chemistry, and Biology will all use answers. The English test will use a combination of testing and answers. Choose one question for Chinese and one question for English, two questions for Q&A, and ten sentences. For the remaining subjects, choose four questions. Students may not do more than the required number of questions for each subject. This will be stated on the test paper. All test questions will be in classical Chinese, but scientific terms should be noted with their original names. The test committee members will draft twice the number of test questions and send them to the chairman for selection. For example, for the selection of four questions, 24 questions will be drafted and 12 questions will be selected. Students will select four questions from these. The same applies to the rest. Also, the rules for the Entrance Examination Committee, the rules for the Middle School Student Graduation Entrance Examination Hall, and the format for the certificate of admission to higher education were passed (all omitted). The second committee meeting is scheduled to be held at the Department of Education again at 3 PM on June 12th.

The Ministry of Education Submits to the League of Nations the 1934 Report on Education in China (II)

(II) Secondary Education 222

The three types of schools within the secondary education stage – middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools – have all undergone significant reforms this year.

Since the 1922 middle school system adopted the 3-3 system, with the first three years being junior high school and the last three years being senior high school, normal and vocational courses could be established in senior high schools. As a result, many independently established normal and vocational schools were merged into senior high schools. However, the effectiveness of this was not easily seen. Therefore, in 1933, the Ministry revised the secondary school system, stipulating that normal schools and vocational schools should be established separately, and promulgated and implemented the laws and regulations. The main points are briefly described as follows:

Middle schools are divided into junior and senior levels, with each level having a study period of three years. Junior high schools enroll elementary school graduates or those with equivalent academic ability. Senior high schools enroll junior high school graduates or those with equivalent academic ability.

Normal Schools: Normal schools enroll junior high school graduates with a study period of three years. Normal schools may establish special normal courses and kindergarten normal courses as appropriate. Special normal courses enroll senior high school graduates with a study period of one year. Kindergarten normal courses enroll junior high school graduates with a study period of two or three years. When there is an insufficient supply of teachers for local elementary schools, simple normal schools may be established, enrolling elementary school graduates for a four-year program, or a simple normal course may be attached to normal schools and public junior high schools, enrolling junior high school graduates for a study period of one year. All types of normal schools are generally public.

Vocational schools are divided into junior and senior levels. Junior vocational schools have a study period of one to three years, enrolling elementary school graduates and those with equivalent academic ability. Senior vocational schools have a study period of three years, enrolling junior high school graduates and those with equivalent academic ability. Vocational schools may, as needed, establish vocational supplementary schools or vocational supplementary classes, enrolling workers engaged in actual production, with varying study periods.

After the promulgation of these laws and regulations, in order to reduce the establishment of normal schools and vocational schools in ordinary middle schools, the Ministry of Education specially stipulated the standard for the distribution of secondary education funds in each province and city, and issued a notice for compliance. The standards are as follows: Vocational school funding shall not be less than 35 percent, normal school funding shall account for approximately 25 percent, and middle school funding shall account for approximately 40 percent.

If the distribution of secondary education funds in each province and city does not meet these standards, it should be gradually increased or decreased from 1934 to 1937 in order to comply.

In order to standardize the graduation level of students in various middle schools and improve teaching efficiency, the Ministry of Education formulated the Middle School Graduation Entrance Examination Regulations in 1932, stipulating that those who do not pass the entrance examination may not graduate. Since its implementation in various provinces and cities, it has been effective.

The general situation of various secondary schools from 1930 to 1931 is described below:

School Type Number of Schools Number of Students Amount of Funding

Junior High School 1,330 227,867 14,791,711

Middle School 554 179,081 20,540,210

Normal School 84 82,809 8,419,140

Vocational School 272 34,852 4,961,996

Total for Provinces and Cities 2,992 514,609 48,713,057

The quantities of all the above items have improved compared to the previous year.

(III) Elementary Education 223

Given China's vast territory and large population, the number of school-age children is naturally very large. Compulsory education is difficult to universalize in a short time. In order to promote compulsory education, the Ministry of Education promulgated the Outline of the First Phase Implementation of Compulsory Education Measures in 1932, with 1932 to 1935 as the first phase. During this period, each county and city in the country should designate experimental compulsory education zones in both urban and rural areas. All school-age children in the zones should receive compulsory education. The magistrates and chiefs of public security bureaus of each county have the responsibility to assist in the implementation of compulsory education, and those who fail to do so should be punished. At the same time, in order to help older out-of-school children, the Ministry also promulgated the Implementation Measures for Short-Term Compulsory Education, stipulating that short-term elementary schools or short-term elementary school classes should be established in various places, with the aim of literacy, enrolling out-of-school children aged 10 to 16 to receive short-term compulsory education. The study period is limited to one year.

Since the promulgation of these two measures, the educational administrative agencies in various provinces and cities have implemented them accordingly. It is expected that compulsory education will make considerable progress in a short period of time.

The general situation of elementary education from 1930 to 1931 is briefly described below:

Number of Schools 250,840

Number of Children 10,948,979

Amount of Annual Expenditure 89,416,977

The quantities of all the above items have increased compared to the previous year.

Among the provinces and cities, Shanxi Province has achieved the best results in implementing compulsory education. The number of children enrolled accounts for about 80 percent of the total number of school-age children. This is followed by Weihaiwei and Shanghai, which are also around 60 percent. Most other provinces and cities are between 30 and 40 percent.

In addition, the bandit-controlled provinces are also paying special attention to and making arrangements for restoring general education in the area.

Comparison of the Number of Schools, Students, and Funding for Various Secondary Schools Nationwide Since the Founding of the Republic 224

The Ministry of Education has compiled statistics on the number of schools, students, and funding for various secondary schools nationwide since the founding of the Republic. Here is a summary: (1) In the first year of the Republic, there were 500 middle schools and junior high schools, 253 normal schools, and 79 vocational schools (totaling 832 schools). The number of students was 59,971 in middle schools and junior high schools, 28,605 in normal schools, and 14,469 in vocational schools (totaling 103,045 students). The funding amounted to 3,296,672 yuan for middle schools and junior high schools, 2,040,387 yuan for normal schools, and 1,024,903 yuan for vocational schools (totaling 6,361,962 yuan). (2) In the fifth year of the Republic, there were 653 middle schools and junior high schools, 195 normal schools, and 84 vocational schools (totaling 932 schools). The number of students was 75,595 in middle schools and junior high schools, 24,959 in normal schools, and 10,524 in vocational schools (totaling 111,078 students). The funding amounted to 4,200,412 yuan for middle schools and junior high schools, 3,077,746 yuan for normal schools, and 1,296,901 yuan for vocational schools (totaling 8,575,059 yuan). (3) In the eleventh year of the Republic, there were 547 middle schools and junior high schools, 385 normal schools, and 164 vocational schools (totaling 1,096 schools). The number of students was 118,598 in middle schools and junior high schools, 43,846 in normal schools, and 20,360 in vocational schools (totaling 182,804 students). The funding amounted to 6,600,256 yuan for middle schools and junior high schools, 4,633,919 yuan for normal schools, and 2,790,005 yuan for vocational schools (totaling 14,024,180 yuan). (4) In the fourteenth year of the Republic, there were 687 middle schools and junior high schools, 301 normal schools, and 154 vocational schools (totaling 1,142 schools). The number of students was 129,978 in middle schools and junior high schools, 37,992 in normal schools, and 18,011 in vocational schools (totaling 185,981 students). The funding amounted to 9,540,228 yuan for middle schools and junior high schools, 4,368,262 yuan for normal schools, and 1,760,493 yuan for vocational schools (totaling 15,668,983 yuan). (5) In the nineteenth year of the Republic, there were 1,874 middle schools and junior high schools, 846 normal schools, and 272 vocational schools (totaling 2,992 schools). The number of students was 396,948 in middle schools and junior high schools, 82,809 in normal schools, and 34,852 in vocational schools (totaling 514,609 students). The funding amounted to 35,331,921 yuan for middle schools and junior high schools, 8,419,140 yuan for normal schools, and 4,961,996 yuan for vocational schools (totaling 48,713,027 yuan).

(Explanation) From the first year to the nineteenth year of the Republic, the number of middle schools and junior high schools has increased nearly fourfold, normal schools have increased by three and a half times, and vocational schools have also increased nearly fourfold. The number of students in middle schools and junior high schools has increased sevenfold, normal schools have increased threefold, and vocational schools have only increased by two and a half times. The annual expenditure on middle schools and junior high schools has increased tenfold, normal schools have increased by over fourfold, and vocational schools have also only increased by over fourfold. This indicates that the increase in ordinary middle schools is greater than that of normal schools and vocational schools. At a time when vocational education is being promoted, this kind of development is actually an abnormal development.

Special Report

A Glimpse of Japanese Education - Lecture by Du Gang, Notes by Qin Guangan and Chen Hekun 236

Mr. Du recently returned from Japan after inspecting children's education. At the invitation of Tao Guangchuan, principal of the Municipal Jingye Middle School, he gave a report in the school's auditorium on what he saw and heard. The following is a record of his lecture:

Japanese education is best managed at the elementary school level. Elementary school buildings are often large buildings costing hundreds of thousands or even one or two million yuan. On the one hand, their funding is sufficient, but on the other hand, it can also be seen that they attach great importance to elementary school education. They pay special attention to physical education. Almost every elementary school has a very large playground. The physical education teaching materials are mostly apparatus exercises and are very substantial, similar to our country in the 7th and 8th years of the Republic. Every elementary school student can perform very good skills. Their spirit is even more admirable. I remember that when we went to Kobe Kitano Elementary School, it was raining, but many elementary school students were barefoot and wearing only single layers of clothing, practicing diligently and tirelessly on the wet playground. Their physical education teaching materials are almost the same for boys and girls, and male teachers are employed in both boys' and girls' schools, and they are also responsible for the class teachers. This is because they firmly believe that all citizens must have strong physiques. To make the national body universally good, it cannot be entrusted solely to the school's physical education teachers, and the teachers themselves should also have a good spirit. This is their insightful view that physical education should be taken over by the class teachers.

Secondly, regarding Japanese elementary school teachers, almost all of them are graduates of the Normal School. At the same time, normal school graduates can only become elementary school teachers. After graduation, they are assigned by the government, and their salaries are about 45 yuan to 80 yuan per month for women, and 50 yuan to 150 yuan as the highest amount for men, based on the teaching performance of each teacher, with salary increases based on the assessment by the inspectors and principals. They attach great importance to the position of principal, and people without very rich experience and virtue cannot be appointed. When we visited Kobe, a 43-year-old principal told us that he was the youngest of the sixty or so elementary school principals in Kobe. Some were even elderly men in their sixties or seventies. This shows how much attention they pay to elementary school education. In terms of moral education in Japanese elementary schools, it is centered on the Emperor. Every elementary school student respects the Emperor, and every elementary school student worships figures who have contributed to the country. There are many shrines in society that display idols of these figures or display their achievements during their lifetime in the form of objects, texts, and pictures to inspire respect. In short, every elementary school student already has the concept of loyalty to the Emperor and patriotism, and the spirit of sacrificing for the country.

Japanese elementary school students have very good discipline. During class, in a school with thousands of students, no students can be seen outside the classroom. They like to wear uniforms, especially old uniforms, because this shows that they are in a higher grade and consider it an honor. At the same time, people in general society also have great respect for these elementary school students wearing old or torn uniforms. This concept is the same for middle school and university students. In terms of the curriculum of Japanese elementary school students, in addition to citizenship, which is the same as ours, there is also a self-cultivation class for training personal self-cultivation. In addition to lectures by teachers, they also have a practice room for practicing various rules of etiquette. Therefore, they have been trained in form and are very polite when they are elementary school students. In terms of equipment, as I said earlier, because funding is sufficient, all kinds of courses are naturally perfect. There are no special classrooms, such as drawing classrooms, handicraft classrooms, music classrooms, history classrooms, geography classrooms, and physics and chemistry classrooms. Their methods and spirit are all focused on practice. For example, in their elementary school handicrafts, the classroom is divided into metalworking, woodworking, lathe working, and sand casting workshops. In addition, they also have a local room, which displays real objects or charts of local products, businesses, customs, and folklore.

When we went to Japan this time, although they expressed a warm welcome on the surface, there were still many very important places that we could not see. Even if we saw them, it was just a fleeting glance, and we rarely had the opportunity to stop and look carefully. Therefore, what we saw was just a general outline.

Elementary schools are like this, and middle schools do not allow us to investigate in detail. I remember once visiting a chemical industrial school, and I only saw that the equipment inside was substantial and the various drugs were very abundant. Their mechanical industrial school is also very large in scale, and I think it can manufacture military supplies when necessary. The various works of the students are quite impressive, and the products are sold outside.

Spring and Autumn

Record of Fragrant Incense Fading 237

— Original by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Because these pouches have no prescribed style or color, you are free to sew them as you wish, according to your own ideas. So all sorts of ingenious styles and bright colors were adopted without limit. However, the function of these pouches was purely decorative; in fact, no one ever used them to hold anything.

As for the belt itself, it was woven with blue silk thread. The color was of course very striking. And to fasten this belt, as usual, there was a buckle. The styles of these buckles were also not prescribed, allowing the wearer to come up with various designs themselves. Thus, this buckle, like the pouch, became a good source of ostentation and showing off wealth. An unexpected, special buckle revealed his own wealth and power. The most common were gold, silver, or copper buckles, the style depending on the wearer's preference, and they were usually different. However, these silver and copper things were, after all, very ordinary materials, only used by lower-ranking officials who were limited by their financial resources. Qing Shan would absolutely not want them! His buckle was carved from the finest jade. My father also had such a buckle, the style was very exquisitely carved. Perhaps Qing Shan himself liked this style, or perhaps it was purely the skill of the jade craftsman, that cannot be known. But I can guarantee with certainty that a buckle like his was worth at least one thousand taels of treasury silver. At the current exchange rate, that would be over one thousand five hundred yuan in national currency. Qing Shan also wore a huge jade ring on his finger, its value probably not far from that of the buckle; so, adding it all up, the value of his entire outfit was at least five thousand taels of silver, equivalent to about seven thousand yuan in today's Chinese national currency. As for how many sets of such outfits he had, that was something no one else could know! A Minister of the Imperial Household had such rich and beautiful clothing, no one could say that he was unworthy. Although, in fact, he still had to rely on Li Lianying's every breath, often getting things to give him as gifts. (31)

Compromising with Ghosts 238

— Xun Zi

One day, in the courtroom lounge, I met Teacher Yuan Zhonglian. Teacher Yuan was a devout Buddhist and observed the precepts very strictly. He told me that he knew how to perform the Flame Mouth ceremony, which belongs to the esoteric sect of Buddhism and can transcend hungry ghosts. Mr. Yuan also told me an event to prove that ghosts exist.

Mr. Yuan said: After the January 28th Incident, in the Dachang area, a lady was possessed by a ghost. The ghost was originally a company commander of the 88th Division, who spoke pure Hangzhou Mandarin. Because in the underworld, he was cold and hungry, so he asked the lady's family to specifically request the Diamond Sutra. The family inquired everywhere and found that an old nun nearby had accumulated 8,000 volumes of the Diamond Sutra that she had recited, so they bought them all and burned them. The ghost company commander was overjoyed and said that not only he himself, but even the entire company of soldiers under his command, would be transcended!

Mr. Yuan's propagation of doctrine from a Buddhist standpoint is another matter. However, I had other thoughts when I heard it. The Chinese are truly worthy of being a peace-loving people, even compromising with ghosts and gods. When ghosts and gods cause trouble, all they want is some benefits, so they set out wine and food, light incense and candles, and invite the ghosts and gods to eat and drink. Finally, they burn a large pile of silver ingots to make the ghosts and gods satisfied and leave. Alas! The essence of Buddhism is actually to compromise with ghosts and gods!

Christianity is different. They treat demons without ceremony, wanting to expel them. If demons are not easy to get rid of, they fight them until they are victorious. Therefore, in Christian hymns, there are triumphant songs similar to victory songs. It turns out that Christianity is a worldly dharma, and Buddhism's transcendental dharma is fundamentally different!

However, the Chinese are a people who believe in Buddhism, so they specialize in compromise. This is the same as sending ghosts away with wine, food, incense, candles, and paper ingots, a manifestation of the compromising doctrine of "giving him whatever he wants"!

I advise the Chinese not to compromise with ghosts and gods in the future. They should still learn from Christianity and fight demons!

The Utilization of Scenic Spots 239

— Qian Zuizhu

The scenic spots of Suzhou are not utilized by the people of Suzhou, but are utilized by the Japanese. Their business methods are so pervasive that even Europeans and Americans have to retreat. The day before yesterday, I happened to accompany a few friends to play in Tianping Mountain. As soon as we entered Tongzi Gate, we saw two or three "semi-old guns" rushing up to act as "tour guides." With me, this "guide," by their side, they were naturally refused. But he was still unwilling to give up and followed up, saying, "Gentlemen, when you visit the mountains and rivers, do you want to bring some souvenirs back? I have excellent scenic photos here. Bring a few back to your residence, and it won't be a waste to come out and play once."

My friend was touched by him, so he stopped to look at the photos in his hand.

There was a stack of about a hundred photos. He specially picked out a set of Tianping Mountain photos, ten in total:

"Sir, these are the famous scenic spots of Tianping Mountain, ten in total, only five jiao (cents)."

"Do you have Tiger Hill?" my friend asked.

"Yes, yes," he picked out another set of twelve, "also only five jiao."

As a result, one yuan bought three sets, and my friend was extremely happy.

After playing, we passed by a Japanese shop, "Toyodo," and saw several "semi-old guns" walking out with a large bag of photos. Because we were going the same way, I chatted with them and asked about the origin of the photos: "The Japanese give us this kind of scenic photo, a set of one hundred, every day to hawk to tourists. After selling a set, they give us two yuan and five jiao, and if we don't sell them all, we return them. We poor friends have no capital to do business, and if we can earn eight jiao, who wouldn't want to do it, but you need an introduction."

My friend was very angry when he heard this and tore the photos in his hand in half.

Poetry of Xuan Yinlu

— Fu Gong

Walking in the Wilderness Early in the Morning 241

Desolate, my body is like an unmoored boat. I go where I intend, neither leaving nor staying. Coming here, I understand all the flavors of Jiangnan. Thank you, spring breeze, for being so gentle.

Spring Mud 242

Spring mud does not taint the fragrant skirt. It is left to correct the slanderous writings of moths. A moment of warmth still penetrates the bones. All around, criticisms arise because of it. When can I see the end of the cycle of the wheel? When can I trace the initial grievances and kindnesses back to the tooth marks? Cut off the tallest flowering magnolia branch. Snow-white skin and jade petals emulate the beauty of the lake.

Northeast Four Battalion Commanders 243

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Eighth: A Coincidence to Watch the Play, Lovesickness to Pick Up a Handkerchief, Diligent Questions About Illness, Misunderstanding in a Letter

He sat on the bed, feeling depressed all afternoon. By evening, he couldn't bear it any longer and secretly told Jiang about it. Jiang, by now, felt that her son-in-law's father was quite good. Moreover, their attitude towards marriage was to "marry a chicken, follow the chicken; marry a dog, follow the dog." Not to mention that they were very satisfied with their son-in-law, even if they weren't, they couldn't say a word about it to anyone. No matter what, they had to get that handkerchief back. She, like her daughter, tossed and turned in bed all night because of this. The next morning, she deliberately lingered at the door, watching. When she saw a maid from the Gan family come out, she smiled and said, "Aunt Wang, Happy New Year! Is your master at home?" Aunt Wang replied, "The old lady sends you her New Year's greetings. Our master has gone to the market, and the mistress is playing mahjong. No one is home. I'm taking something to the mistress." As she spoke, she held up a jade cigarette holder, smiled, and said, "Taking this to her." Jiang said, "Does your family have any taboos about entering the house? If not, I'll come to your house to see Second Master's illness." (Note: Common custom in some old families, from New Year's Day until the Lantern Festival, women are prohibited from entering the house.) Aunt Wang laughed, "Our mistress even goes to other people's houses to play mahjong, what taboos are there?" As she spoke, she left with a smile. Jiang hesitated at her own door for a while, then slowly walked towards the Gan family's door. After pacing around for a long time, the same Aunt Wang who had delivered the cigarette holder returned and asked her to go to Ji Zhi's room. Ji Zhi was staring out the window in a daze when he suddenly saw Jiang come in. This was unexpected. He quickly reached out from under the covers and made a few fist salutes towards her. Jiang entered the room, not looking at his face, but at his mattress. She stood in front of the bed and asked, "We were all fine when we came back from the theater. How did you become unwell?" Ji Zhi said, "Catching a cold is very easy. I don't deserve the Old Madam coming to see me." (382)

Miscellaneous Talk

About Yan Ziling's Fishing Platform 244

— Huo Xueming

I recently read Mr. Chen Shicheng's "Tour of Qililong" in this journal's Spring Outing Special. There was a passage in it: "The fishing platform towers on the mountainside, about two hundred feet above the water. How could one fish from there? Could it be that times have changed, and things are different now than in the past? If this platform were suitable for fishing, then the entire Hangzhou prefecture would be a marshland!"

After carefully considering Mr. Chen's meaning, I suspect that the fishing platform is too high. Yan Ziling could not have cast a line two hundred feet long in those days and caught a bass. This is truly like Yang Wanli's poem from the Song Dynasty: "Fishing stone three thousand feet high, what could one use as fishing line?" It has the same sense of doubt. Even the Yanling Chronicle says: "Yan Ziling's Fishing Platform, there is a stone by the mountain, called the Fishing Altar, facing east and west, over a hundred feet high, overlooking the Great River."

First, in various chronicles before the Song Dynasty, there is no mention of the fishing platform. In the Water Classic Commentary by Li Daoyuan of the Later Wei Dynasty, it only says: "Under Yanling Lai Mountain is a stone chamber, where Yan Ziling lived during the reign of Emperor Guangwu of the Han Dynasty. Below the mountain is a large rock, several tens of yards in circumference, bordering the Jiaoliu Pool, where Ling used to roam." Perhaps from this, someone fabricated the story of the sheepskin cloak by the swamp to describe Ziling's purity. Throughout history, reclusive scholars, such as Shun at Leize, Shangfu at the Wei River, and Zhuangzi observing fish on the Hao River, all used it as a metaphor for the tranquility of human nature. Therefore, it is fitting to say that Ziling fished. Xu Hun's "Below Yanling Terrace, the Tong River flows, how many can fish for bass?" Perhaps he was the first to praise fishing. However, we should know that even though Ziling lived in seclusion in the stone chamber, free from the burdens of military and state affairs, he would stroll to the Tong River when he was happy. But the place where he fished was the large rock at the foot of the mountain, as mentioned by Li Daoyuan! Not the stone pavilion on the mountain, more than a hundred feet above the water!

Second, upon further reading of the gazetteer, it says: "South of Tonglu County is Yan Ziling's fishing place. Today, there is a stone by the mountain, flat on top, where ten people can sit, overlooking the water; it is called Yanling Fishing Altar." The so-called Fishing Altar refers to a huge rock by the river, not a stone pavilion that has been far-fetched. Reading Tang Luo Binwang's imperial edict: "I arrived at Qilitan during the three dog days, this place is the mouth of the Xin'an River. There is Yan Ziling's Fishing Reef there." Here, it is further affirmed that when Yan Ziling farmed and fished in the Fuchun Mountains, there was only a fishing reef, not a fishing platform. The so-called reef is a huge rock by the river.

Third, we can be sure that the two stone pavilions on the summit of Mount Fuchun were definitely not built by Yan Ziling himself. He also did not need to build an altar and then fish; if we further examine the structure of the stone pavilions, they are not architecture from the Han Dynasty. We know that between the stone pavilions, the one on the east side has a plaque that reads "Noble Demeanor of a Thousand Years," which of course refers to Ziling; the one on the west side has a plaque that reads "Leaving a Thread of the Cauldron," which refers to Xie Ao. In fact, Ziling and Xie Ao would never praise themselves. These two pavilions are now equally dilapidated to the same extent. Therefore, I am certain that they were built at the same time. Moreover, in reality, there is no such long fishing line! As for why the stone pavilions are not built on the edge of the water or on the side of the mountain, but must be located high on the summit, there is also an explanation:

Respect for great personalities must be matched with a lofty position. The architecture of ancient Roman churches, with a sacred cross on the spire, is nothing more than wanting people to see this dignified form from afar and generate infinite feelings. Putting the fishing altar high in the clouds is also the same idea. We cannot say that Mr. Chen YingShi could ride a horse in the clouds just because we see his bronze statue by West Lake, right?

From this, we can draw a conclusion: the black rock among the thickets on the riverbank below Mount Fuchun, where fishing boats can be moored, is the place where Yan Ziling cast his line in those years. The stone pavilion on the summit is a building erected by later generations to commemorate Yan Ziling. Moreover, the character "altar" in Fishing Altar is defined in Shuowen as a place for sealing soil and offering sacrifices, containing the meaning of respecting ancestors and commemoration. Therefore, someone guessed that times have changed, worried that Ziling could not fish, and even suspected that Hangzhou prefecture would become a marshland, which is really unnecessary! The transformation from fishing reef to fishing altar, from fishing altar to the tall fishing platform, which is today's stone pavilion, is probably the only reason for the misunderstanding.

Having said that, I still hope that scholars will come up with more convincing evidence to explain when and by whom the existing fishing platform was built; then explaining this small doubt of the general public is not a boring act!

Commercial News

Finance: Silver Faction Has Signs of Internal Strife, Bid Prices Rebound to Three Yuan and a Half, US President Studies Silver Bill, Initial Setback, Foreign Exchange Tight, Central Bank Opens for Cash, Trend is Bullish 245

Yesterday, the gold market was stable due to conflicting news about the silver bill, a decline in forward silver prices, and a steadying of sentiment. Furthermore, due to settlement relations, the domestic market tightened, and the Central Bank actively opened for cash, making the market bullish. At the close, it rose further. Initially, overseas silver markets in the UK and US had surged, but forward silver prices on the Metals Exchange fell by six to eight and two-tenths of a penny. Exchange rates opened higher, narrowing the gap. London spot gold fell by two pence, US cotton fell by twelve pounds, and US wheat fell by half a point, causing sentiment to turn bullish. It was rumored that the White House had not fully confirmed everything about the silver bill. Spot prices opened at thirteen to fourteen yuan. Reuters reported that President Roosevelt's consideration of nationalizing silver was benevolent, and that the President was receptive to permissive and directive legislation on silver reserves. Although the President opposed confiscating silver coins in the same way as gold, he agreed that the government could buy silver bars. Pittman said that the silver legislative draft was progressing well and could be submitted to the President by the end of the week, causing prices to rise initially and then fall back to 1007 yuan. However, due to the tight foreign exchange market, the market remained stable. Later, banks actively settled their accounts, and the Central Bank vigorously intervened, gradually raising prices by more than ten yuan. The Associated Press reported that the President's support for silver as a reserve caused a setback. The domestic market hardened slightly. Although silver prices in the Seattle night market rose 0.25 and then fell 0.25, there was no significant impact. Later, the gold market fell slightly. The market was stable after opening due to the decline of silver prices in the Seattle night market by 0.125. It was rumored that the silver bill was delayed for discussion. However, Reuters corrected the report that silver prices in the night market in December had increased by 0.125, and prices initially rose and then fell slightly. Later, dealers counter-bargained, and banks were not short of supply. Exchange rates in the UK and US tightened consistently. The Bombay exchange rate fell by eight annas. The Central Bank opened for cash again, causing prices to rise rapidly, breaking through the 20-yuan mark. The Da Mei Evening News reported that the US President said there was no immediate need for silver legislation, and that the meeting with the silver faction would be held tomorrow. In addition, Senator Borah suddenly broke away from the silver faction, indicating signs of internal strife among silver advocates. The closing price was the most bullish. The price of red gold was 1028 yuan. The day's market conditions are recorded as follows:

The opening price in the morning was 1015 yuan, a rebound of 15 yuan and 30 cents compared to the previous close. Spot prices opened at 14 yuan. The initial selling price of near-term exchange rates was 1 shilling, 3 and 4375 pence for British exchange and 33 yuan and 0.0625 for US exchange. They then tightened. Silk and Tea: Jiangsu and Zhejiang Spring Silkworms Still Hold a Pessimistic View 260

Sultry Sudden Cold Thunderstorm Silkworm Ants All Start to Change

(Haining Discovers Silkworm Measles) Farmers in urban and rural areas, the local silkworms hatched early this year have suffered damage due to the cold and rainy weather. Improved species were bred to supplement them, but the silkworm ants in the early sleep still show little change due to the long period of rainy days. They began to eat leaves during the first sleep, but their development is still unsound. Now, the early batch has had its major sleep, and the late batch only ate leaves during the third sleep. Unexpectedly, in recent days, it started with hot and sultry weather, followed by sudden cold and thunderstorms, resulting in early silkworms spitting yellow pus, excreting black water, and smelling strangely after death. The loss of local silkworms is heavier, almost completely abandoned.

(Many Silkworms Rot and Die in Xinchang) In the Huangze area of Xinchang, many people raise improved silkworms, and many also breed local species. Due to continuous rain and cold weather, most of the local silkworms died stiffly in the second and third sleeps. The improved species also began to stagnate, losing their sleep. In the past two days, it was extremely hot and cold. The temperature differed by 30 to 40 degrees in two days, and there were also heavy thunderstorms, resulting in early silkworms in the third sleep all developing silkworm plague. Most of the local silkworms rotted and died. The infection was very rapid. Although isolation was added, the loss of silkworm ants was 30% to 40% per day.

(Danyang Young Silkworms Lose Sleep) Due to the cold weather in the four rural areas, the mulberry trees sprouted late, and the silkworm spread was later than usual. The ants were unevenly released. Although the improved species were fed with fresh mulberry during the first sleep, they showed little change despite the bad weather. The early batch had already completed two sleeps and was fully grown, and the late batch had also started eating leaves. In the past two days, it suddenly became hot and sultry. The next day, it was suddenly cold, and it rained like a pillar, causing the early silkworm ants to lie stiff and unable to get up, wandering in the curtain, and acting clumsily. The late batch had a sharp decrease in appetite, and the current situation is not good.
