Free Talk

Miscellaneous Notes on Hospitalization 264

— Xiao Long

(4) The Lamb on the Altar

If I were to name the biggest liars in the world, I would definitely say it's doctors. Doctors never tell patients the truth. When a patient is about to die, the doctor will still say to him: "Don't worry, you'll get better soon." They keep deceiving the patient until their last breath. Similarly, that doctor with a Hitler-like mustache also used the same trick on me. After a nurse covered my body with a thick quilt, the doctor took a syringe filled with anesthetic and said to me, "This is the greatest pain you will ever feel. After this, you won't feel any more pain." As he spoke, he inserted the needle into my throat to administer local anesthesia. I knew that the pain of the injection was limited, so I endured it contentedly, letting him inject both sides of my throat six times.

My throat gradually felt a little numb. After a while, several nurses prepared all the instruments, and the doctor first inserted those terrifying instruments into my throat.

I immediately realized that everything he had told me was a lie.

I struggled, but my hands and feet were restrained, completely like a lamb being slaughtered on the altar.

I saw blood splashing from my throat, splattering on the hands of the nurses and the doctor, on the quilt, and on the wall. I vaguely saw those terrifying instruments being exchanged among the doctor and several nurses under the light. The effectiveness of the anesthetic injection seemed minimal to me at that time because I still felt a lot of pain. I wanted to scream, but I couldn't because many things were blocking my mouth.

Although the doctor's speed of the surgery was commendable, said to be less than two minutes in total, it felt like two centuries had passed to me until the doctor took out the last forceps and said, "Okay!" only then did I feel like I had been released from the greatest torture.

At that time, if I had the right to kill someone, I think I would definitely raise a knife without hesitation and chop down on the doctor's head. Even though he patted my shoulder and said with a smile, "The surgery went very smoothly because you were able to handle it very well."

My nasal passages were full of blood, and my throat felt swollen. Breathing seemed to be blocked. Although the doctor kept telling me to open my mouth and breathe, I still felt suffocated and unable to breathe. I felt like I was about to die. I felt like I had completely experienced the sensation of being hanged before being strangled, and the pain of those dying people whose tracheas were clogged with phlegm.

It is said that people who commit suicide will definitely regret it in the moment before death. Unfortunately, regret is too late, and the result is only death. Therefore, I now think that if there is anyone who wants to commit suicide, in order to avoid irreparable regret, it is best to ask the doctor to operate on the tonsils first, to taste that kind of experience close to death. Fortunately, this is not real death, and there is no fear of regret. This will definitely stop him on the brink, turn back, and struggle harder on the road of life.

Being Earnest 265

— Lin Kemu

Egyptian culture has long been buried, and the pyramids stand alone. Standing in the middle of the desert, it makes people think of the grand and majestic past. Why were the pyramids built? It is because the ancient Egyptians were "earnest."

But the Chinese have a different attitude towards life, "The theater is a small world, and the world is a big theater." Everyone thinks of themselves as playing roles on stage, intentionally or unintentionally. Since they are acting in a play, of course, there is no such thing as being earnest. Everyone is just pretending, and it's all muddled. Isn't the horizontal scroll of the famous scholar Zheng Banqiao hanging everywhere? The text says: "It's rare to be muddled."

However, if being muddled is not innate but needs to be pretended, it also requires being earnest. Although Zheng Banqiao seems to be cynical, he is very earnest at heart. Otherwise, his paintings and calligraphy would never have such profound attainments. And what his art expresses is not muddled at all. In modern times, there are many disasters, and right and wrong arise. People's spirits are attacked everywhere. Because they are oppressed, they can only become decadent and not earnest.

It seems that only Buddhism advocates emptiness and silence, but the principle of Dependent Origination of the Mahayana is against those who take the appearance of emptiness and become greedy. Various faults arise in the ultimate emptiness, and it cannot be interpreted as being unearnest or a talisman for laziness. Just look at the hard work of many Buddhists, and you will know that their purpose is not to act in a play. The Five Hegemons and Seven Heroes are clowns, and it is true that only Sakyamuni, Jesus, and the Chinese Laozi, Zhuangzi, Shenzi, and Hanzi can play the role of clowns, but it is still a bit unsuitable.

How can the spirit of us Chinese be unearnest? Doctors do not forgive germs when diagnosing diseases, so that patients retain some diseases in their bodies. Political factions also do not show any mercy when attacking dissidents, only short of "whipping the grave". Small vendors who are arguing over the tip of an awl are more shrewd than Western accountants when it comes to being clear about every cent. Only national affairs are difficult to muddle through. With a strong enemy in front of us, we are not allowed to be earnest, so we have to give up. There are several ways to say that you are not earnest. One is to say to the oppressor that if you are beaten and unable to fight back, please don't be earnest. This is a cry for mercy. Although it is a failure, there is a chance of survival. One is to say to yourself that you have become a complete muddled insect and will never be cured. One is to say to the person you have defeated that it is a kind of anesthetic to make people feel at ease as slaves. Besides, many people are acting in a play, using counterfeit money, or specializing in the empty city trick, and they can't be earnest.

Perhaps an earnest life has too much suffering, but only this is the way to survive. The pyramids were not built casually.

New Shoal of Zigui 266

— Guo Mengte

Zigui County, formerly known as Guizhou, is located west of Yichang, only a hundred or so *li* by water, and there are steamers going up and down every day. Outsiders would surely think that the county's transportation is very convenient.

But that's not the case. Steamers going up to Sichuan and down to Yichang rarely stop in this county. This is because the area is right within the so-called Three Gorges, with high mountains, narrow gorges, steep river currents, and even more treacherous shoals.

During this season of low winter water, even the steamers with full horsepower that specialize in navigating the Sichuan River have to spend hundreds of dollars, hiring the local boat trackers of the shoal to shout, pull, and haul with all their might when passing the famous "New Shoal" of this county.

The New Shoal is probably named after a "Discharge Shoal" (洩灘) twenty *li* upstream to the west. Like other shoals, the New Shoal was formed naturally by the collapse of high mountains. In these months of low water, the rocks on the river surface jut out menacingly, causing the river flow to form a steep cliff more than ten feet high. All steamers going west must first throw the iron cable onto the south bank, have thousands of people pull on it, and then use the machinery at the front to winch it up. So,

"Heave-ho! Heave-ho! Heave! Heave! Heave!"

The number of people pulling the boat is countless! They climb up the rocks and jump down again; they crowd together and then disperse; there are men and women, very old men and very young children. Although the weather is very cold, many young men still wear only a torn blue jacket. Set off by the gray-white beach, they sometimes look like individual or rows of distant trees.

"Heave! Heave-ho! Heave!"

Their voices are very loud, harmonious, and rhythmic, sometimes a sound is prolonged for a long time, and sometimes a tone is repeated very quickly and urgently! Heave! Heave! Heave.

Unfortunately, this great and beautiful sound is always hindered by its environment and cannot be transmitted far to the world. The echo returning from the valley seems as if someone is imitating it in a very, very distant place! But it is very weak.

There are about two to three hundred households on both sides of the New Shoal. Most of them rely on this shoal for a living. Straw mat sheds extend from halfway up the mountain all the way to the riverbank. But it has not formed even a small street market; they live very freely and scattered. In addition to selling tea and wine, the most common commodity is opium.

These boat trackers spend all day in these straw huts, sitting on a kind of long bench, hugging their knees with their hands, looking into the distance, and listening to the roar of the shoal water.

In addition to pulling steamers, they also pull wooden boats loaded with local merchants' goods up the shoal or contract to guide these wooden boats down the shoal. These people's lives change very little. In the winter, they rely entirely on this business to make a living. They know in advance what time each day which boat will pass. When the boat arrives, men, women, old and young all participate:

"Heave-ho! Heave—ho!"

It is said that as long as you participate, whether you pull or not, you will still get a few copper coins.

To the east of the New Shoal, there is a mountain said to have been chained in the back with iron chains, hence the name "Locked Mountain" (鎖住山). The stone peaks on both sides collapse into the heart of the river. If one day it collapses like the old mountain above the New Shoal, it would be extremely beneficial for these people. So they often say:

"For Zigui to prosper, unless 'Locked Mountain' collapses."

They are constantly hoping for a newer New Shoal to appear in Zigui.

Rouge Water 267

— Bai Wei

In the dining hall of a hotel in Paris, twenty or so Chinese men and women are sitting around an oval table, enjoying a fine dinner; it is an engagement banquet.

Zhi Mu, because of his young age and close friendship with the host, was placed at the very end of the table. He wasn't feeling well that evening and didn't want to attend the banquet in the first place. But he couldn't resist the host's repeated phone calls and finally attended.

Miss Duan happened to be sitting to his right, a slightly plump nineteen-year-old girl who spoke Beijing dialect with a pleasant accent. In many social settings, she had trained her demeanor to be neither dissolute nor shy. The unique beauty of a young girl was fully expressed by her embellishments. She had only been in France for four months, and she had already become the center of pursuit for some men. There were two at the table: they admired Miss Duan but were afraid to approach her; now they were shooting jealous glances from the other end of the oval table, expressing unnamed resentment at Zhi Mu's proximity to Miss Duan.

The hosts and guests were all talking and laughing excitedly. The twenty or so men and women unconsciously divided into several small groups, each with a focus of discussion. Miss Duan had always been talkative, and Miss Yu, Mrs. Hong, and Mr. Lu nearby could also contribute to the fun, but Zhi Mu had hardly spoken. He drank and ate silently, not feeling the need to make any superfluous remarks. This made the guests next to him feel strangely annoyed and out of place.

Zhi Mu's silence particularly aroused Miss Duan's aversion. She thought: I have never met such a clumsy and indifferent young man who is not even ugly! He not only doesn't know how to show the minimum politeness to his neighbor, but he doesn't even give half a smile to the female guest beside him. He's probably newly arrived in France. But judging from his well-tailored evening dress and his skillful use of knives and forks, it seems that he has lived in France for a long time. In short, it's simply unfortunate to sit with such a young man! "Let me teach him a lesson." Miss Duan raised her eyebrows and smiled slightly.

So she sent a suggestive glance to Miss Yu, Mrs. Hong, and Mr. Lu, and then quietly pursed her red lips towards Zhi Mu, and they all nodded in tacit agreement. Zhi Mu didn't see it at all. He only occasionally noticed Miss Duan picking up her handbag placed on her lap, taking out a small mirror, and naturally applying some rouge to her thin lips.

Halfway through the banquet, the guests began to toast the newly engaged hosts and unanimously asked the hosts to drink a crossed-arms cup of wine. After a burst of laughter, it was the guests' turn to toast each other.

"Mr. Su, would you like to have a drink with me?" Miss Duan said to Zhi Mu with a charming smile.

"That would be an honor," Zhi Mu replied calmly.

"Mr. Su, this full glass of red wine, I haven't even touched it yet, so please drink it. Please forgive me for only drinking half a glass of white wine to accompany you."

"Thank you," Zhi Mu raised the glass that Miss Duan gently pushed over, poured the liquid inside completely into his mouth, and swallowed it in one breath without thinking.

Immediately he realized that the liquid was not red wine at all, and it didn't have that sour and sweet taste! He frowned and analyzed it in a hurry, and then determined that the liquid was just a glass of mineral water, and further examination of the outside of the glass clearly showed rouge washed off from Miss Duan's lips. Zhi Mu cursed Miss Duan inwardly: "So it turns out that she applied rouge several times just now, the purpose was to prepare to wash it in mineral water, posing as red wine, to fool me." His face flushed. He smiled bitterly at Miss Yu, Mrs. Hong, and Mr. Lu, who were trying to suppress their laughter. He had been tricked by this cunning girl!

"Thank you," Miss Duan also drank half a glass of white wine at the same time. She looked at the empty glass in front of Zhi Mu and smiled softly. Zhi Mu turned his head away in resentment, sizing up this mischievous Miss Duan. She was talking to Mrs. Jin on her right, only giving him a profile to admire. His eyes quickly followed her forehead, over her nose and mouth, to her neck. The very beautiful curve made him exhale a long breath of satisfaction. Then he greedily looked down from her chest all the way to her thighs.

"Let me hold your plump body for one night to compensate for the exquisite naughtiness of this glass of rouge water!" He turned his head back and sat upright. He no longer stared at Miss Duan, so that others would not know his thoughts.

After champagne was poured into the funnel-shaped glasses in front of everyone, everyone raised their glasses, thanked the hosts, and wished each other health and happiness. Some drank it all in one breath, while others only tasted it and put the glass down. The banquet was considered over. The hosts and guests stood up in unison, left the table, and sat around several coffee tables, drinking another small glass of strong sweet wine or brandy. At the same time, the waiters also served coffee. (To be continued)

Early Summer Night 268

— Sha Ming

When the sun sets below the horizon, the rosy clouds in the blue sky have all faded away.

The frogs in the garden begin to croak restlessly,

Heavy shadows rush through the woods like charging cattle,

The drowsy streetlights flicker dimly.

Wandering alone in the long and empty corridor, lost in thought,

Suddenly, the mournful cry of an owl rises,

Is it like a widow's lament?

Melancholy, sorrow, and fear completely envelop my body.

Mountain Shop Ticket (6) 269

— Tang Xiru

Afa didn't dare to hope he would win, but he desperately wanted to. Two mice were jumping in his temples, he was covered in sweat, his eyes were blurred, he couldn't see what was written on the blackboard, and the heads of the people in front were constantly rising and falling. "Only one character 'wealth' (財) is right," someone squeezed out, saying disappointedly. Afa's heart lit up. But it immediately darkened again. What's the use of getting one or two characters right? It's even more unpleasant than not getting any right at all!

The people inside the shop squeezed out, and the people outside squeezed in. The eyes of those squeezing in were all eager, and the faces of those squeezing out were all ashen.

It was Afa's turn. Layer by layer, he had squeezed from the last row to the second row. He looked up! What! He almost shouted out. All the blood, flesh, and bones in his body danced and sang. Slow down! Could it be that he was dreaming? Could the words written on the blackboard be those characters that he knew so well that he almost didn't recognize them today? He rubbed his eyes, rubbed them again, until tears came out. Could these be the characters he had circled? Was he having a fever, or was it real? He was so anxious he wanted to cry! He was so happy he wanted to cry! He touched his forehead, and large beads of sweat were seeping out. Ah! Are the characters written on the blackboard really those characters? Can you guarantee that in a few minutes they won't transform like the Guangzhou lottery tickets and be worth nothing? Could these characters really be the ones he circled? They stood there, all so majestic, like old friends who had suddenly become officials, and he was a little afraid to go forward and recognize them! He wanted everyone to tell him, and to tell him loudly, that he was not dreaming or having a fever! It was all real! He had won with these characters! His two cents had really turned into tens of thousands of dollars! And those tens of thousands of dollars were all his!

He seemed dazed, and asked: (The words were almost stuck in his throat, and he couldn't force them out) "Excuse me, excuse me, what characters won?" As he said this, he touched the middle-aged man wearing glasses standing in front of him. "Big, wealth, money, four, ten thousand, more, gold!"

"Really?"

The man with glasses seemed insulted and turned his head to look at another blackboard.

"Is it a two-cent ticket?"

"Is it from the previous two days?"

"If you win with a two-cent ticket, will you really get more than forty thousand dollars?"

He still wanted to ask, he still wanted to ask many questions. This matter was too bizarre, too complicated, too absurd, more unbelievable than a dream. No, he wouldn't be at peace until he had the money in his hands and didn't ask any more questions.

It was true that he had won. Many people confirmed that the characters on the blackboard were no different from the characters he had circled. But the money would be available tomorrow morning. They had to wait for the remittance from the Macau headquarters, which was the usual practice.

He squeezed out of the pile of envious eyes. His head was held very high: "I'm a rich man! I'm a rich man!" He took one step and recited one sentence, and laughed after each sentence.

Brief Remarks

County Magistrate Punished with Hard Labor 270

— Mingtang

Jinan Dispatch: An, the County Magistrate of Dong'a County, because he abused public funds while in office and put them all in his private pockets, was sued by the people to the province. After a military court investigation confirmed the facts, he was sentenced by Chairman Han Fuqu of Shandong Province to a fine equal to twice the amount of the embezzled funds and to hard labor, carrying earth to repair the Dongmen city wall road as a warning to corrupt officials. This can be said to be a very interesting matter. Chairman Han Fuqu of Shandong Province has been in office for several years, and his actions are often surprising. For example, he previously personally tried a case of passion killing, and now he has sentenced the county magistrate to hard labor, carrying earth to repair the road on the city wall. There are several other similar matters, but unfortunately, I can't remember them all. In short, they are all very special. Although this is not within the law, given the ineffectiveness of today's laws and the prevalence of corruption, doing these very special things outside the law can be said to be satisfying. As mentioned earlier, County Magistrate An of Dong'a County abused public funds while in office, which under normal circumstances would not be considered a complete matter. Even if the people sued to the province, wouldn't it just end with "there is a cause for the matter, but no evidence has been found"? However, Han Fuqu gave him "hard labor," which is meaningful. Punishing the county magistrate with hard labor is to completely expose the county magistrate's crimes to the people. I think that when the county magistrate is doing hard labor, many people will definitely stare at him; and under the public gaze, the county magistrate will definitely be ashamed beyond measure.

However, to return to the question, is it effective to punish corruption by simply punishing one or two county magistrates with hard labor? This is somewhat questionable. Because, as we know, corruption is produced by a certain society. A certain social organization then produces a certain social situation. And the current society is fundamentally a corrupt society. In such a society, how can one find people who are not corrupt? Therefore, this is not a question of whether a part of the officials are corrupt, but rather that this society fundamentally cannot produce incorruptible officials. Han Fuqu's method of punishing county magistrates with hard labor is like killing a dog to warn the monkeys, but will the majority of corrupt officials be able to learn from the past after Chairman Han's "killing"? This is the first question we must raise.

Of course, Han Fuqu's punishment of a certain county magistrate was only an occasional measure, and he did not say that corruption could necessarily be eradicated by this. Therefore, to a certain extent, we may as well agree with his action. However, we must not forget that this is only an occasional event, and at most it is only pleasing to the people. It is not necessarily effective in eradicating corruption. The real eradication of corruption can only be achieved in the course of our overthrowing the old society, transforming the new society, and the practice of the masses. Only when the masses truly overthrow the old society and transform the new society can corruption be completely defeated and eradicated. This is the point that we should recognize today.

A Trip to the Fan Ancestral Hall in Tianping 271

— Zou Zhao

In the past, there was a famous scholar from Shanxi who, because he loved the scenery of Suzhou, abandoned his original home in Shanxi and called himself a Suzhou person. What is it about Suzhou that makes people change their affections like this? Indeed, Suzhou has many things that can make people linger! However, I especially love her waters: whether it is the spring water with gentle waves or the autumn water with a desolate air, they are both lovable. They are really as interesting as her girls! The waters of Suzhou.

The late spring weather is completely immersed in a gentle atmosphere. Quietly driving a small boat, from the city to Tianping Mountain. Although there is a long journey of thirty *li*, it will not make people feel the slightest bit lonely, the scenery along the way is enough to amuse you; remember, the one paddling the oars is still a Wu girl! I put my bare feet in the water and let them soak, making a gurgling sound; I couldn't help but hum Wu Meicun's poem: "In front of the door is a stretch of Hengtang water, the oars of Hengtang fly away like a bird." If this doesn't describe the waters of Suzhou, what else does? I don't want my name to be left forever in the world, I just want to be a small fish in the river here.

Setting off to Tianping in the morning, you can reach it in three hours. The mountain is not very high, but it is so charming and moving! I thought of Dai Chunshi's famous line, "Spring mountains are like beauties." Spring mountains are really beautiful! Because the mountain is quiet, the chirping of birds seems even more secluded and pleasant to the ear; the birds probably have added the atmosphere of the Six Dynasties! Otherwise, why haven't I heard it in other places.

I came to Tianping to visit the ancestral hall of Fan Wenzheng Gong (范文正公); however, the Fan Ancestral Hall, famous for thousands of years, has long been reduced to overgrown weeds! I pushed aside many vines to find the ancestral hall gate, but it was deeply locked, forcing me to turn to a side path and pay homage to the statue of Wenzheng Gong in the three dilapidated houses. The dust was so thick, the clay sculpture had faded a layer of color, and everything looked desolate and pitiful. Our great man of a generation! You made a good Yitian Ji (義田記), but what about your descendants now? I heard from the elders in the village that the descendants of the Fan family are still virtuous, and there are many wealthy people in the city, but everyone

Page 18

is unwilling to donate money, allowing the famous historical sites to continue to decay like this, which is a pity.

Deep in the bamboo forest, ancient trees soar into the sky, surrounded by short walls. Inside is the tomb of Wenzheng Gong, surrounded by mountains on three sides, and facing the magnificent peaks of Wanhuchao Tian (萬笏朝天) in front, a magnificent sight. It is said that this is the tomb of Wenzheng Gong's clothes and hat. There is clear spring water here, I scooped some with my hands and drank it, and it was indeed cool and refreshing, probably because I had been walking for a long time and was thirsty! I thought:

To the east of the tomb is Gaoyizhuang (高義莊), built at the foot of Tianping Mountain, with the imperial inscription of Emperor Gaozong of the Qing Dynasty enshrined in the main hall. Perhaps because of the imperial inscription, the Zhuang is better repaired than the ancestral hall, probably for this reason.

Further past is the Yushuting (御書亭), which is said to be where Emperor Gaozong of the Qing Dynasty stayed during his southern tour. There are two poems made by the emperor, and the local people regard them as sacred and specially built a pavilion to enshrine them, but now it has also been abandoned! Leaving only people to reminisce.

The passing of time forced me to return. I really didn't want to leave here! I would rather stay in the mountains for the rest of my life and not return to the polluted city. But after all, I had to return. I lay on the clean stern of the boat, watching the flying returning clouds, completing my journey in the hazy twilight.

How to Avoid Being Pessimistic in Life 272

— Ben

Living in this era of the century, generally speaking, everyone has some three parts boredom, five parts pain. The ultimate in boredom and pain is to make people discouraged and pessimistic. This is an inevitable kind of era disease, which is indeed annoying to talk about.

Look; in this large group of colleagues, who can escape this trap.

Old Zhang frowns all day long, and always talks about "no hope." Originally, he was only in his twenties, a young and vigorous man, but he looks depressed and has no vitality at all. When he hears people talk about world affairs, he will scold like a village woman, as if the world is bad to the core, and there is nothing to praise or linger over. It is said that the reason why he is so pessimistic is that he was once tossed about in the political vortex, and his base colleagues sold out the interests of the public. So he resolutely withdrew, and then he took a pessimistic view of everything, and his attitude suddenly became negative.

Old Xiao seems like he is about to cry when he talks about women. Although he is not as completely disappointed as Old Zhang in other things, he always expresses full pessimism. It is said that he has been fooled by women, and he has also played with women. From this, he understood why women are women, and felt that they are really hateful things. So he was extremely disappointed in them, and also fundamentally pessimistic about life.

Although Old Wen is relatively better, he has recently joined them and become pessimistic as well. Whenever the topic of salary comes up, he pouts, and even scolds the accountant's mother. Twenty days have passed in April, and there is no news about the March salary. In the future, it will definitely be worthless, completely donated, purely voluntary work. What kind of world is this? So Old Wen gets particularly upset when he talks about these things, and there is a reason for it.

In a nutshell, who among the large group of colleagues is not like this? When they meet, they are always like enemies, and it is difficult to see a smile on some faces. Even if there is, it always disappears quickly.

Extending this, among the 400 million compatriots, who is not like this except for a small number of the "successful class," especially the young people.

This is not a good phenomenon, and we must find a way to cheer up.

So, how can we avoid being pessimistic? What kind of power should we use to eliminate the entanglement of pessimism? According to my thinking, if we can follow the following methods, we will definitely obtain considerable effectiveness.

First, what I want to propose is that we should have a clear understanding, whether it is of life or of society, we must see clearly that we are human beings, and human beings have a special mission, which is to be active in our view of life, take on our responsibilities, and be determined to do something beneficial for society. We must know that once we fall into pessimism, we will not be able to accomplish anything at all, and we will fundamentally undermine the meaning of life, and just live a muddled life.

Second, I feel that what should be proposed is that we should take personal gains and losses lightly and on a small scale. If a love affair fails, why is it worth worrying about so much? If we have been tortured in politics, we should seize the route of improvement. In short, we should see that there are always places in the world that are more worthy of praise than love, and politics will never always be a black mess.

Third, what I want to propose is that our daily life should be rigorous and disciplined. In other words, we should live in extremely tense "busyness," studying hard, writing hard, and working hard, then boredom and pain will never climb into our hearts. In fact, the reason why many people call themselves "bored" is purely because they are "idle" and have nothing to do, so the seeds of boredom attack their hearts, making it impossible for you not to be pessimistic.

I wrote a muddled piece, and I feel that it is based on experience. I often encourage myself with this, and I am even more willing to encourage my friends who have fallen into the path of pessimism.

A Certain Mansion 273

— Rose

Just as dawn broke, a black Studebaker sped through the morning air. Vegetable vendors were already carrying their loads to the early market, and the Madam had just returned from playing mahjong all night at a certain mansion. Wang Ma hurried to welcome the Madam inside, and the Madam began to chatter endlessly about her mahjong experience of the night. Whether triumphant or frustrated, she would excitedly speak loudly, until the Fourth Young Master, deep in sleep, was startled awake by the noisy sounds. He demanded that Chun Xiang help him get dressed. The Master also feigned a cough on his opium couch. Realizing it was still time for others to sleep, she quietly lay down on her own opium couch and began to smoke.

The Fourth Young Master, dressed, entered the room. He remembered that the teacher had instructed him yesterday to bring half a dollar for the aviation donation. He asked the Madam, but she had just lost money, and the mention of aviation donation gave her a headache: "What aviation donation, it's all a bunch of deceitful nonsense. I spent a hundred dollars on the last aviation lottery, and didn't even win anything. Ignore them. Tell the teacher that your mother said we're not donating."

The child was rebuffed and, fearing the teacher's scolding, started to cry, "The teacher said we have to donate; everyone else is donating, some even one or two dollars."

"I said we're not donating – not a single penny."

The child continued to cry, annoying the Madam, who scolded him to no avail. Finally, she took out a small two-dime bill from her wallet: "Take it, and tell the teacher we're poor and can only donate two dimes."

The child took the money, still crying.

The Eldest Young Master and his wife had been dancing all night, only returning home at half past three in the morning to sleep. At this moment, they were awakened by the Madam's noisy return, followed by the Fourth Young Master's crying. The Eldest Young Master flew into a rage, shouting and cursing from upstairs. The Eldest Young Mistress, finding it unbearable, quickly ordered Lotus to take the two colorful paper hats brought back from the dance hall to the Fourth Young Master, telling her to quickly coax him and send him off to school.

Lotus came in and said many nice things. The Fourth Young Master finally forgot about the five-dime aviation donation, put on the paper hat, demanded several kisses from Lotus, and happily jumped into the car.

Stepping out of the door, he ran into two unfamiliar men in Western suits driving a brightly shining limousine, sending the Fourth Concubine and Miss Wang home. The Fourth Concubine took a box of chocolates out of her coat pocket and put it in the Fourth Young Master's hand, then she and the Third Young Mistress slipped stealthily into their own rooms.

At school, the Fourth Young Master still wore the paper hat, giving the other one to his best friend, and sharing the chocolates with his classmates. He explained to them that his older brother often took his sister-in-law to dance halls, and these hats were given to them there. Sometimes the dance halls also gave dancers all kinds of interesting toys, and his brother had even taken him to play there once, where he had seen many beautiful women. The children were all envious.

After school, upon returning home, the Madam was again preparing to go out to play mahjong, and the Fourth Young Master tugged at her sleeve, wanting to go with her. After some arguing, the Madam, without options, took out a dollar from her wallet and put it in his hand, telling him to take Lotus to the movies.

So the child stopped making a fuss, and Lotus quietly returned to her room to doll herself up; they rode in the Madam's car together to the movie theater.

— Meng

"I say, Elder Sister Next Door, why are you so busy?" "You don't know, Elder Sister, my paralyzed father is blind, and my mother is feeble, my three younger siblings are not even ten years old yet,

The entire family of six depends on me alone!"

A Private Letter 275

— Jian

Dear XX,

I read your letter again at dusk yesterday. It was another debt-collecting letter! Why are you so relentless? I told you before that my love for Shuangmei arose from ordinary circumstances: first acquaintance, then friendship, and eventually love. It was all very normal, nothing special to tell. Yet you insist on a detailed account, as if you wouldn't be satisfied until you knew every detail.

Why are you so unsatisfied? I ask you—

Alright, if you insist on knowing, then I will tell you.

In a mild autumn, I was strolling along the S River. At that time, my mood was like yours, every action filled with a dream of love. I was hoping to meet a woman on this journey, and that this woman would be the one I had been waiting for and would have a love affair with me. Naturally, someone traveling with such expectations is in a dangerous position, because his loneliness makes him prone to a longing for love.

After a long wait, it finally arrived. One day, it was a misty morning, I think, I was at a bus station, waiting for my travel companion to visit Mount W. My luggage was simple: just a blanket and a briefcase.

The morning breeze carried a hint of chill, and I leaned against the entrance of the bus station, lost in my thoughts. What kind of travel companion would I meet on the bus? Would the person I was waiting for be on this trip, or on the second, or the third? A vague sadness weighed slightly on my heart.

Suddenly, I heard footsteps outside – the sound of a woman's leather shoes. I quickly looked up. Ah, the person I was waiting for had arrived – a woman with a graceful figure and charming appearance.

As soon as she entered the station, she asked if there were any buses. I felt that this was a blessing, so I eagerly stepped forward and said to her, "Are you also going to Mount W, Madam? How about we travel together?"

"Oh, are you also going to Mount W, Sir? Then, then that would be great."

Since the bus wouldn't depart with only one passenger, my suggestion was exactly what she wanted.

So we took the bus to Mount W together. The bumpy mountain road gave us plenty of time to talk. That's how we got acquainted.

When the bus reached XX Cave, we had to take a sedan chair to continue. This gave me a chance to offer my services. So I hired a sedan chair for her and took care of her luggage. Then the two of us went up the mountain together.

On the bus, I learned that she was a graduate of a normal school and had worked in the social sector for several years. She was visiting Mount W to see her sick sister. However, from her gentle demeanor, one could not detect any sign of a primary school teacher, and her conversation was nothing like that of a rigid normal school student.

I don't know why, but the moment I saw her, I loved her, and I immediately knew that she was the person I had been waiting for, that she was the lover Heaven had destined for me.

The Game of Language 276

— Tianhua

The same lesson taught by two different teachers can result in one enlivening the entire classroom while the other may only manage to induce sleep with their voice – this is something we often see in school. The primary reason for a teacher's success or failure should be attributed to their ability to speak well. Not only teachers, but anyone's success or failure is closely related to their ability to speak. This may seem like a miracle, but one can rise to high office and gain great wealth and power over the masses with their silver tongue. We need not look to far-off figures like Su Qin and Zhang Yi from the Warring States period who exchanged eloquent speech for high positions, but consider the famous figures on the political stage in Europe and America. How many of them were unable to win the support of their people through eloquent words? Speech is necessary in all aspects and deserves our attention.

Webster, the creator of the great dictionary, was a master conversationalist. His words could increase one's courage. "I would rather recognize Han Jingzhou than be enfeoffed as a marquis of ten thousand households." Han Jingzhou must have been an engaging conversationalist who left a good impression. Or, "Fall in love at first sight" – seeing your face and hearing your conversation can often have such wonderful results.

Good conversation is not merely a "game of language"; it often has practical effects. Conversation, to be more precise, should be a form of "careful observation," with a serious meaning.

Page 19

, not containing any sense of play. Without looking at your , merely through the attitude you take, and the you adopt in conversation, one can easily determine the kind of person you are. Your thoughts, aspirations, knowledge, intelligence, and memory can all be accurately assessed from the impression you make during a few minutes of conversation. Can this be considered a "game of language?"

Brevity is the key to conversation. When ten or twenty minutes of conversation can resolve matters of national importance, then conversation is both simple and crucial. A master conversationalist is succinct and precise, never verbose. Excessive words will always lead to failure. Those who speak eloquently may be the least skilled. They easily expose their shortcomings in front of others, easily "reveal their cards," letting others know their secrets. "Silence is golden, speaking is silver" – this saying is insightful.

The art of conversation can be learned and trained. Diplomats and politicians are not born that way. Lawyers and judges must not only spend four or five years in university but also train themselves as much as possible through speeches, debates, and mock trials. "Conversation Studies" will become a discipline, and should be a discipline, and is already tending to become one. Since there are "Rhetoric" and "Debate Techniques," why shouldn't there be "Conversation Studies" or "Conversation Techniques"?

There is a field called "Social Control" in American sociology that attempts to control human behavior through various methods, such as praise, reward, and intimidation, to influence the actions of others. The application of these methods often relies on conversation. Therefore, they pay close attention to this. A "Social Control" expert is certainly a great conversationalist, someone who understands human psychology and is skilled in rhetoric. The dialectical method of scientific sociology is also closely related to conversation, as it instructs us to recognize reality from contradictions, understand individuals from the whole, and seek the truth of facts from the movement and development of things. Familiarity with these principles can help us achieve the desired success in conversation. Future sociologists and psychologists will inevitably emphasize this human language function, develop it, and benefit both individuals and society. Perhaps, in the near future, general schools will establish "Conversation Departments," just like the "Chinese Language Department" and "English Language Department" that exist in schools today?

Many great scholars have failed because they were not good at this. Many people with insufficient academic ability have succeeded with the help of their mouths. Isn't this worth our attention? Are we still treating it as a "game of language" and ignoring it?

Amateur Mailbox

Secret Pregnancy 277

Editor:

I have a friend who met a woman last year. This woman's family had already arranged a marriage for her. Later, they fell in love and had a physical relationship. Soon after, she became secretly pregnant, six months along. Her original fiancé had even set a date to marry her. How could she marry him? She had no choice but to run away to my friend's place, and they began to live together. But the wedding date was approaching, so her parents were extremely anxious and searched everywhere, finally finding my friend. Her parents were furious and vowed to never give my friend peace. Sir, what can be done? Please help him think of a perfect solution. Sincerely, Wang Mingqu, bowing respectfully.

Answer: When a man and a woman get too close, love often arises naturally. Therefore, those who are already engaged or have partners should be especially careful when interacting with friends of the opposite sex, because such situations easily lead to unfortunate tragedies. If one is dissatisfied with a marriage arranged by their family, they should first cancel the engagement. It is never appropriate to ignore it and fall in love with someone else, let alone recklessly engage in a physical relationship. Similarly, the other party should also exercise extreme restraint, ensuring that the relationship does not stray beyond the bounds of friendship. Even if the engagement is dissolved, but not recognized by the family, one still cannot do this and have a relationship with another person. Wouldn't that make the family even more disgusted? Wouldn't that create even more trouble and make it more difficult to resolve the problem than breaking off the engagement? Moreover, breaking off an arranged engagement, although opposed by stubborn families, is still sympathized with by society. But a situation like your friend's lover's is not only not sympathized with but also despised. Therefore, before helping your friend solve the problem, the editor must attribute it to their lack of reason and acting too emotionally.

But what's done is done, and what good is it to blame the past? Moreover, stubborn families who are too inflexible and completely disregard the wishes of their children, as well as modern marriage concepts, are also the main causes of such tragedies. Naturally, we cannot completely blame your friend and others. Now, the editor believes that the best course of action for them is to have her propose breaking off the engagement on their side. Marriage agreements have no absolute validity, and not complying is not a big deal. At most, it would only involve compensating the other party for their losses. On the one hand, she must also beg her parents to accept their marriage. Although her parents deeply hate their daughter's behavior, they still have a sense of parental love. If she uses tactful language and admits her mistakes, I think they will definitely not make things difficult for your friend and force them to separate. In the event that they are extremely stubborn and unwilling to agree, then she can also tell her parents that "she had no obligation to obey a marriage arranged by her parents." Her only mistake was not breaking off the engagement beforehand. Therefore, even if her parents go to court to sue your friend, it will mostly involve a reconciliation, and nothing serious will happen. The editor

Novel

A Poor Gentleman (Part 4) 278

— By George Gissing, Translated by Sun Pu

Awakening at eight o'clock – he could tell the time from the nearby chimes – Mr. Dunbar hurried to dress. Opening the door, he saw a tray outside, holding the smallest possible amount of breakfast food: half a pint of milk, bread, and butter. At nine o'clock, he went downstairs and solemnly knocked on the door of a front room, which opened with a discordant sound inviting him in. This room was occupied by a middle-aged man and a young girl, who were wholeheartedly engaged in the daily work of ordinary bookbinding.

"Good morning, sir," Mr. Dunbar said, bowing his head, "Good morning, Miss Sharg. Fine weather! Delightful weather!"

As if on a frosty morning, he stood rubbing his hands. The old bookbinder nodded coldly and, after hesitating, immediately gave Mr. Dunbar a task. The gentleman enthusiastically set to work. He was learning the basics of bookbinding and worked patiently, showing some natural talent, until the end of the day's work.

Mr. Dunbar, a gentleman from Buckinghamshire, once lived in comfort and considerable dignity on the income from sound investments, had now fallen to this state. He had studied at Harrow and graduated from Cambridge. By the time he seriously considered a career, he felt it was almost too late to do anything; and since he had no need to trouble himself with such thoughts, he settled near the village home of his wealthy and influential friend, Mr. Callman, and lived a life of simple idleness. The years passed quietly. He had considered marriage once or twice, but deep reflection made him hesitant; eventually, he realized he was born for bachelorhood and content with a single life. If only he could have seen the unreliability of other temptations with the same clarity! Unfortunately, he listened to Mr. Callman, whose usual conversation was about speculation, companies, and high interest rates. Mr. Dunbar was tempted not for his own sake; he had more money than he could use. But he thought of his sister, married to an unsuccessful village lawyer, and their six children, who, like the wealthy uncles in novels, should be happily assisted when they came of age. He blindly trusted Callman's plan, and as a result, one morning he found himself trembling on the brink of ruin; on receiving concrete reports, he fell off the cliff.

The Shun Pao Screen Section

Is There a Secret to Little Star LeRoy's Expressions? (Part 1) 279

— Guangdao

In "A Bedtime Story," those of us who have seen the performance of little star Baby LeRoy, who co-starred with Heifetz, all find it a bit strange. How can he make all kinds of expressions? Who taught him? How was he taught? It's interesting to talk about it briefly now.

Many people say that there must be some secret method, something that cannot be done outside of filming. But it is said that there is no secret method in it. It is completely using the very simple, basic methods that everyone received when they were young, with some innovative ideas added. Plus, Baby LeRoy is an extremely clever child, which makes the task twice as effective and easy. Another point is that Baby LeRoy's caretakers like to deliberately exaggerate Baby LeRoy's abilities, saying that he has a unique talent and that they often feel inadequate. They like to say that he is a natural "actor" and that he must understand the plot. That is especially a joke. Imagine a twenty-month-old child understanding the script and knowing how to perform; it's like saying he can even read the script. However, his special intelligence, his ability to move his face, his extremely cute temperament, and his ability and willingness to cooperate with the people around him are beyond the reach of ordinary children. But to say that he understands the plot is truly an exaggeration.

Baby LeRoy has a thorough understanding of his personal director's intentions. His personal director is a Miss Rachel Smith. She is in charge of all the children at Paramount and has a special affection for Baby LeRoy. Wherever Baby LeRoy is, there is also Miss Smith. Baby LeRoy also listens to Smith the most. He can understand and obey all her orders, hints, and requests one by one. Many people claim to be Baby LeRoy's "discoverers," but the true discoverer is Miss Smith. She was the first to see him in the Salvation Army orphanage and pay attention to him. She was the first to coax him into making all kinds of funny movements. Baby LeRoy is able to "learn by imitation." Whatever you do to him, he will imitate, and it is extremely natural and realistic. His "feelings" in front of the camera are completely at the command of his director, Miss Smith. As for the plot and script, it can be said that they have nothing to do with Baby LeRoy.

When Baby LeRoy acted in his first film, he was only six months old, so there were naturally few opportunities to make him express emotions. At that time, to capture the kind of expression he needed, you could only wait for him to slowly develop the expression needed in the story. Fortunately, his responsiveness is very fast, and people don't have to wait long. He is so naturally innocent and lively that his every move is almost always worth putting in the camera. The funny thing is that it is very difficult to make him cry, perhaps because he has that lively and playful innocence, and no one can bear to make him cry. (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "The Girl and the Boy" 280

— Luo Ping

The Girl and the Boy

"The Girl and the Boy" is an old work by Lilian Harvey. In terms of directing techniques, it is slightly outdated. In today's context, it cannot be said to belong to the "positive" aspect.

However, I think there are several aspects of "The Girl and the Boy" that are worth mentioning.

When Jenny goes on stage to perform, she is ridiculed by a large group of hotel servants below the stage. The noisy sounds made the Duke in the backstage anxious and unable to do anything, covering his ears and not daring to listen to the boos from the front stage. The description of the Duke being ridiculed is indeed enough.

But there is also positive ridicule; when Jenny and Victor meet, the description of many audience members pointing at the Duke is also good.

Lu Xun Bellos, who plays the Duke, is very well suited to play this ridiculed role.

This kind of ridicule of noble people is certainly not based on a political stance. It merely satirizes destructive vanity and sings the praises of pure love.

Is so-called "vanity" worth our satire? I think it is more important to fundamentally eliminate the source of vanity.

As for pure love, we have said more than once that it cannot but be an excessively beautiful fantasy in the present.

The praise, the ridicule of the Duke, is nothing more than an expression of the ideology of the urban petty bourgeoisie. They sing the praises of the warmth of spring, hating and envying those who stand above them. And isn't the bouncing singing and dancing in "The Girl and the Boy" also perfectly suited to their tastes?

Someone said: "If you have painful things, just go to Lilian. Her plays can often tell people some ways to get rid of pain." Doesn't this already explain their ideas? Moreover, this also explains the meaning of this kind of "musical."

In "The Girl and the Boy," Lilian Harvey fulfilled her singing and dancing duties under the direction of Wilhelm Thiele, but her acting talent could not be concealed, such as in the scene where Jenny provokes Victor.

In my opinion, Lilian's personality is flirtatious, Sophisticated, a typical daughter of a capitalist society. In "The Girl and the Boy," no matter how much the singing and dancing tramples on her personality, you can still see some of her personality after all.

"Torrential Rain and Pear Blossoms" - My Review 281

— Xu Hairong

The acting power in this film is indeed very moving. Although the story is quite ordinary, the portrayal here is so truthful and vivid.

In terms of structure, we can discover Mr. Ma Xuweibang's cleverness. He has made very appropriate preparations for the arrangement of the environment, the placement of characters, and the construction of the film's atmosphere of sorrow, which is gratifying.

However, we must point out the director's oversights. For example, when Xiao Ying falls on the road on her way home, he did not arrange for torrential rain, which is an oversight. In addition, things like Xiao Qin and Xiao Ying having their hair permed and eyebrows drawn are also somewhat inconsistent with reality.

Written After Watching "Torrential Rain and Pear Blossoms" 282

— Nai Huang

"Torrential Rain and Pear Blossoms," which everyone has been eagerly anticipating, has finally premiered at the Jin Cheng Theater.

Chen Yanyan has changed her style in this film, but her performance is still good. Her expressions are quite capable of moving people.

Gao Zhanfei is very careful in this film. Among his past films, I think Gao Zhanfei's performance in "Torrential Rain and Pear Blossoms" is the best.

Tan Ying originally specialized in performing flirtatious roles, but in "Torrential Rain and Pear Blossoms," she has also changed her style, but has instead performed more earnestly and made progress.

He Feiguang is working very hard, but due to the limited screen time, he inevitably has some inconspicuous moments.

In short, "Torrential Rain and Pear Blossoms" is a masterpiece in the Chinese film scene in recent years. The photography, lighting, and set design also have considerable achievements.

Director Ma Xuweibang can also be considered successful in directing this film.

Liliane Haidt's Old Partners, Henri Garat and Willy Fritsch 283

— Shen Weng

Whenever we mention old male-female partners on the screen, we think of movie queen and emperor Janet Gaynor and Charles Farrell, Jeanette MacDonald and Maurice Chevalier, as well as Greta Garbo and John Gilbert, and so on.

Now, let me talk about Liliane Haidt again. In the United States, because she has made very few films, she does not yet have a fixed partner. But in Europe, she has two very famous old partners. One is Willy Fritsch, who is rumored to be marrying Haidt, and the other is Henri Garat. You have probably heard these two names a lot! The most interesting thing is not that Haidt collaborates with Willy Fritsch in this film and with Henri Garat in that film, but that these two old partners are used simultaneously in one film; and they play the same role, which may sound strange to you all.

In fact, the Ufa company often made copies of a film in three languages: English, French, and German. In the German copy, Willy Fritsch is cast. But in the English or French copy, Willy Fritsch is replaced by Henri Garat. Like many films in the past, such as "The Love Waltz," "The Road to Paradise," and "The Congress Dances," because the copies shown in China were in English or French, we only knew that the male lead was Henri Garat, and we would not have thought that there was also a Willy Fritsch. Now, the Nanjing Grand Theatre is showing "The Girl and the Boy," starring Liliane Haidt. The male lead in this film is also Henri Garat. I dare not say much about how well it performs right now. But in any case, we have seen quite a few films they have collaborated on, and they will definitely not disappoint us.

— Shen Fen

Since the Tianyi Film Company's "The Fire of Youth," "Good Land," "Fleeting Time," and "Spring Dreams in the Palace" were released in succession, because there has been significant progress in consciousness, technique, and all other aspects, the public's estimation of Tianyi has also increased a lot. Recently, the company's "Rouge and Iron Blood" (previously named "Iron Blood Rouge"), which has been promoted for a long time, will be released in a major local theater within ten days. Movie Novel

The House of Rothschild (18) 285

— Wen Yin

Nathan stuck his head out of the carriage and said to them, "I hope this whole war is not built on such a romantic basis." Fitzroy and Julie reluctantly separated. When they walked up to Nathan, he said to Fitzroy: "Colonel Fitzroy, I give Napoleon a hundred days – no more. If, after a hundred days, you are still alive – you seem to be an unkillable youth – you can come to London and talk to me." Fitzroy looked pleased and thanked Nathan profusely: "I'll be counting the days one by one." He finished speaking, and helped Julie into the carriage. Julie got into the carriage and kept sticking her head out to smile at Fitz, feeling unspeakably happy, until the carriage drove away.

In the days that followed, as tensions increased day by day, Julie's heart was still filled with hope. When she walked in the garden, she sang softly with boundless joy, secretly counting the days, hoping that her lover would return to her arms sooner. But in Nathan's heart, he only felt the burden increase day by day. How long could the Allied forces hold out? How many days could he himself hold out? His heart could not help but be anxious. One morning, Hannah was pinning a boutonniere on him when she said, "My dear, you are bravely holding on, but I'm afraid you have reached your breaking point." Nathan smiled, but very reluctantly. He said: "I have promised the Allied powers, I cannot exhaust my meager strength, but if the situation in the exchange yesterday were to happen again tomorrow, I'm afraid the Rothschilds will have to close their doors." Hannah trembled in fright when she heard this. She cried out, "Nathan!" She unconsciously dropped the pin she was going to use to attach the flower. She said with tears in her eyes and helplessness, "Nathan, I truly admire you. You fight for what you believe is just. Even if you fail, you will fail for glory." Nathan forced a smile: "With a virtuous and brave wife like you, and a little rose pinned on my lapel, even if I lose all my wealth, I am still the richest person in the world."

Rothschild ran in. He silently handed a small roll of paper to Nathan. Nathan silently read it. Then he read it out loud. It read: "Blücher's troops have begun to retreat, Napoleon has used all his strength against Wellington – James." Julie cried when she heard this. She said, "Today is the hundredth day, and Fitzroy has not returned!" Nathan felt very uncomfortable, but he still forced a smile and comforted her: "The hundredth day is not over yet. Julie, have you forgotten? I am a magician. I know that a message of love and hope is already on its way here." He told his wife, "Hannah, take her away." He then said to his secretary, "Rothschild, come with me." They went outside, and Nathan stopped. He said thoughtfully, "Carriages, rooms, servants, all that we have today – but tomorrow, I'm afraid..." As he left to get into the carriage, his boutonniere fell off because it was not properly pinned, but he did not know it at all. (To be continued)
